The functional tests cover the empty-estimates-zero / single-element / duplicate-collapses semantics, a 100k-distinct estimate within 3 standard errors, the small-cardinality linear-counting accuracy, `default(int)` / `Guid.Empty` / empty-string as ordinary elements, the out-of-band `null`-reference path (a `StringFnV1AHasher` estimator that would otherwise throw), `Clear` (and the already-empty no-op), precision→register-count sizing across `p ∈ {4, 10, 14, 16}`, `StandardError` shrinking with precision, higher-precision-gives-tighter-estimate, the `IEnumerable` ctor (distinct counting, duplicate-honoring, non-collection source, empty source, precision honoring, null-source `ArgumentNullException` including beating a bad precision), constructor validation (precision below `MIN_PRECISION` / above `MAX_PRECISION`, boundary values accepted), and `UnionWith` (disjoint-stream union, overlapping-stream union, other-left-unmodified, null, incompatible-precision `ArgumentException`); the accuracy suite **statistically** asserts the realized relative error stays within ~3 standard errors across `n ∈ {1k, 10k, 100k, 1M}` int, `{5k, 50k}` string, and 100k long cardinalities (deterministic data), plus a duplicate-heavy 1M-add / 25k-distinct stream counting only the distinct values; the collision suite drives a degenerate constant hasher (every element shares one base hash) to prove the estimate gracefully collapses to one distinct value (an underestimate, not a crash), a negative-constant `int.MinValue` base hash for in-range register/rank derivation, and the minimum precision (widest rank field) producing valid indices and ranks. A `HyperLogLog` arm was also added to the differential testing layer: a CsCheck model property test (`CollectionModelPropertyTests.HyperLogLog_ShouldEstimateDistinctCount_VsBclHashSet`) and a `Celerity.Fuzz` target (`HyperLogLog`, registered in `Differential.All`), both reconciling the estimate against a `HashSet<int>` oracle's exact `Count` within a small slack (the tiny key domain sits deep in the linear-counting regime, where the estimate is exact apart from the rare register collision that can undercount by one — never an overcount beyond rounding).
- `HyperLogLogBenchmark` in `Celerity.Benchmarks`, comparing `HyperLogLog<int, Int32WangNaiveHasher>` against a `HashSet<int>` baseline at 1k / 100k items across `Add` (building each structure from scratch) and `Estimate` (`EstimateCardinality` vs `HashSet.Count` on a pre-built structure). Like `BloomFilterBenchmark` it enables `[MemoryDiagnoser]` because the headline is allocation — the `Allocated` column shows the estimator building in a fixed register-array footprint that does not grow with the cardinality, versus a `HashSet` storing every distinct element. The `[Params]` field is named `ItemCount` so the dashboard's benchmark-name parser picks it up. Registered in `Celerity.Benchmarks/Program.cs`'s core `--ci` `CoreBenchmarks` array so it joins the `RunAllJoined` CI report and the gh-pages dashboard.
- Benchmark dashboard wiring for `HyperLogLog`: a "What ships in the box" ship card in `web/index.html`, and a `COLLECTIONS` entry (key / title / vs `HashSet<int>` / ops `['Add', 'Estimate']`) in both `web/dev/bench/index.html` and `web/dev/bench/detail.html` so the auto-published `data.js` is surfaced rather than ignored. The baseline series parses as the existing `HashSet` `BCL_TYPES` entry (the benchmark's baseline methods are named `HashSet_*`), so no `BCL_TYPES` change is needed.
- Documentation for `HyperLogLog`: a full section in `docs/api/collections.md` (the fixed-tiny-memory / bounded-relative-error / add-and-estimate contract, the register-rank / harmonic-mean / linear-counting algorithm and single-hasher-call SplitMix64 derivation, constructors and validation ordering, the full method/property surface, default-element and out-of-band-`null` handling, when to pick it over `HashSet` / `CeleritySet` and how it differs from `BloomFilter`, and a runnable unique-visitor + shard-merge example) and README updates — the Collections list, the "Choosing a collection" decision table, and a new "count distinct elements in a fixed few KB" Quick start subsection. The `Celerity.AotSmokeTest` now exercises `HyperLogLog<int, Int32WangNaiveHasher>` (add / distinct count / duplicate collapse / a 50k-element estimate-within-bound sweep / `UnionWith` / `Clear`), `HyperLogLog<string, StringFnV1AHasher>` (the `IEnumerable` ctor and the out-of-band `null` element), and `HyperLogLog<Guid, GuidHasher>` (the `Guid.Empty` element) so the Native AOT publish job compiles the new generic instantiations, the SplitMix64 avalanche, and the `LeadingZeroCount` rank path.
- `BitSet` in `Celerity.Collections` — a dense, fixed-length **exact** bit vector packed into 64-bit words, the second of the milestone 2.0.0 specialized-collections work and the deterministic counterpart to the probabilistic `BloomFilter<T, THasher>` ([#30](https://github.com/marius-bughiu/Celerity/issues/30)). Where a Bloom filter trades exactness for memory, a `BitSet` stores one bit per index with no error, and it is a drop-in alternative to `System.Collections.BitArray` tuned for two operations the BCL type does not offer directly: **population count** (`Count` returns the number of set bits in `O(Length / 64)` via a hardware `BitOperations.PopCount` per word — `BitArray` exposes no cardinality at all) and **SIMD-accelerated bulk boolean ops** (`And` / `Or` / `Xor` / `Not` combine the whole vector a `Vector<ulong>` at a time when the hardware accelerates it, falling back to a scalar 64-bit-word loop, where `BitArray` walks 32-bit words). Bit `i` lives in word `i / 64` at bit position `i % 64`; any bits in the final word beyond `Length` are kept clear at all times (after `SetAll`, `Not`, and the bulk operators mask the tail) so `Count` / `Any` / `All` never observe a stray out-of-range bit. Public surface: three constructors (`(length)`, `(length, defaultValue)`, `(bool[])`), the `this[int]` indexer plus `Get` / `Set` / `Flip` single-bit access (all range-checked), `SetAll` / `Clear`, in-place chainable `And` / `Or` / `Xor` (equal-length, else `ArgumentException`; `null` ⇒ `ArgumentNullException`) and `Not`, the `Any` / `All` (vacuously true when empty) / `None` predicates, `Length` and the popcount `Count`, an allocation-free `IEnumerable<bool>` struct `Enumerator` over bit *values* (mirroring `BitArray`), and an allocation-free `EnumerateSetBits()` over set-bit *indices* (skipping clear words in one comparison and locating bits via `BitOperations.TrailingZeroCount`). Both enumerators are `_version`-guarded and throw `InvalidOperationException` on mid-iteration mutation. Documented as the pick for dense small-integer index sets / fixed flag universes (bitmaps, visited/presence masks, sieves) where you count set bits or combine whole vectors, rather than a `BitArray` replacement in every case. AOT-safe (no reflection); `Get` / `Set` / `Count` and the bulk ops are allocation-free.
- `BitSetTests`, `BitSetBulkOpsTests`, and `BitSetEnumerationTests` — dedicated suites. The functional tests cover the three constructors (including zero-length and negative-length `ArgumentOutOfRangeException`, `null`-array `ArgumentNullException`, and `defaultValue: true`), `Get` / `Set` / indexer round-trips across word boundaries (bits 0 / 63 / 64 / 127), `Set(false)` clearing, out-of-range `Get` / `Set` / `Flip`, `Flip`'s returned new value, `SetAll(true)` with **tail-bit masking** past `Length` (130 bits over 3 words), `SetAll(false)` / `Clear`, the `Any` / `All` / `None` predicates, popcount `Count`, and the `All` word-boundary edge cases (exactly 64 bits with no tail; a lone missing tail bit at index 64). The bulk-ops suite checks `And` / `Or` / `Xor` / `Not` semantics, that `Not` does not leak tail bits and is its own inverse, same-instance return for chaining, length-mismatch `ArgumentException` and `null` `ArgumentNullException`, and a **`Theory` that reconciles all four operators against a scalar `bool[]` reference at sizes 10 / 1000 / 4096** (sub-word, multi-word-with-remainder, and vector-width-aligned, so both the SIMD path and its scalar tail are exercised). The enumeration suite covers the value enumerator (incl. empty, generic, and non-generic `IEnumerable` paths), `EnumerateSetBits` (ascending indices, empty, all-set, clear-word skipping, generic / non-generic paths), `Reset` on both enumerators, and mid-iteration mutation throwing `InvalidOperationException`. A `BitSet` arm was also added to the differential testing layer: **two-directional** CsCheck model property tests (`CollectionModelPropertyTests.BitSet_ShouldMatch_BoolArrayModel` reconciling per-bit state, `Count`, and `EnumerateSetBits` against a `bool[]` oracle after random Set/Flip/SetAll/Clear sequences, and `BitSet_BulkOps_ShouldMatch_ElementwiseModel` reconciling `And` / `Or` / `Xor` / `Not`) and a `Celerity.Fuzz` target (`BitSet`, registered in `Differential.All`) that fuzzes random-length sets against a `bool[]` oracle across single-bit ops and the bulk operators.
- `BitSetBenchmark` in `Celerity.Benchmarks`, comparing `BitSet` against a `System.Collections.BitArray` baseline at 1024 / 1,000,000 bits across `PopCount` (`BitSet.Count` vs a bit-by-bit loop over `BitArray`, since `BitArray` has no cardinality), `And`, `Or`, and `Xor` (construction is identical for both — a per-bit pass over the same `bool[]` — so each combine category isolates the bulk-op cost). Enables `[MemoryDiagnoser]`. The benchmark's `[Params]` field is named `ItemCount` (not `BitCount`) so the dashboard's benchmark-name parser picks it up like every other collection. Registered in `Celerity.Benchmarks/Program.cs`'s core `--ci` `CoreBenchmarks` array so it joins the `RunAllJoined` CI report and the gh-pages dashboard.
- Benchmark dashboard wiring for `BitSet`: a "What ships in the box" ship card in `web/index.html`, and a `COLLECTIONS` entry (key / title / vs `BitArray` / ops `['PopCount', 'And', 'Or', 'Xor']`, with a custom `items: [1024, 1000000]` since `BitSet` is benchmarked at those bit counts rather than the default 1k / 100k) in both `web/dev/bench/index.html` and `web/dev/bench/detail.html`. Unlike the other collections the baseline is `System.Collections.BitArray`, so **`'BitArray'` was added to the `BCL_TYPES` set** in both dashboard files (the benchmark's baseline methods are named `BitArray_*`) so the baseline series is recognized.
- Documentation for `BitSet`: a full section in `docs/api/collections.md` (the exact-vs-probabilistic framing against `BloomFilter`, the popcount and SIMD-bulk-op advantages over `BitArray`, the tail-bit-clearing invariant, constructors and validation, the full method/property surface, both enumerators, when to pick it over `IntSet` / `LongSet` (dense vs sparse) and `BloomFilter` (exact vs approximate), and a runnable Sieve-of-Eratosthenes example) and README updates — the Collections list and the "Choosing a collection" decision table. The `Celerity.AotSmokeTest` now exercises `BitSet` (set / get / popcount / flip / `SetAll` with tail masking / `Not` / the SIMD `And` and `Or` over 1000-bit vectors / `EnumerateSetBits` over a sparse 300-bit set / the value enumerator) so the Native AOT publish job compiles the `Vector<ulong>` bulk paths and the `TrailingZeroCount` set-bit walk.
- `BloomFilter<T, THasher>` in `Celerity.Collections` — a space-efficient **probabilistic** set membership filter, the first of the milestone 2.0.0 specialized-collections work ([#30](https://github.com/marius-bughiu/Celerity/issues/30)). It answers "is this element *possibly* present?" with nothing but a bit array and a handful of hash functions, so for membership-only workloads it uses a small fraction of the memory of a `HashSet<T>` and never grows with element size. The contract is the defining Bloom-filter trade-off: **no false negatives** (a `Contains` returning `false` is always correct — the element was definitely never added) and **bounded false positives** (a `true` is probably correct, at a tunable rate). The filter sizes itself at construction from the expected element count `n` and target false-positive rate `p` using the standard optimal formulas — bit count `m = ceil(-n·ln(p) / (ln 2)²)` rounded **up to a power of two** so a bit index is a mask rather than a modulo (the extra bits only lower the realized rate, never raise it), and hash count `k = round((m/n)·ln 2)`, at least one. The `k` bit positions for an element are derived from a **single** `IHashProvider<T>` call by **double hashing** (Kirsch–Mitzenmacher): the 32-bit base hash is avalanched into 64 bits (a SplitMix64 finalizer) whose two halves seed the recurrence `g_i = h1 + i·h2` (the stride forced odd so the `k` probes spread out), so adding hash functions costs arithmetic, not more `Hash()` calls. Because the filter stores only bits there is no empty-slot sentinel, so unlike the hash-table collections it needs **no out-of-band handling** for `default(T)` (a zero `int`, `Guid.Empty`, the empty string are ordinary elements); a `null` reference is mapped to a fixed base hash so the hasher (the string hashers throw on `null`) is never invoked with `null`, via a `typeof(T).IsValueType`-guarded check the JIT folds away for value-type instantiations (no boxing). Public surface: `Add`, `Contains`, `Clear`, `UnionWith` (in-place bitwise-OR merge of two equally-parameterized filters), `Count` (an **insertion counter**, documented as *not* a distinct-element count), `Capacity`, `BitCount`, `HashCount`, `FalsePositiveRate`, and `CurrentFalsePositiveProbability` (a popcount-based estimate of the realized rate at the current fill), plus two constructors (`(expectedItems, falsePositiveRate)` and `(IEnumerable<T>, falsePositiveRate)` that sizes from `ICollection<T>.Count` or a counting pass, with null-source-beats-bad-rate validation ordering). There is deliberately **no `Remove`** (clearing one bit could erase membership for an unrelated element, introducing false negatives) — `Clear` resets the whole filter. Documented as the pick for membership gates / dedup pre-filters where a bounded false-positive rate buys a large memory saving, rather than a `HashSet` replacement. AOT-safe (no reflection); `Add` / `Contains` are allocation-free.
- `BloomFilterTests`, `BloomFilterFalsePositiveTests`, and `BloomFilterCollisionTests` — dedicated suites. The functional tests cover add/contains round-trip, the duplicate-still-increments-`Count` semantics, no-false-negatives over a 1000-element fill, `default(int)` / `Guid.Empty` / empty-string as ordinary elements, the out-of-band `null`-reference path (a `StringFnV1AHasher` filter that would otherwise throw), `Clear` (and the already-empty no-op), the power-of-two `BitCount` / positive `HashCount` sizing, lower-rate-allocates-more-bits, the tiny-capacity one-word floor, `CurrentFalsePositiveProbability` rising as the filter fills, the `IEnumerable` ctor (collection-count sizing, non-collection counting-pass sizing, empty source, null-source `ArgumentNullException` including beating a bad rate), full constructor validation (non-positive `expectedItems`; rate `<= 0` / `>= 1` / negative / `> 1` / `NaN`), and `UnionWith` (merge, other-left-unmodified, null, incompatible-size `ArgumentException`); the false-positive suite **statistically** asserts the realized rate stays at or under target across `p ∈ {0.1, 0.01, 0.001}` (10k-element fills, 100k disjoint absent queries, deterministic data) with no false negatives, the same for a 5k-string filter, and the estimated probability near target at capacity; the collision suite drives a degenerate constant hasher (all elements share one base hash) to prove the no-false-negatives guarantee survives the worst case (the filter merely degrades to everything-looks-present), plus a negative-constant `int.MinValue` base hash to confirm the `uint` cast / mask keeps the bit index in range. A `BloomFilter` arm was also added to the differential testing layer: a **one-directional** CsCheck model property test (`CollectionModelPropertyTests.BloomFilter_ShouldHaveNoFalseNegatives_VsBclHashSet`) and a `Celerity.Fuzz` target (`BloomFilter`, registered in `Differential.All`), both reconciling that every element a `HashSet<int>` oracle holds tests present (absence is not reconciled — a `true` may be a legitimate false positive).
- `BloomFilterBenchmark` in `Celerity.Benchmarks`, comparing `BloomFilter<int, Int32WangNaiveHasher>` against a `HashSet<int>` baseline at 1k / 100k items across `Add`, `Contains` (present keys), and `ContainsMissing` (absent keys). Unlike the other set benchmarks it enables `[MemoryDiagnoser]` because the filter's headline is allocation — the `Allocated` column shows it building in a fraction of the `HashSet`'s space (bit array vs buckets + entries). Registered in `Celerity.Benchmarks/Program.cs`'s core `--ci` `CoreBenchmarks` array so it joins the `RunAllJoined` CI report and the gh-pages dashboard.
- Benchmark dashboard wiring for `BloomFilter`: a "What ships in the box" ship card in `web/index.html`, and a `COLLECTIONS` entry (key / title / vs `HashSet<int>` / ops `['Add', 'Contains', 'ContainsMissing']`) in both `web/dev/bench/index.html` and `web/dev/bench/detail.html` so the auto-published `data.js` is surfaced rather than ignored. The baseline series parses as the existing `HashSet` `BCL_TYPES` entry (the benchmark's baseline methods are named `HashSet_*`), so no `BCL_TYPES` change is needed.
- Documentation for `BloomFilter`: a full section in `docs/api/collections.md` (the no-false-negatives / bounded-false-positives / no-`Remove` contract, the optimal `m` / `k` sizing and double-hashing derivation, constructors and validation ordering, the full method/property surface, default-element and out-of-band-`null` handling, when to pick it over `CeleritySet` / `FrozenCeleritySet`, and a runnable crawler-frontier example) and README updates — the Collections list, the "Choosing a collection" decision table, and a new "probabilistic membership at a fraction of the memory" Quick start subsection. The `Celerity.AotSmokeTest` now constructs `BloomFilter<int, Int32WangNaiveHasher>` (add / contains / negative lookup / power-of-two sizing / a 500-element no-false-negatives sweep / `UnionWith` / `Clear`), `BloomFilter<string, StringFnV1AHasher>` (the `IEnumerable` ctor and the out-of-band `null` element), and `BloomFilter<Guid, GuidHasher>` (the `Guid.Empty` element) so the Native AOT publish job compiles the new generic instantiations and the double-hashing probe path.
- `HashCachingDictionary<TKey, TValue, THasher>` in `Celerity.Collections` — a drop-in peer of `CelerityDictionary` that takes the **struct-of-arrays layout** one step further, delivering the 2.0.0 struct-of-arrays layout experiment ([#65](https://github.com/marius-bughiu/Celerity/issues/65)). Alongside the parallel `keys` / `values` arrays it keeps a dense side array of 32-bit hash **fingerprints**, one per slot: the fingerprint of an occupied slot is the key's hash with its top bit forced set (`hash | 0x80000000`, always non-zero), and an empty slot is the array default `0`, so the fingerprint array doubles as the occupancy bitmap. A linear probe scans only that compact `int[]` metadata buffer and dereferences a key (running the full `EqualityComparer<TKey>` check) **only on a fingerprint match**, so cache-cold lookups stay inside one buffer and expensive key comparisons (long strings, large value-type keys) are filtered out by a single integer compare. Because the forced occupied bit sits above every power-of-two table mask, the cached fingerprint also yields the slot index directly (`fingerprint & mask`): a `Resize` re-homes every entry straight from its stored fingerprint **without invoking the hasher once**, and backward-shift (tombstone-free) deletion reads each candidate's natural slot from its fingerprint too. The public surface is byte-for-byte identical to `CelerityDictionary`: indexer get/set, `ContainsKey`, `ContainsValue`, `TryGetValue`, `Add`, `TryAdd`, `Remove` (both `bool Remove(key)` and `bool Remove(key, out TValue?)`), `Clear`, `Count`, allocation-free struct `Keys` / `Values` views and `Enumerator` (with `_version` mutation detection), `IReadOnlyDictionary<TKey, TValue?>`, and both constructors (`(capacity, loadFactor)` and `(IEnumerable<KeyValuePair<TKey, TValue>>, capacity, loadFactor)` with the same power-of-two sizing, load-factor-headroom bulk sizing, validation, and out-of-band `default(TKey)` handling so the hasher is never invoked with the zero / null key). A new-key `Add` / `TryAdd` / indexer-set costs exactly one `Hash()` call. The cost versus `CelerityDictionary` is four bytes of metadata per slot; it is documented as the pick for lookup-dominated workloads, costly-equality keys, and large cache-cold tables (complementary to `SwissDictionary`'s SIMD one-byte tags), rather than a default. AOT-safe; hot-path lookup is allocation-free.
- `HashCachingDictionaryTests`, `HashCachingDictionaryCollisionTests`, and `HashCachingDictionaryEnumerationTests` — dedicated suites mirroring the `CelerityDictionary*` files (the closest structural analog: same linear-probing + backward-shift machinery). The functional tests cover insert/retrieve/overwrite, `ContainsKey`, `Remove`, resize, the out-of-band `0` / `Guid.Empty` default key surviving resize, `TryGetValue` hit/miss, `Clear` (including the already-empty no-op), and `Add` / `TryAdd` duplicate semantics; the collision suite adds full-collision insert/overwrite/remove/resize chains (every key sharing one fingerprint — the worst case for the filter), the backward-shift wrap-around branches under an identity hasher, `null`-string-key round-trips, and a **differential fuzz** (`RandomizedOps_ShouldMatchBclDictionary`, 5000 random Set/Remove/Lookup ops over a deliberately tiny key universe across four seeds) reconciled against a `Dictionary<int, int>` oracle; the enumeration suite mirrors the full `Keys` / `Values` / `Enumerator` surface including default-key yield, mid-enumeration mutation detection, and the boxed generic / non-generic `IEnumerable` paths. A `HashCachingDictionary` arm was also added to the differential testing layer: a CsCheck model property test (`CollectionModelPropertyTests.HashCachingDictionary_ShouldMatch_BclDictionary`) and a `Celerity.Fuzz` target (`HashCachingDictionary`, registered in `Differential.All`), both reconciled against a `Dictionary<int, int>` oracle.
- Cross-collection shared tests extended to cover `HashCachingDictionary` alongside `CelerityDictionary` / `RobinHoodDictionary` / `SwissDictionary` / `PooledCelerityDictionary` in all thirteen shared files: `AddAndTryAddTests`, `ConstructorValidationTests`, `IEnumerableConstructorTests`, `IEnumerableConstructorNullPriorityTests`, `ReadOnlyDictionaryInterfaceTests`, `RemoveOutValueTests`, `ContainsValueTests`, `LoadFactorBoundaryTests`, `IndexerReturnTypeTests`, `IndexerOverwriteResizeTests` (overwrite at threshold does not resize), `TryAddDuplicateResizeTests` (duplicate `TryAdd` at threshold keeps an active enumerator valid; a new-key `TryAdd` invalidates it), `TryAddProbeCountTests` (a new-key / duplicate `TryAdd` does exactly one `Hash()` call), and `BulkConstructorNoResizeTests` (a bulk construct from a known-`Count` source costs exactly N hashes with no resize).
- `HashCachingDictionaryBenchmark` in `Celerity.Benchmarks`, mirroring `CelerityDictionaryBenchmark` / `SwissDictionaryBenchmark` (Insert / Lookup / Remove against a `Dictionary<int, int>` baseline at 1k / 100k items, with the per-`Remove` `[IterationSetup]` pattern), and registered in `Program.cs`'s core `--ci` `CoreBenchmarks` so the joined CI report and the gh-pages dashboard include it.
- Benchmark dashboard wiring for `HashCachingDictionary`: a "What ships in the box" ship card in `web/index.html`, and a `COLLECTIONS` entry (key / title / vs / ops) in both `web/dev/bench/index.html` and `web/dev/bench/detail.html` so the auto-published `data.js` is surfaced rather than ignored. The baseline series parses as the existing `Dictionary` `BCL_TYPES` entry (the benchmark's baseline methods are named `Dictionary_*`), so no `BCL_TYPES` change is needed.
- Documentation for `HashCachingDictionary`: a full section in `docs/api/collections.md` (what the cached-fingerprint side array does, the metadata-only probe and rehash-without-re-hashing properties, when to pick it over `CelerityDictionary` and how it complements `SwissDictionary`, constructors, default-key handling, runnable usage example) and README updates — the Collections list, the "Choosing a collection" decision table, and a "Quick start" subsection. The `Celerity.AotSmokeTest` now constructs `HashCachingDictionary<int, int, Int32WangNaiveHasher>` (indexer / Add / TryAdd / backward-shift Remove / out-of-band zero key / a 500-entry resize sweep / enumeration), `HashCachingDictionary<string, int, StringMurmur3Hasher>` (the `IEnumerable` ctor and out-of-band `null` key), and `HashCachingDictionary<Guid, string, GuidHasher>` (the `Guid.Empty` default-key slot) so the Native AOT publish job compiles the new generic instantiations and the fingerprint probe path.
- `SwissDictionary<TKey, TValue, THasher>` in `Celerity.Collections` — a drop-in peer of `CelerityDictionary` that resolves collisions with **SIMD-accelerated group probing** in the spirit of Google's Swiss Tables and Facebook's `F14`, delivering the 2.0.0 SIMD-accelerated probing experiment ([#64](https://github.com/marius-bughiu/Celerity/issues/64)). It keeps a parallel array of one-byte **control** tags — one per slot, separate from the key/value arrays — each holding `EMPTY`, `DELETED` (a tombstone), or, for an occupied slot, the low 7 bits of the key's hash (its *h2* fragment). Slots are grouped into aligned blocks of 16, so a single portable `Vector128<sbyte>` compare tests all 16 control bytes in a group at once (via `Vector128.Equals(...).ExtractMostSignificantBits()` → a 16-bit candidate mask); only the matching candidate slots pay a full key comparison, and a group with any `EMPTY` slot ends the probe. The `Vector128` API JITs to SSE2 / AVX2 on x86, AdvSimd on Arm, and a scalar software fallback elsewhere, so the type is correct everywhere and fast where hardware SIMD is available. Deletion uses Swiss-table tombstones — a freed slot becomes `EMPTY` only when its group still holds an `EMPTY` (so no resident probed past it), else a `DELETED` tombstone that a lookup walks past but does not terminate on — and tombstones are reclaimed by a same-size rehash when they accumulate, so insert/delete churn cannot grow the table without bound. The public surface is byte-for-byte identical to `CelerityDictionary`: indexer get/set, `ContainsKey`, `ContainsValue`, `TryGetValue`, `Add`, `TryAdd`, `Remove` (both `bool Remove(key)` and `bool Remove(key, out TValue?)`), `Clear`, `Count`, allocation-free struct `Keys` / `Values` views and `Enumerator` (with `_version` mutation detection), `IReadOnlyDictionary<TKey, TValue?>`, and both constructors (`(capacity, loadFactor)` and `(IEnumerable<KeyValuePair<TKey, TValue>>, capacity, loadFactor)` with the same power-of-two sizing — floored to one 16-slot SIMD group — load-factor-headroom bulk sizing, validation, and out-of-band `default(TKey)` handling so the hasher is never invoked with the zero / null key). The combined insert probe checks for an existing key and chooses the insertion slot (reusing the first tombstone, else the first empty) in one walk, so a new-key `Add` / `TryAdd` / indexer-set costs exactly one `Hash()` call. The cost versus `CelerityDictionary` is the one-byte control tag per slot; it is documented as the pick for lookup-heavy workloads (large tables, many negative lookups, clustered keys) rather than a default. AOT-safe; hot-path lookup is allocation-free.
- `SwissDictionaryTests`, `SwissDictionaryCollisionTests`, and `SwissDictionaryEnumerationTests` — dedicated suites mirroring the `CelerityDictionary*` / `RobinHoodDictionary*` files. The functional tests cover insert/retrieve/overwrite, `ContainsKey`, `Remove`, resize, the out-of-band `0` / `Guid.Empty` default key surviving resize, `TryGetValue` hit/miss, `Clear` (including the already-empty no-op), and `Add` / `TryAdd` duplicate semantics; the collision suite adds full-collision insert/overwrite/remove/resize chains into a single home group (the multi-group probe-overflow path), the Swiss-specific **tombstone** behaviour (a lookup that must find a key *past* a tombstone, and an insert/remove churn that exercises the tombstone-reclaiming rehash without unbounded growth), group-straddling clusters under an identity hasher, early-missing negative lookups, `null`-string-key round-trips, and a **differential fuzz** (`RandomizedOps_ShouldMatchBclDictionary`, 5000 random Set/Remove/Lookup ops over a deliberately tiny key universe across four seeds) reconciled against a `Dictionary<int, int>` oracle; the enumeration suite mirrors the full `Keys` / `Values` / `Enumerator` surface including default-key yield, mid-enumeration mutation detection, and the boxed generic / non-generic `IEnumerable` paths. A `SwissDictionary` arm was also added to the differential testing layer: a CsCheck model property test (`CollectionModelPropertyTests.SwissDictionary_ShouldMatch_BclDictionary`) and a `Celerity.Fuzz` target (`SwissDictionary`, registered in `Differential.All`), both reconciled against a `Dictionary<int, int>` oracle.
- Cross-collection shared tests extended to cover `SwissDictionary` alongside `CelerityDictionary` / `RobinHoodDictionary` / `PooledCelerityDictionary` in all thirteen shared files: `AddAndTryAddTests`, `ConstructorValidationTests`, `IEnumerableConstructorTests`, `IEnumerableConstructorNullPriorityTests`, `ReadOnlyDictionaryInterfaceTests`, `RemoveOutValueTests`, `ContainsValueTests`, `LoadFactorBoundaryTests`, `IndexerReturnTypeTests`, `IndexerOverwriteResizeTests` (overwrite at threshold does not resize), `TryAddDuplicateResizeTests` (duplicate `TryAdd` at threshold keeps an active enumerator valid; a new-key `TryAdd` invalidates it), `TryAddProbeCountTests` (a new-key / duplicate `TryAdd` does exactly one `Hash()` call), and `BulkConstructorNoResizeTests` (a bulk construct from a known-`Count` source costs exactly N hashes with no resize).
- `SwissDictionaryBenchmark` in `Celerity.Benchmarks`, mirroring `CelerityDictionaryBenchmark` / `RobinHoodDictionaryBenchmark` (Insert / Lookup / Remove against a `Dictionary<int, int>` baseline at 1k / 100k items, with the per-`Remove` `[IterationSetup]` pattern), and registered in `Program.cs`'s core `--ci` `CoreBenchmarks` so the joined CI report and the gh-pages dashboard include it.
- Benchmark dashboard wiring for `SwissDictionary`: a "What ships in the box" ship card in `web/index.html`, and a `COLLECTIONS` entry (key / title / vs / ops) in both `web/dev/bench/index.html` and `web/dev/bench/detail.html` so the auto-published `data.js` is surfaced rather than ignored. The baseline series parses as the existing `Dictionary` `BCL_TYPES` entry (the benchmark's baseline methods are named `Dictionary_*`), so no `BCL_TYPES` change is needed.
- Documentation for `SwissDictionary`: a full section in `docs/api/collections.md` (what SIMD group probing does, the control-byte / tombstone design, when to pick it over `CelerityDictionary`, constructors, default-key handling, runnable usage example) and README updates — the Collections list, the "Choosing a collection" decision table, and a "Quick start" subsection. The `Celerity.AotSmokeTest` now constructs `SwissDictionary<int, int, Int32WangNaiveHasher>` (indexer / Add / TryAdd / tombstone Remove / out-of-band zero key / a 500-entry resize sweep / enumeration), `SwissDictionary<string, int, StringMurmur3Hasher>` (the `IEnumerable` ctor and out-of-band `null` key), and `SwissDictionary<Guid, string, GuidHasher>` (the `Guid.Empty` default-key slot) so the Native AOT publish job compiles the new generic instantiations and the `Vector128` group-compare path.

### Changed

- **Repositioned the hasher docs & README away from "faster hashing" toward distribution / avalanche / determinism**, completing milestone 1.6.0 ([#184](https://github.com/marius-bughiu/Celerity/issues/184)). The hashers cannot win on raw speed — for `int`, `GetHashCode()` *is* the identity (zero work); for `string`, `GetHashCode()` is already a per-process-randomized **Marvin32** — so the docs now lead with the real value proposition (avalanche, reproducible determinism, adversarial resistance, the zero-cost devirtualized generic). The README's "**up to 2.4× faster than `Dictionary<int,int>`**" headline is reframed as a *collection-layout* win (open addressing with direct `==` comparison and no per-call `EqualityComparer<T>` dispatch), explicitly **independent of the hasher**. A new **HashDoS caveat** is added to both `README.md` and `docs/api/hashing.md`: fixed-seed hashers are *not* a HashDoS defence — a hardcoded-seed Murmur3 / FNV / xxHash is no more flood-resistant than Marvin32 (usually less, since an attacker who knows the fixed seed precomputes collisions offline); what stops flooding is a **keyed** PRF with a *secret, per-process-random* key, so for untrusted `string` keys the BCL `string.GetHashCode()` (`DefaultHasher<string>`) is the safe default and the keyed SipHash / HighwayHash hashers help only when also given a secret seed. `hashing.md`'s "Choosing a hasher" section gains an explicit speed-vs-quality-curve framing block (the F14 / ahash / FxHash trusted-uniform-vs-clustered-vs-untrusted decision), and the "Benchmarking the string hashers" section, `docs/performance.md`, and the dashboard blurb all reframe the isolated `Hash()` sweeps as a raw-mixing-cost diagnostic to be read alongside the end-to-end probe analysis.

### Fixed

- **`CelerityMultiMap<TKey, TValue, THasher>.AddRange` no longer registers a phantom key for an empty sequence** ([#215](https://github.com/marius-bughiu/Celerity/issues/215)). `AddRange` called `GroupForAdd(key)` — which eagerly creates the value group, inserts the key into the probe table (or the out-of-band default-key slot), and increments `_count` — *before* consulting the supplied `values`. When `values` was empty and the key was new, the method added nothing but left the key registered with a zero-length group and an inflated `Count`, so `map.AddRange("ghost", Enumerable.Empty<int>())` made `Count == 1`, `ContainsKey("ghost") == true`, and surfaced `"ghost"` as an empty `Grouping` in enumeration — violating the type's invariant that a present key always has at least one value (the invariant `Add` / `Remove` / `RemoveAll` maintain, and that `Remove` relies on, since it can only delete a key by emptying its group). `AddRange` now peeks the first element of the sequence through the enumerator and only calls `GroupForAdd` once it knows at least one value will be added, so an empty `AddRange` is a true no-op for both normal and default/`null` keys (and an empty `AddRange` on an already-present key leaves it untouched). Covered by new `AddRange_WithEmptySequence_*` regression tests in `CelerityMultiMapTests`. (Parity note: this is a behaviour fix in an existing collection method, not a new collection / public API / hasher, so the cross-collection shared-test, benchmark, dashboard `COLLECTIONS`, API-doc-section, and ROADMAP facets of the parity checklist do not apply — the in-`CelerityMultiMapTests` regression coverage and this changelog entry are the applicable facets.)
- **The Benchmarks CI workflow now actually completes and publishes** ([#217](https://github.com/marius-bughiu/Celerity/issues/217)). Two independent bugs had left the continuous regression gate and the gh-pages performance dashboard dead on every run. **(1) The core suite was too slow to finish:** at full BenchmarkDotNet accuracy (`Job.Default.WithLaunchCount(2)`) one pass over the ~300-case core suite takes ~3h, and the PR path benchmarks the suite **twice** (PR head + `main` base, back-to-back on one runner for the same-runner A/B that cancels hardware variance), so it blew past GitHub Actions' 6h job ceiling and was **cancelled on every PR**. Rather than trade away measurement accuracy, the suite is now **sharded across a parallel matrix**: `Celerity.Benchmarks` gains a `--shard <total> <index>` switch (Program.cs) that greedy-balances the core classes by case count, `benchmarks.yml` runs one matrix job per shard (each measuring only its slice's head + base at full `Job.Default` accuracy, so wall time is ~3h / shardCount), and a new `aggregate` job stitches the per-shard JSON reports back together for the regression comment / gh-pages publish. Sharding is **by benchmark class**, which preserves the same-runner A/B invariant (a class's head and base measurements always run together on one runner). **(2) The gh-pages publish always failed**, even when a `main` run finished: the `actions/checkout` step used `fetch-depth: 0` **with `filter: tree:0`**, a blobless partial clone that advertises every commit as "have" while missing the underlying objects, so `github-action-benchmark`'s own `git fetch origin gh-pages:gh-pages` (and the base `git worktree add`) aborted with `fatal: missing blob object … did not send all necessary objects` and `data.js` was never pushed. The `filter: tree:0` is removed from both `benchmarks.yml` and `benchmarks-extended.yml` (the weekly extended dashboard had the identical bug), and a `timeout-minutes` guard is added to the shard job so any future slowdown fails fast instead of burning the full 6h. (Parity note: this is a CI/tooling fix — no new collection, public API, or hasher — so the dedicated-test, cross-collection-shared-test, benchmark-registration, dashboard-`COLLECTIONS`, API-doc, and ROADMAP facets of the parity checklist do not apply; this changelog entry is the applicable facet.)

## [1.5.0] - 2026-06-07

### Added

- `PooledCelerityDictionary<TKey, TValue, THasher>` in `Celerity.Collections` — a drop-in, `IDisposable` peer of `CelerityDictionary` whose backing key/value arrays are **rented from `ArrayPool<T>.Shared`** instead of allocated on the managed heap, delivering the milestone 2.0.0 memory-pooled-collections work ([#21](https://github.com/marius-bughiu/Celerity/issues/21)). The public surface is byte-for-byte identical to `CelerityDictionary` — indexer get/set, `ContainsKey`, `ContainsValue`, `TryGetValue`, `Add`, `TryAdd`, `Remove` (both `bool Remove(key)` and `bool Remove(key, out TValue?)`), `Clear`, `Count`, allocation-free struct `Keys` / `Values` views and `Enumerator` (with `_version` mutation detection), `IReadOnlyDictionary<TKey, TValue?>`, both constructors with the same power-of-two sizing / load-factor-headroom bulk sizing / validation / out-of-band `default(TKey)` handling — with one addition: `IDisposable`. `Dispose` returns the rented buffers to the pool (and every internal `Resize` returns the old buffers as it rents the doubled pair), so build/use/dispose cycles on a hot path recycle buffers instead of producing Gen 0 / LOH garbage. Because `ArrayPool.Rent` may hand back an array **larger** than requested, the type tracks its logical power-of-two capacity and probe mask independently of the rented array's `Length` and only ever reads or writes the live region — so the uncleared tail of an over-provisioned buffer never surfaces in `Count`, enumeration, or `ContainsValue`. Reference-type (or reference-containing) buffers are cleared on return so the pool does not keep keys / values reachable after disposal (memory-leak prevention); value-type buffers skip the clear. `Dispose` is idempotent and after it every member throws `ObjectDisposedException`; `ArrayPool<T>.Shared` never throws on exhaustion (it allocates a fresh buffer), so callers never handle a pool-empty condition. Not disposing is not a leak — the arrays are GC-reclaimed like any managed array, you just forfeit the pooling benefit. AOT-safe (no reflection); hot-path lookup is allocation-free.
- `PooledCelerityDictionaryTests`, `PooledCelerityDictionaryCollisionTests`, and `PooledCelerityDictionaryEnumerationTests` — dedicated suites mirroring the `CelerityDictionary*` files (insert/retrieve/overwrite, `ContainsKey` / `ContainsValue`, `Remove`, resize, the out-of-band `0` / `Guid.Empty` / `null` default key surviving resize, `TryGetValue` hit/miss, `Clear`, `Add` / `TryAdd` duplicate semantics; full-collision insert/overwrite/remove/resize chains, the backward-shift wrap-around branches, `null`-string-key round-trips, and a differential fuzz over a tiny key universe reconciled against a `Dictionary<int,int>` oracle; the full `Keys` / `Values` / `Enumerator` surface including default-key yield, mid-enumeration mutation detection, and the boxed generic / non-generic `IEnumerable` paths), plus **pooled-specific lifecycle tests**: idempotent `Dispose`, `ObjectDisposedException` on every member after disposal, correctness across many rent/return resizes, that an over-provisioned rent's garbage tail never leaks into enumeration / `Count` / `ContainsValue`, and the reference-type clear-on-return path. A `PooledCelerityDictionary` arm was also added to the differential testing layer: a CsCheck model property test (`CollectionModelPropertyTests.PooledCelerityDictionary_ShouldMatch_BclDictionary`) and a `Celerity.Fuzz` target (`PooledCelerityDictionary`, registered in `Differential.All`), both reconciled against a `Dictionary<int, int>` oracle.
- Cross-collection shared tests extended to cover `PooledCelerityDictionary` alongside `CelerityDictionary` in all thirteen shared files: `AddAndTryAddTests`, `ConstructorValidationTests`, `IEnumerableConstructorTests`, `IEnumerableConstructorNullPriorityTests`, `ReadOnlyDictionaryInterfaceTests` (including the polymorphic `IReadOnlyDictionary<int,int>` consumer), `RemoveOutValueTests`, `ContainsValueTests`, `LoadFactorBoundaryTests`, `IndexerReturnTypeTests`, `IndexerOverwriteResizeTests`, `TryAddDuplicateResizeTests`, `TryAddProbeCountTests` (the single-`Hash`-call insert path), and `BulkConstructorNoResizeTests` (a bulk construct from a known-`Count` source costs exactly N hashes with no resize). Each added block uses `using` so the rented buffers are returned.
- `PooledCelerityDictionaryBenchmark` in `Celerity.Benchmarks`, mirroring `CelerityDictionaryBenchmark` (Insert / Lookup / Remove against a `Dictionary<int, int>` baseline at 1k / 100k items, with the per-`Remove` `[IterationSetup]` pattern). Unlike the other collection benchmarks it enables `[MemoryDiagnoser]` with the GC columns on, because the pooled type's whole value is allocation: the `Insert` row builds and `Dispose`s a dictionary each iteration so the rented buffers are reused, and the `Allocated` column shows that win versus the non-pooled `Dictionary` baseline. Registered in `Celerity.Benchmarks/Program.cs`'s core `--ci` `CoreBenchmarks` array so it joins the `RunAllJoined` CI report and the gh-pages dashboard.
- Benchmark dashboard wiring for `PooledCelerityDictionary`: a "What ships in the box" ship card in `web/index.html`, and a `COLLECTIONS` entry (key / title / vs `Dictionary<int, int>` / ops `['Insert', 'Lookup', 'Remove']`) in both `web/dev/bench/index.html` and `web/dev/bench/detail.html`. The baseline series parses as the existing `Dictionary` `BCL_TYPES` entry (the benchmark's baseline methods are named `Dictionary_*`), so no `BCL_TYPES` change is needed.
- Documentation for `PooledCelerityDictionary`: a full section in `docs/api/collections.md` (why pooled storage, when to pick it over `CelerityDictionary`, the rent/return/Dispose lifecycle and pooling contract — idempotent dispose, not-disposing-is-not-a-leak, pool-exhaustion handling, reference-type clear-on-return, and over-provisioned-rent handling — constructors, default-key handling, and a runnable `using` example), and README updates — the Collections list, a new "pooled storage for short-lived dictionaries" Quick start subsection, and the "Choosing a collection" decision table. The `Celerity.AotSmokeTest` now constructs `PooledCelerityDictionary<int, int, Int32WangNaiveHasher>` (indexer / Add / TryAdd / Remove / out-of-band zero key / enumeration / `using` disposal) and `PooledCelerityDictionary<string, string, StringFnV1AHasher>` (the reference-type clear-on-return path and the out-of-band `null` key) so the Native AOT publish job compiles the new generic instantiations.
- `FrozenCeleritySet` / `FrozenCeleritySet<THasher>` in `Celerity.Collections` — a build-once, read-many set of `string` elements, the **set counterpart of `FrozenCelerityDictionary`** and the second half of the 1.2.0 frozen-collections work ([#22](https://github.com/marius-bughiu/Celerity/issues/22)). Like the frozen dictionary it is immutable (constructed once from an `IEnumerable<string>`, no mutating members) and at construction searches a small parameter space — candidate power-of-two table sizes × a per-build mixing seed — for a **perfect** (collision-free) placement of the elements; when found (`IsPerfectlyHashed == true`) a `Contains` is a single hash, a single array index, and a single equality check, with no probing. When two distinct elements collide on the chosen hasher's raw 32-bit code (e.g. `"A"` / `"Ł"` under the low-byte `StringFnV1AHasher`), a perfect placement is impossible, so the build falls back to an open-addressed linear-probing table (`IsPerfectlyHashed == false`); membership tests stay correct (the equality check disambiguates), just not single-probe. The one contract difference from the frozen *dictionary* is intentional and idiomatic for a set: **duplicate elements are silently deduplicated** (matching BCL `FrozenSet<T>` and the mutable `CeleritySet`) rather than throwing. Read API: `Contains`, `Count`, `IsPerfectlyHashed`, an allocation-free struct `Enumerator` (the out-of-band `null` element, if present, is yielded first), and the full `IReadOnlySet<string>` surface (`SetEquals`, `IsSubsetOf`, `IsProperSubsetOf`, `IsSupersetOf`, `IsProperSupersetOf`, `Overlaps` — the superset/overlap shapes stream `other` against the `O(1)` membership test, the subset/equality shapes materialize `other`'s distinct elements once into an ordinal set, and each throws `ArgumentNullException` on a `null` `other`). The `null` element is stored out-of-band (the hasher is never invoked with `null`) and the empty string is an ordinary element. The convenience `FrozenCeleritySet` defaults to `StringFnV1AHasher`; the `<THasher>` overload accepts any string hasher. AOT-safe (no reflection); hot-path membership is allocation-free.
- `FrozenCeleritySetTests` — a dedicated suite mirroring `FrozenCelerityDictionaryTests` for the set (construction & round-trip, present/absent `Contains`, empty-string-as-regular-element, out-of-band `null`-element round-trip and absence, `null`-source rejection, **duplicate / duplicate-`null` silent dedupe** (the set-vs-dictionary contract difference), empty source, the perfect fast path asserted via `IsPerfectlyHashed` on a strong hasher, the **fallback correctness** case where base-hash-colliding `"A"` / `"Ł"` under `StringFnV1AHasher` force linear probing yet stay distinct, absent-elements-hashing-into-occupied-slots miss, a 1000-element build-and-round-trip sweep with 1000 absent-element misses, enumeration including the `null` element, the `IReadOnlySet` surface, **the full set-algebra matrix** (`SetEquals` / `IsSubsetOf` / `IsProperSubsetOf` / `IsSupersetOf` / `IsProperSupersetOf` / `Overlaps`, including duplicates-in-`other`, the `null` element, and `null`-`other` throwing), the custom-hasher overload, the default convenience type, and the non-generic `IEnumerable` / `Reset` paths).
- A `FrozenCeleritySet` parity arm added to the differential testing layer: a CsCheck model property test (`CollectionModelPropertyTests.FrozenCeleritySet_ShouldMatch_BclHashSet`, building from a duplicate-rich source and reconciling distinct membership, absent-element misses, full-enumeration round-trip, and set-algebra against a `HashSet<string>` oracle) and a `Celerity.Fuzz` target (`FrozenCeleritySet`, registered in `Differential.All`) that fuzzes a duplicate-rich source against the BCL oracle and cross-checks count, per-element `Contains`, duplicate-free enumeration, and set-algebra.
- Cross-collection shared tests extended to cover `FrozenCeleritySet` in `SetIEnumerableConstructorTests` (the mirror of the dictionary `IEnumerableConstructorTests`): null-source `ArgumentNullException`, empty source, array / non-collection-enumerable copy, duplicate and duplicate-`null` dedupe, the out-of-band `null` element, large-source fidelity, source independence, the `<THasher>` open-generic overload, and a frozen-set-from-frozen-set round-trip. The hash-table-mutation shared files genuinely do not apply and are intentionally not extended: `SetConstructorValidationTests` (no `capacity` / `loadFactor` — the perfect-hash build sizes the table itself), `TryAddDuplicateResizeTests` / `TryAddProbeCountTests` (immutable, no `TryAdd`), and the dictionary-only shared files.
- `FrozenCeleritySetBenchmark` in `Celerity.Benchmarks`, mirroring `FrozenCelerityDictionaryBenchmark` — a `Build` + `Contains` comparison of `FrozenCeleritySet` against the BCL `System.Collections.Frozen.FrozenSet<string>` baseline (the true build-once counterpart; a mutable `HashSet<>` does no build-time hashing optimization, so it is not a like-for-like baseline for a frozen, perfect-hashed set), over the same `[Params(1000, 100_000)]` identifier-shaped distinct element sets. Registered in `Celerity.Benchmarks/Program.cs`'s core `--ci` `CoreBenchmarks` array so it joins the `RunAllJoined` CI report and the gh-pages dashboard.
- Benchmark dashboard wiring for `FrozenCeleritySet`: a "What ships in the box" ship card in `web/index.html`, and a `COLLECTIONS` entry (key / title / vs / ops `['Build', 'Contains']`) in both `web/dev/bench/index.html` and `web/dev/bench/detail.html`. `FrozenSet` was added to each dashboard's `BCL_TYPES` set so the parser treats the benchmark's `FrozenSet_*` methods as the baseline series (the comparison is Celerity-frozen vs BCL-frozen rather than vs the mutable `HashSet<>`).
- Documentation for `FrozenCeleritySet`: a full section in `docs/api/collections.md` (both the convenience and `<THasher>` overloads: the perfect-hash design and the set-vs-dictionary dedupe contract, constructor, `Count` / `IsPerfectlyHashed`, `Contains`, the `IReadOnlySet` set-algebra surface, null-element handling, the perfect fast path vs the linear-probing fallback, and runnable examples), and README updates — the Collections list, the "Choosing a collection" decision table, and a new "build-once string membership" Quick start subsection. The `Celerity.AotSmokeTest` now constructs `FrozenCeleritySet` (default, with the out-of-band `null` element and the `IReadOnlySet` surface), `FrozenCeleritySet<StringMurmur3Hasher>`, and the base-hash-collision fallback (`StringFnV1AHasher` over `"A"` / `"Ł"`) so the Native AOT publish job compiles the new generic instantiations and exercises both lookup paths.
- `RobinHoodDictionary<TKey, TValue, THasher>` in `Celerity.Collections` — a drop-in peer of `CelerityDictionary` that resolves collisions with **Robin Hood** open addressing instead of plain linear probing, delivering the 1.2.0 Robin Hood probing experiment ([#63](https://github.com/marius-bughiu/Celerity/issues/63)). Every occupied slot stores its probe sequence length (PSL — distance from the ideal slot) in a parallel `int[]`; on insert an incoming key that has travelled further than the resident displaces it ("robs from the rich") and the evicted entry is re-inserted further along, which bounds probe-length variance so worst-case lookups stay close to the average on clustered / adversarial key distributions. The stored PSL also lets a *negative* lookup terminate early — once the probe distance exceeds the resident slot's PSL the key cannot be present. Deletion is Robin Hood backward-shift (pull each follower back one slot, decrementing its PSL, until an empty or already-home slot). The public surface is byte-for-byte identical to `CelerityDictionary`: indexer get/set, `ContainsKey`, `ContainsValue`, `TryGetValue`, `Add`, `TryAdd`, `Remove` (both `bool Remove(key)` and `bool Remove(key, out TValue?)`), `Clear`, `Count`, allocation-free struct `Keys` / `Values` views and `Enumerator` (with `_version` mutation detection), `IReadOnlyDictionary<TKey, TValue?>`, and both constructors (`(capacity, loadFactor)` and `(IEnumerable<KeyValuePair<TKey, TValue>>, capacity, loadFactor)` with the same power-of-two sizing, load-factor-headroom bulk sizing, validation, and out-of-band `default(TKey)` handling). The insert path computes the key hash once and threads it through both the existence probe and the displacement insertion, so a new-key `Add` / `TryAdd` / indexer-set costs exactly one `Hash()` call (displaced residents are never re-hashed). The cost versus `CelerityDictionary` is the per-slot PSL `int` (more allocation) and a little extra insert work for the swaps; on uniform keys with a good hasher it is a wash or a slight loss, so it is documented as the pick for the clustered / adversarial case rather than a default. AOT-safe; hot-path lookup is allocation-free.
- `RobinHoodDictionaryTests`, `RobinHoodDictionaryCollisionTests`, and `RobinHoodDictionaryEnumerationTests` — dedicated suites mirroring the `CelerityDictionary*` files. The functional tests cover insert/retrieve/overwrite, `ContainsKey`, `Remove`, resize, the out-of-band `0` / `Guid.Empty` default key surviving resize, `TryGetValue` hit/miss, `Clear` (including the already-empty no-op), and `Add` / `TryAdd` duplicate semantics; the collision suite adds full-collision insert/overwrite/remove/resize chains, the Robin Hood **displacement** path (a longer-travelled key robbing a richer resident while every key stays reachable), early-terminating negative lookups on clustered keys, `null`-string-key round-trips, and a **differential fuzz** (`RandomizedOps_ShouldMatchBclDictionary`, 5000 random Set/Remove/Lookup ops over a deliberately tiny key universe across four seeds) reconciled against a `Dictionary<int, int>` oracle to stress the swap / backward-shift machinery; the enumeration suite mirrors the full `Keys` / `Values` / `Enumerator` surface including default-key yield, mid-enumeration mutation detection, and the boxed generic / non-generic `IEnumerable` paths. A `RobinHoodDictionary` arm was also added to the differential testing layer: a CsCheck model property test (`CollectionModelPropertyTests.RobinHoodDictionary_ShouldMatch_BclDictionary`) and a `Celerity.Fuzz` target (`RobinHoodDictionary`, registered in `Differential.All`), both reconciled against a `Dictionary<int, int>` oracle.
- Cross-collection shared tests extended to cover `RobinHoodDictionary` alongside `CelerityDictionary` in all thirteen shared files: `AddAndTryAddTests`, `ConstructorValidationTests`, `IEnumerableConstructorTests`, `IEnumerableConstructorNullPriorityTests`, `ReadOnlyDictionaryInterfaceTests`, `RemoveOutValueTests`, `ContainsValueTests`, `LoadFactorBoundaryTests`, `IndexerReturnTypeTests`, `IndexerOverwriteResizeTests` (overwrite at threshold does not resize), `TryAddDuplicateResizeTests` (duplicate `TryAdd` at threshold keeps an active enumerator valid; a new-key `TryAdd` invalidates it), `TryAddProbeCountTests` (a new-key / duplicate `TryAdd` does exactly one `Hash()` call — the single-hash insert path), and `BulkConstructorNoResizeTests` (a bulk construct from a known-`Count` source costs exactly N hashes with no resize).
- `RobinHoodDictionaryBenchmark` in `Celerity.Benchmarks`, mirroring `CelerityDictionaryBenchmark` (Insert / Lookup / Remove against a `Dictionary<int, int>` baseline at 1k / 100k items, with the per-`Remove` `[IterationSetup]` pattern), and registered in `Program.cs`'s core `--ci` `benchmarkTypes` so the joined CI report and the gh-pages dashboard include it.
- Benchmark dashboard wiring for `RobinHoodDictionary`: a "What ships in the box" ship card in `web/index.html`, and a `COLLECTIONS` entry (key / title / vs / ops) in both `web/dev/bench/index.html` and `web/dev/bench/detail.html` so the auto-published `data.js` is surfaced rather than ignored.
- Documentation for `RobinHoodDictionary`: a full section in `docs/api/collections.md` (what Robin Hood probing does, when to pick it over `CelerityDictionary`, constructors, default-key handling, runnable usage example) and README updates — the Collections list, the "Choosing a collection" decision table, and a "Quick start" subsection.
- `SmallDictionary<TKey, TValue>` in `Celerity.Collections` — a dictionary tuned for the very-small (`n <= ~16`) case, where a linear scan over a flat backing array beats a probe-based hash table (the shape compilers, IL emitters, AST attribute bags, and per-request maps hit constantly). The 1.2.0 small-collection ([#61](https://github.com/marius-bughiu/Celerity/issues/61)). It stores entries in insertion-dense parallel `TKey?[]` / `TValue?[]` arrays and answers every query with a linear scan using `EqualityComparer<TKey>.Default`, so there is **no hasher** (no `THasher` type parameter): nothing is hashed, which means there is no empty-slot sentinel and therefore **no out-of-band default-key slot** — a `0` / `null` / `Guid.Empty` key is stored inline like any other, a deliberate simplification over the hash-table dictionaries. The trade-off is that lookups / `Add` / `TryAdd` / `ContainsKey` / `Remove` are `O(n)` rather than `O(1)`, so the type is for small key sets and is documented as degrading for large ones (it does not auto-promote to a hash table; it grows its arrays and keeps scanning). `Remove` swaps the last entry into the vacated slot (an `O(1)` move once the key is found), so enumeration order is unspecified; a pure indexer overwrite never grows the arrays. Public API mirrors the other Celerity dictionaries: indexer get/set (get returns the non-nullable `TValue` and throws `KeyNotFoundException` on miss), `ContainsKey`, `ContainsValue`, `TryGetValue`, `Add`, `TryAdd`, `Remove` (both `bool Remove(key)` and `bool Remove(key, out TValue?)`), `Clear`, `Count`, allocation-free struct `Keys` / `Values` views and `Enumerator` (with `_version` mutation detection), `IReadOnlyDictionary<TKey, TValue?>`, and an `IEnumerable<KeyValuePair<TKey, TValue>>` constructor (duplicate keys throw `ArgumentException`; a `null` source throws `ArgumentNullException`, checked before the capacity validation). The constructor takes a `capacity` (used verbatim, not rounded to a power of two, since there is no probe mask; `0` defers allocation) and — unlike the hash-table dictionaries — has **no `loadFactor`** parameter. AOT-safe (no reflection); hot-path lookup is allocation-free.
- `SmallDictionaryTests` and `SmallDictionaryEnumerationTests` — dedicated suites mirroring `IntDictionaryTests` / `IntDictionaryEnumerationTests`, adapted for a hasher-less type: indexer insert/retrieve/overwrite (and overwrite-at-capacity not growing), `Remove` from first / middle / last slot via the swap-with-last path, grow-on-capacity-exceeded, the inline `0` / `null` default key exercised as an ordinary entry, `TryGetValue` hit/miss, `Clear` (including the already-empty no-op), remove-then-reinsert fidelity, zero-capacity deferred allocation, and the full enumeration surface (yield-once, reflect removal/clear, survive growth, mid-enumeration mutation/remove/clear detection on `MoveNext` and `Reset`, `Keys` / `Values` views and counts, the boxed generic and non-generic `IEnumerable` paths, and `Reset` reuse). A dedicated `*CollisionTests` file is intentionally **not** added: a linear-scan dictionary has no hashing and therefore no collisions to test.
- A `SmallDictionary` parity arm added to the differential testing layer: a CsCheck model property test (`CollectionModelPropertyTests.SmallDictionary_ShouldMatch_BclDictionary`, against a `Dictionary<int, int>` oracle over a random Set/Remove/TryAdd/Clear op stream) and a `Celerity.Fuzz` target (`SmallDictionary`, registered in `Differential.All`) that fuzzes the same op stream against the BCL oracle and cross-checks count, per-key lookups, and duplicate-free enumeration.
- Cross-collection shared tests extended to cover `SmallDictionary`: `AddAndTryAddTests` (Add/TryAdd new/duplicate/zero-key, duplicate leaves value unchanged), `ConstructorValidationTests` (negative-capacity throw and zero-capacity accept — the loadFactor rows genuinely do not apply, as `SmallDictionary` has no load factor), `ContainsValueTests` (empty-map false, regular-slot hit, default/zero value, post-`Remove` the swapped-out value does not linger, `null` value), `IEnumerableConstructorTests` (null-source `ArgumentNullException` with `paramName` `"source"`, duplicate-key `ArgumentException`, array / non-collection-enumerable copy, large-source fidelity), `IEnumerableConstructorNullPriorityTests` (null source beats the only other ctor validation it has — a negative `capacity`), `IndexerReturnTypeTests` (the primary indexer's declared return type is the non-nullable `TValue`), `ReadOnlyDictionaryInterfaceTests` (assignability, interface indexer / `TryGetValue` / `Keys` / `Values` / generic + non-generic enumeration / LINQ `Count`, and the polymorphic `IReadOnlyDictionary<int,int>` consumer), `RemoveOutValueTests` (captured-value path, missing-key / empty-map false, default-value capture, middle-slot removal keeping the rest, remove-then-reinsert, version bump invalidating an active enumerator), and `TryAddDuplicateResizeTests` (a duplicate `TryAdd` at exactly full capacity is a no-op that keeps an active enumerator valid; a new-key `TryAdd` that grows the arrays invalidates it). The hash-specific shared files do not apply and are intentionally not extended: `LoadFactorBoundaryTests` (no load factor), `TryAddProbeCountTests` and `IndexerOverwriteResizeTests` (both count `IHashProvider.Hash` calls — there is no hasher), and the `Set*` files (sets only).
- `SmallDictionaryBenchmark` in `Celerity.Benchmarks` — an `Insert` / `Lookup` / `Remove` comparison of `SmallDictionary<int, int>` against the BCL `Dictionary<int, int>` baseline. Unlike the hash-table benchmarks it uses **small** `[Params(8, 64)]` item counts rather than `1000 / 100_000`: `SmallDictionary` is a small-`n` collection whose `O(n)` scan is meant to win at low `n` and lose as `n` grows (and an `O(n²)` insert sweep at 100k would be both meaningless and far too slow for CI), so 8 (a clear win) and 64 (into the crossover region) show both sides honestly. Same per-`Remove` `[IterationSetup]` rebuild pattern as the other collection benchmarks. Registered in `Celerity.Benchmarks/Program.cs`'s `CoreBenchmarks` array so it joins the `RunAllJoined` CI report consumed by `github-action-benchmark` and published to the gh-pages benchmark history on every push to `main`.
- Dashboard wiring for `SmallDictionary`: a "What ships in the box" ship card in `web/index.html`, and a `COLLECTIONS` entry in both `web/dev/bench/index.html` (key / title / vs `Dictionary<int, int>` / ops `['Insert', 'Lookup', 'Remove']`) and `web/dev/bench/detail.html` (key / title / vs). Because `SmallDictionary` is benchmarked at `8 / 64` items rather than the `1000 / 100_000` the hash tables use, both dashboards were generalized to support **per-collection item counts**: each `COLLECTIONS` entry may now carry an optional `items` array (defaulting to `[1000, 100000]` when absent, preserving every existing collection's behaviour), and the chart cells, headline detail strings, detail-page item-count toggle buttons, and URL/param validation read from it. The baseline series parses as the existing `Dictionary` `BCL_TYPES` entry (the benchmark's baseline methods are named `Dictionary_*`), so no `BCL_TYPES` change is needed.
- `docs/api/collections.md` and `README.md` — a full `SmallDictionary` section in the API reference (the no-hasher / flat-array design and its trade-offs, constructors with the verbatim `capacity` and the absent `loadFactor`, `Count`, the indexer, every method, the inline default-key handling, and a runnable per-scope-symbol-table example), the README Collections list and "Choosing a collection" decision table updated to ship it (with the small-`n`-only guidance), a new "the tiny-map fast path" Quick start subsection, and the "all collections handle `default(TKey)` out-of-band" note corrected to carve out `SmallDictionary`'s inline default key. The `Celerity.AotSmokeTest` now constructs `SmallDictionary<int, int>` (indexer / Add / TryAdd / Remove / inline zero key / enumeration) and `SmallDictionary<string, int>` (the `IEnumerable` ctor and inline `null` key) so the Native AOT publish job compiles the new generic instantiations.

- Expanded the benchmark project (`src/Celerity.Benchmarks`) with an **extended, on-demand suite** that goes beyond the single random-key comparison ([#26](https://github.com/marius-bughiu/Celerity/issues/26), [#60](https://github.com/marius-bughiu/Celerity/issues/60)). New `KeyDistributions` helper generates **uniform / sequential / clustered / adversarial** integer and long key sets, and eight new benchmark classes use them: `DistributionBenchmark` (insert/lookup across distributions), `AdversarialHasherBenchmark` (shows `Int32WangNaiveHasher` degrading to O(n) on engineered collisions while `Int32Murmur3Hasher` stays O(1)), `LargeDatasetBenchmark` (1M/5M items), `MemoryAllocationBenchmark` (grow-vs-presized allocations with the full `MemoryDiagnoser` columns), `ConcurrentAccessBenchmark` (read scaling at 1/4/8 threads vs `ConcurrentDictionary<,>`), `CacheLocalityBenchmark` (in-order vs shuffled probing), `LibraryComparisonBenchmark` (vs the BCL `FrozenDictionary<,>`), and `RealWorldWorkloadBenchmark` (mixed ~80/12/8 read/write/remove stream with a hot key set). These run on demand (e.g. `dotnet run -c Release -- --filter "*Distribution*"`) and are **kept out of the per-PR CI regression run** so the same-runner A/B comparison stays fast and low-variance; `Program.cs` now splits a CI-tracked `CoreBenchmarks` set from the local-only `ExtendedBenchmarks` set. In CI they additionally run **weekly** (and on demand) via a new `benchmarks-extended.yml` workflow (`--ci-extended`), which publishes to a **separate `dev/bench-extended` dashboard** on gh-pages — linked as *Extended* in the site nav and kept apart from the per-commit core trend. Documented in [`docs/performance.md`](docs/performance.md#extended-benchmark-suite).
- `CelerityMultiMap<TKey, TValue, THasher>` in `Celerity.Collections` — a one-to-many map (multi-map / multi-dictionary): each key maps to an ordered *group* of values rather than a single value. The 1.2.0 one-to-many collection ([#18](https://github.com/marius-bughiu/Celerity/issues/18)). It reuses `CelerityDictionary`'s open-addressed, linear-probing key table and the same `where THasher : struct, IHashProvider<TKey>` constraint (so the JIT devirtualizes and inlines the key hash), storing a `List<TValue?>` value group alongside each key slot. `Add(key, value)` **always appends** — adding the same key twice groups the values, and adding the same value twice under one key keeps both copies. Public API: `Add`, `AddRange`, `Remove(key, value)` (removes one occurrence; removes the key when its group empties), `RemoveAll(key)` (removes the key and all its values), `Clear`, `ContainsKey`, `Contains(key, value)`, `ContainsValue(value)`, `CountValues(key)`, `TryGetValues(key, out ValueGroup)`, the `ValueGroup this[key]` indexer (returns an **empty group** for an absent key, matching `ILookup` semantics, rather than throwing), `Count` (distinct keys) and `ValueCount` (total values), an allocation-free struct `Enumerator` yielding one `Grouping` (`IGrouping<TKey, TValue?>`) per key, and a `Keys` view. Reads are allocation-free (the indexer / `TryGetValues` hand back a lightweight `ValueGroup` struct over the live backing list); the write path allocates one backing list per distinct key, inherent to storing a group per key. Implements `ILookup<TKey, TValue?>`, so it flows through LINQ. `default(TKey)` (`null` / `0` / `Guid.Empty`) is stored out-of-band — the hasher is never invoked with it, so it never collides with the empty-slot sentinel — and behaves as an ordinary key (yielded first in enumeration). The `IEnumerable<KeyValuePair<TKey, TValue>>` constructor groups duplicate keys in source order (duplicate keys are not an error, unlike the dictionaries); a `null` source throws `ArgumentNullException`, and `capacity` / `loadFactor` are validated exactly as the dictionaries. AOT-safe (no reflection).
- `CelerityMultiMapTests`, `CelerityMultiMapCollisionTests`, and `CelerityMultiMapEnumerationTests` — dedicated suites mirroring the `CelerityDictionary*` files for the grouping semantics: grouping Adds (including duplicate keys and duplicate values), the indexer/`TryGetValues` empty-on-miss group views, `Contains(key, value)` / `ContainsValue` / `CountValues`, both removal shapes (`Remove(key, value)` collapsing a key when its last value is removed, and `RemoveAll(key)`), `Clear`, `Count` vs `ValueCount`, `AddRange`, the out-of-band default-key group for `string` (`null`), `int` (`0`), and `Guid` (`Guid.Empty`), the `IEnumerable<KeyValuePair<,>>` grouping constructor, and the `ILookup<,>` surface; collision tests under a constant hasher (and an identity hasher for the wrapped-cluster branch) that assert grouping stays distinct under a single probe chain and that backward-shift deletion on a collapsed key never orphans the others; and enumeration tests for the struct `Grouping` enumerator (default-key group first), the per-group `ValueGroup` enumerator, the `Keys` view, mid-enumeration mutation detection (including a value-only `Add`/`Remove` on an existing key), and the boxed `IEnumerable<IGrouping<,>>` / non-generic paths.
- Cross-collection shared tests extended to cover `CelerityMultiMap`: `ConstructorValidationTests` (capacity / loadFactor validation, zero capacity, valid load factors), `ContainsValueTests` (the whole-map value scan including the default-key group and `null` values), `LoadFactorBoundaryTests` (early resize preserves every group; multiple resizes; the default-key group does not corrupt resize accounting), `IEnumerableConstructorTests` (null-source `ArgumentNullException`, grouping of duplicate keys in source order, non-collection-enumerable copy, null-string-key capture, large-source fidelity, independence from a mutated source, and flow through `ILookup<,>`), and `IEnumerableConstructorNullPriorityTests` (a `null` source surfaces as `ArgumentNullException` even with an invalid `loadFactor`). The single-value-dictionary shared files do not apply to a multi-map and are intentionally not extended: `AddAndTryAddTests` / `TryAddDuplicateResizeTests` / `TryAddProbeCountTests` (a multi-map has no `TryAdd`; `Add` appends and duplicates are allowed), `RemoveOutValueTests` (the removal shapes are `Remove(key, value)` / `RemoveAll(key)`, neither with an `out` value), `ReadOnlyDictionaryInterfaceTests` (the map implements `ILookup<,>`, not the single-value `IReadOnlyDictionary<,>`), `IndexerReturnTypeTests` / `IndexerOverwriteResizeTests` (the indexer returns a `ValueGroup` view and is get-only — there is no overwriting setter), and the `Set*` files (sets only).
- `CelerityMultiMapBenchmark` in `Celerity.Benchmarks` — an `Insert` / `Lookup` / `Remove` comparison of `CelerityMultiMap<int, int, Int32WangNaiveHasher>` against the idiomatic BCL multi-map baseline `Dictionary<int, List<int>>` (the fair like-for-like for a one-to-many map; a plain `Dictionary<,>` holds one value per key, so it is not a multi-map baseline), over the same `[Params(1000, 100_000)]` key sets with two values grouped per key, using the same per-`Remove` `[IterationSetup]` rebuild pattern as the other collection benchmarks. Registered in `Celerity.Benchmarks/Program.cs`'s `benchmarkTypes` array so it joins the `RunAllJoined` CI report consumed by `github-action-benchmark` and published to the gh-pages benchmark history on every push to `main`.
- Dashboard wiring for `CelerityMultiMap`: `web/index.html` "What ships in the box" ship card, and the `COLLECTIONS` arrays in `web/dev/bench/index.html` (key / title / vs `Dictionary<int, List<int>>` / ops `['Insert', 'Lookup', 'Remove']`) and `web/dev/bench/detail.html` (key / title / vs). The baseline series parses as the existing `Dictionary` `BCL_TYPES` entry (the benchmark's baseline methods are named `Dictionary_*`), so no `BCL_TYPES` change is needed.
- `docs/api/collections.md` and `README.md` — a full `CelerityMultiMap` section in the API reference (constructors, `Count` / `ValueCount`, the empty-on-miss indexer, every method, the `ValueGroup` / `Grouping` nested views, default-key handling, the `ILookup<,>` surface, and a runnable example), the README Collections list and "Choosing a collection" decision table updated to ship it, and a new "one key, many values" Quick start subsection. The `Celerity.AotSmokeTest` now constructs `CelerityMultiMap<string, int, StringFnV1AHasher>` (grouping Adds, the out-of-band `null` key, both removal shapes, the `ILookup<,>` surface) and `CelerityMultiMap<Guid, int, GuidHasher>` (the `Guid.Empty` default-key group) so the Native AOT publish job compiles the new generic instantiations.
- `FrozenCelerityDictionary<TValue>` / `FrozenCelerityDictionary<TValue, THasher>` in `Celerity.Collections` — a build-once, read-many dictionary for `string` keys, in the spirit of the BCL `System.Collections.Frozen.FrozenDictionary<,>` but tunable through Celerity's `IHashProvider<T>`. The flagship 1.2.0 collection ([#62](https://github.com/marius-bughiu/Celerity/issues/62)). It is immutable (constructed once from an `IEnumerable<KeyValuePair<string, TValue>>`, no mutating members) and at construction searches a small parameter space — candidate power-of-two table sizes × a per-build mixing seed — for a **perfect** (collision-free) placement of the keys; when found (`IsPerfectlyHashed == true`) a lookup is a single hash, a single array index, and a single equality check, with no probing. When two distinct keys collide on the chosen hasher's raw 32-bit code (e.g. `"A"` / `"Ł"` under the low-byte `StringFnV1AHasher`), a perfect placement is impossible — the mixing seed is a pure function of that code — so the build falls back to an open-addressed linear-probing table (`IsPerfectlyHashed == false`); lookups stay correct (the equality check disambiguates), just not single-probe. Read API: indexer get (throws `KeyNotFoundException` on miss), `ContainsKey`, `TryGetValue`, `ContainsValue`, `Count`, `IsPerfectlyHashed`, allocation-free struct `Keys` / `Values` views and enumerator (the `null`-key entry, if present, is yielded first), and `IReadOnlyDictionary<string, TValue?>`. The `null` key is stored out-of-band (the hasher is never invoked with `null`) and the empty string is an ordinary key; duplicate keys (including a duplicate `null` key) and a `null` source throw, matching the mutable Celerity dictionaries and BCL `FrozenDictionary`. The convenience `FrozenCelerityDictionary<TValue>` defaults to `StringFnV1AHasher`; the `<TValue, THasher>` overload accepts any string hasher (use a full-width or strong hasher for non-ASCII / adversarial keys to keep the single-probe fast path). AOT-safe (no reflection). Hot-path lookup is allocation-free.
- `FrozenCelerityDictionaryTests` — a dedicated suite (construction & round-trip, present/absent `TryGetValue`, missing-key `KeyNotFoundException`, empty-string-as-regular-key, out-of-band `null` key round-trip and absence, `null`-source / duplicate-key / duplicate-`null`-key validation, empty source, the perfect fast path asserted via `IsPerfectlyHashed` on a strong hasher, the **fallback correctness** case where base-hash-colliding `"A"` / `"Ł"` under `StringFnV1AHasher` force linear probing yet stay distinct and correct, absent-keys-hashing-into-occupied-slots miss, a 1000-key build-and-round-trip sweep with 1000 absent-key misses, `ContainsValue`, enumeration including the `null` key, `Keys` / `Values` views, the `IReadOnlyDictionary` surface, the custom-hasher overload, and the default convenience type).
- Cross-collection shared tests extended to cover `FrozenCelerityDictionary`: `ReadOnlyDictionaryInterfaceTests` (assignability, interface indexer / `TryGetValue` / `Keys` / `Values` / null-key / non-generic enumeration / LINQ `Count` — the mutation-detection test is intentionally omitted as the type is immutable), `IEnumerableConstructorTests` (its only constructor — null-source `ArgumentNullException` with `paramName` `"source"`, duplicate-key and duplicate-`null`-key `ArgumentException`, empty / array / non-collection-enumerable copy, null-string-key capture, large-source fidelity, independence from a mutated source, and flow through `IReadOnlyDictionary`), `ContainsValueTests` (the read-only-applicable variants), and `IndexerReturnTypeTests` (the primary indexer's declared return type is the non-nullable `TValue`). The mutation/resize/probe-count shared files do not apply to a read-only type.
- `FrozenCelerityDictionaryBenchmark` in `Celerity.Benchmarks` — a `Build` + `Lookup` comparison of `FrozenCelerityDictionary<int>` against the BCL `System.Collections.Frozen.FrozenDictionary<string, int>` baseline (the true build-once counterpart; a mutable `Dictionary<,>` does no build-time hashing optimization, so it is not a like-for-like baseline for a frozen, perfect-hashed dictionary), over the same `[Params(1000, 100_000)]` identifier-shaped distinct key sets. Registered in `Celerity.Benchmarks/Program.cs`'s `benchmarkTypes` array so it joins the `RunAllJoined` CI report consumed by `github-action-benchmark` and published to the gh-pages benchmark history on every push to `main`.
- Dashboard wiring for `FrozenCelerityDictionary`: `web/index.html` "What ships in the box" ship card, and the `COLLECTIONS` arrays in `web/dev/bench/index.html` (key / title / vs / ops `['Build', 'Lookup']`) and `web/dev/bench/detail.html` (key / title / vs). `FrozenDictionary` was added to each dashboard's `BCL_TYPES` set so the parser treats it as the baseline series for this collection (the comparison is Celerity-frozen vs BCL-frozen rather than vs the mutable `Dictionary<,>`).
- `docs/api/collections.md` and `README.md` — a full `FrozenCelerityDictionary` section in the API reference (both the convenience and `<TValue, THasher>` overloads: constructor contract, `Count` / `IsPerfectlyHashed`, indexer, methods, the perfect-hash fast path vs the linear-probing fallback, null-key handling, and runnable examples), the README Collections list and "Choosing a collection" decision table updated to ship it (replacing the "still on the roadmap" note), a new "build-once string lookups" Quick start subsection, and removal of the stale "not the right answer today" bullet that pointed at the BCL `FrozenDictionary`. The `Celerity.AotSmokeTest` now constructs `FrozenCelerityDictionary<int>` (default), `FrozenCelerityDictionary<int, StringMurmur3Hasher>`, and the base-hash-collision fallback (`StringFnV1AHasher` over `"A"` / `"Ł"`) so the Native AOT publish job compiles the new generic instantiations and exercises both lookup paths.
- `StringAdler32Hasher` in `Celerity.Hashing` — the standard **Adler-32** checksum (RFC 1950 — the zlib / PNG variant) hash provider for `string` keys, over the full little-endian UTF-16 byte stream (both bytes of every character). Struct hasher, `[MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]`.
