It is the table-free checksum sibling of `StringCrc32Hasher`: the two are the widely deployed zlib-family checksums, and this fills out the checksum corner of the cheap tier alongside CRC-32. Adler-32 carries two running 16-bit sums modulo `65521` (the largest prime below 2^16) — `a` accumulates the bytes (seeded to `1`), `b` accumulates the running value of `a` after each byte (seeded to `0`) — and packs the result as `(b << 16) | a`. It uses the straightforward per-byte modulo form (two adds and two modulo reductions per byte) with **no table** (unlike the table-driven `StringCrc32Hasher`) and no finalizer, so the per-call path is allocation-free. As a checksum it is **even weaker than CRC-32 as a hash**: for short inputs both sums stay numerically small, so the high bits of the 32-bit result are barely populated and unrelated short keys cluster badly (its low 16 bits are just the byte-sum, so same-length keys whose bytes sum equally collide). Its value here is purely **compatibility** — Adler-32 backs zlib's DEFLATE wrapper, the zlib chunk of PNG, and the rsync rolling-checksum family — so this hasher is the in-box answer when you need to reproduce an Adler-32-based key distribution exactly, the same role `StringCrc32Hasher`, `StringMurmur2Hasher`, and the FNV-1 hashers fill for their external systems; it is not a general-purpose hash. Like the other full-width string hashers it folds both bytes of every 16-bit code unit (low byte then high byte), exactly Adler-32 over the string's native little-endian UTF-16 byte stream, so it distinguishes characters that differ only in their upper byte (e.g. `'A'` `U+0041` vs `'Ł'` `U+0141`, which `StringFnV1AHasher` collides on). `StringAdler32Hasher.Hash(s)` equals the standard Adler-32 over `Encoding.Unicode.GetBytes(s)`; the empty string maps to `1` (`a` stays at its seed `1`, `b` at `0`), and the dictionaries route the out-of-band `null` key around the hasher so this never collides with the empty-slot sentinel. `Hash(null)` throws `ArgumentNullException` (parameter `"key"`), matching the other string hashers. Prefer `StringFnV1AFullHasher` or `StringJenkinsOaatHasher` for general use; reach for `StringAdler32Hasher` only when you specifically need Adler-32 compatibility. Tracked in [#158](https://github.com/marius-bughiu/Celerity/issues/158).
- `StringAdler32HasherTests` — mirrors `StringCrc32HasherTests` for the Adler-32 path, anchored to ground truth: a `Reference_MatchesCanonicalCheckVector` test asserting the test's own independently-written byte-oriented Adler-32 reference reproduces the universal Adler-32 check value (`Adler32("Wikipedia")` ASCII `== 0x11E60398`), so the spec-equivalence theory is pinned to the published standard rather than to a hand-computed value of the hasher itself; the empty-string `1` anchor; a thirteen-case spec-equivalence theory asserting the hasher equals the standard Adler-32 over `Encoding.Unicode.GetBytes(...)` across ASCII / mixed / CJK / embedded-NUL / surrogate-pair inputs and even/odd lengths, pinning the modulus, the seeds, the running-sum order, the byte order, and the `(b << 16) | a` packing without sharing the hasher's char-loop; a `Hash_DiffersFromOtherClassicHashers_ForTypicalInputs` guard asserting Adler-32 is genuinely distinct from `StringCrc32Hasher`, `StringElfHasher`, and `StringDjb2Hasher` (not an accidental alias); determinism across calls and across stateless struct instances; case sensitivity, single-character-change, and append-character avalanche guards; the full-character-distinction regressions shared with the other full-width string hashers (`StringFnV1AHasher` collides `"A"` / `"Ł"` and `"AB"` / `"Łł"`, `StringAdler32Hasher` keeps them distinct); a 1000-key distinctness sweep over a deliberately distinct-byte-sum corpus (each key appends `i` copies of one character so its byte-sum is `P + 97·i`, all distinct mod 65521) — confirming the hasher separates keys it *can* separate, while the type's docs note that arbitrary short keys do not get that guarantee; `Hash(null)` throwing `ArgumentNullException`; and integration tests driving `CelerityDictionary<string, …, StringAdler32Hasher>` and `CeleritySet<string, StringAdler32Hasher>`, including the empty-string regular key, a non-ASCII key, the out-of-band `null` key, and a regression that `'A'` / `'Ł'` are kept as distinct dictionary keys on the probe path.
- `StringHasherBenchmark` (in `Celerity.Benchmarks`) extended with an `Adler32()` `[Benchmark]` in the `Hash` category so the new hasher joins the head-to-head string-hasher throughput comparison across all three key `Shape`s, alongside the existing `Crc32()` checksum benchmark; it flows into the `RunAllJoined` CI report and the gh-pages **Hash function throughput** dashboard section automatically on the next push to `main` (no `Program.cs` change needed — `StringHasherBenchmark` is already registered).
- `docs/api/hashing.md` and `README.md` — a full `StringAdler32Hasher` section (algorithm, the two running 16-bit sums modulo 65521 and the `(b << 16) | a` packing, how it is the table-free checksum sibling of `StringCrc32Hasher`, the even-weaker-than-CRC-32 short-key clustering tradeoff, the Adler-32-compatibility framing, the full-character fold, the universal `0x11E60398` check value, and the `1` empty-string note) added immediately after the `StringCrc32Hasher` entry, the choosing-a-hasher table's `string` row extended to list it next to CRC-32 as the table-free Adler-32-compatibility checksum, and the README `string` hasher-picking bullet extended with the same Adler-32 note. The `Celerity.AotSmokeTest` hasher spread now also constructs a `CelerityDictionary<string, int, StringAdler32Hasher>` so the Native AOT publish job compiles the new generic instantiation.
- `--hash-quality` report mode in `Celerity.Benchmarks` (`HashQualityReportRunner`) — the **distribution** half of the hasher comparison and the offline companion to the throughput benchmarks. `dotnet run -c Release -- --hash-quality` runs `HashQualityEvaluator` over every built-in `string`, integer, and `Guid` hasher and prints GitHub-flavored markdown tables (`DistributionScore`, max bucket load, raw collisions) for 2000 distinct keys across 4096 buckets. Because distribution quality is deterministic — independent of CI hardware / timing noise — these numbers are stable enough to cite directly, unlike throughput. Surfaced a real finding now documented in the choosing-a-hasher guidance: **`StringElfHasher` clusters badly on ASCII keys** (`DistributionScore` ≈ 11.4, max bucket load 31 vs ~4–5 for every other hasher), because the PJW/ELF hash's low output bits mix poorly for ASCII-range inputs; every other hasher distributes near-ideally (≈ 0.97–1.03) on the sample. Closes the "pair throughput with the offline distribution metric" item from issue #155.
- `HasherKeySamples` in `Celerity.Benchmarks` — extracted the deterministic key-sample generation (the three `string` shapes and the integer / `Guid` samples) into one shared, **de-duplicated** source used by both the throughput benchmarks and the `--hash-quality` report, so a hasher's measured speed and its measured distribution describe the *same* keys. `StringHasherBenchmark` and `IntegerHasherBenchmark` now build their samples through it (keys are now guaranteed distinct, which `HashQualityEvaluator` requires and which leaves throughput unaffected).
- `docs/api/hashing.md` — a new "Measured distribution quality" subsection under Benchmarking with the real `--hash-quality` numbers (the three `string`-shape tables and a combined integer / `Guid` table), the `StringElfHasher` ASCII-clustering finding called out, and the reproduction command; the `StringElfHasher` reference section and the choosing-a-hasher table's `string` row are corrected to warn that ELF clusters on ASCII keys (its previous "good for short ASCII identifiers" guidance was contradicted by the measurement) and point to djb2 / sdbm instead. Delivers the distribution half of the "document the measured speed/distribution tradeoffs" item from issue #155 (the throughput half cites the live dashboard, whose numbers are CI-hardware-dependent).
- `StringHasherBenchmark` in `Celerity.Benchmarks` — a head-to-head BenchmarkDotNet throughput comparison of **every** built-in `string` hasher (the 22 currently on `main`: djb2 / djb2a / sdbm / elf / CRC-32, the full FNV-1 and FNV-1a matrix, Jenkins one-at-a-time, Murmur2 / Murmur3, XXH32 / XXH64 / XXH3, CityHash64, MetroHash64, SipHash-1-3 / SipHash-2-4 / HalfSipHash-2-4, and HighwayHash64). Each benchmark hashes a deterministic sample of `2000` distinct keys through one hasher via the `where THasher : struct, IHashProvider<string>` constraint — so the JIT devirtualizes and inlines `Hash` exactly as it does on a real Celerity collection's probe path — XOR-folding the codes into a returned value so the loop can't be elided, with the BCL `string.GetHashCode()` as the `[Benchmark(Baseline = true)]` so each ratio reads as "this hasher relative to the framework string hash". A `[Params]` `Shape` sweep over three representative key shapes — `ShortAscii` (6–12-char identifiers), `LongAscii` (48–80-char path/URL-like keys), and `NonAscii` (10–20-char mixed Latin + CJK) — captures how the length-classed hashers (`StringCityHash64Hasher`, `StringXxHash3Hasher`) and the four-accumulator stripe hashers (`StringXxHash32Hasher`, `StringXxHash64Hasher`) diverge across lengths and how the full-width hashers pay for non-ASCII upper bytes. Hashers are stateless structs instantiated via `default`, so no per-iteration setup is needed (unlike the collection `Remove` benchmarks). This delivers the core line item from issue #24 that had not shipped — *"Benchmarks comparing all hash functions"* — which had been carried over to issue #155 (the benchmark suite was previously collection-only). Addresses issue #155: this and the entries below add the benchmark, the optional `IntegerHasherBenchmark` companion, and the gh-pages dashboard **Hash function throughput** section. The one remaining follow-up — folding the *measured* numbers into the choosing-a-hasher prose — depends on a first post-merge CI run producing data and is tracked in that issue.
- `Celerity.Benchmarks/Program.cs` — `StringHasherBenchmark` registered in the `benchmarkTypes` array so it joins the `RunAllJoined` CI report (`BenchmarkRun-joined-report-full.json`) that `github-action-benchmark` consumes and publishes to the gh-pages benchmark history on every push to `main`.
- `IntegerHasherBenchmark` in `Celerity.Benchmarks` — companion to `StringHasherBenchmark` for the fixed-width integer and `Guid` hashers, grouped by key type via `[BenchmarkCategory]` (`int` → `Int32WangNaiveHasher` / `Int32WangHasher` / `Int32Murmur3Hasher`; `long`, `uint`, `ulong` mirrors; `Guid` → `GuidHasher`), each category baselined against that type's BCL `GetHashCode()`. Same `where THasher : struct, IHashProvider<T>` inlined-`Hash` pattern and XOR-fold-to-return as the string benchmark, over a deterministic 2000-key sample per type. No key-shape `[Params]`: hashing a fixed-width integer is branch-free and constant-time regardless of value, so the sample distribution affects collision *quality* (measured offline by `HashQualityEvaluator`) but not `Hash` throughput. Method names follow `{Type}_{Hasher}` so the dashboard can group them. Registered in `Program.cs`. Completes the optional integer-hasher item from issue #155's scope.
- `web/dev/bench/index.html` — a new **Hash function throughput** dashboard section that renders both hasher benchmarks. It parses the `StringHasherBenchmark.{Method}(Shape: {Shape})` and `IntegerHasherBenchmark.{Type}_{Hasher}` benchmark names out of the joined gh-pages report and draws, per key-type / key-shape group, one ranked horizontal bar per hasher (fastest first) with its ratio versus the framework `GetHashCode()` baseline and its mean time. Implemented as an independent `<script>` IIFE (a bug there cannot break the per-collection charts and vice versa) that stays hidden until the report actually contains hasher benchmarks, so it lights up automatically after the first post-merge `main` benchmark run. Addresses the "wire the hasher comparison into the gh-pages dashboard" follow-up from issue #155; because the comparison is hasher-vs-hasher rather than collection-vs-BCL it is a new section rather than a `COLLECTIONS` entry, as that issue anticipated.
- `docs/api/hashing.md` — a new "Benchmarking the string hashers" section documenting `StringHasherBenchmark` and `IntegerHasherBenchmark`, the three `Shape` key shapes and why they matter, the per-type BCL `GetHashCode()` baselines, the live-dashboard **Hash function throughput** section and the local run command, and an explicit note that the benchmarks measure **throughput only**, cross-referencing `HashQualityEvaluator` so callers read speed alongside distribution quality (a fast hasher that clusters is not a win) when choosing a hasher. `README.md`'s Benchmarks section updated to name both hasher benchmarks and the dashboard section.
- `StringCrc32Hasher` in `Celerity.Hashing` — the standard **CRC-32** (ISO-HDLC / IEEE 802.3 — the zlib / gzip / PNG / Ethernet variant; reflected generator polynomial `0xEDB88320`, initial value `0xFFFFFFFF`, final XOR `0xFFFFFFFF`) hash provider for `string` keys, over the full little-endian UTF-16 byte stream (both bytes of every character). Struct hasher, `[MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]`. It is the **first table-driven** member of the `string` hasher family — the cheap classics `StringDjb2Hasher`, `StringSdbmHasher`, and `StringElfHasher` are all table-free — using the classic 256-entry byte lookup table (one table lookup, one XOR, one shift per byte) held in a single `static readonly` array built once at type initialization, so the per-call path stays allocation-free. CRC-32 is a cyclic redundancy check rather than a designed mixer: the remainder of the message (interpreted as a polynomial over GF(2)) divided by the reflected generator, pre-set to all-ones and bit-inverted at the end. Because it is **linear** over GF(2) its avalanche is weaker than the designed mixers (flipping one input bit flips a fixed, input-independent set of output bits, and the low bits mix poorly), so it clusters sooner than `StringJenkinsOaatHasher` or the strong block hashes on adversarial or heavily clustered keys; its value here is **compatibility** — CRC-32 is one of the most widely deployed checksums and many external systems shard / route / bucket by it, so this hasher is the in-box answer when you need to reproduce a CRC-32-based key distribution exactly, the same role `StringMurmur2Hasher` and the FNV-1 hashers fill for their external systems. Like the other full-width string hashers it folds both bytes of every 16-bit code unit (low byte then high byte), exactly CRC-32 over the string's native little-endian UTF-16 byte stream, so it distinguishes characters that differ only in their upper byte (e.g. `'A'` `U+0041` vs `'Ł'` `U+0141`, which `StringFnV1AHasher` collides on). `StringCrc32Hasher.Hash(s)` equals the standard CRC-32 over `Encoding.Unicode.GetBytes(s)`; the empty string maps to `0` (the initial `0xFFFFFFFF` XORed with the final `0xFFFFFFFF`), and the dictionaries route the out-of-band `null` key around the hasher so this never collides with the empty-slot sentinel. `Hash(null)` throws `ArgumentNullException` (parameter `"key"`), matching the other string hashers. Prefer `StringFnV1AFullHasher` or `StringJenkinsOaatHasher` for general use; reach for `StringCrc32Hasher` when you specifically need CRC-32 compatibility, and escalate to the throughput-oriented strong family for clustered or adversarial keys. Incremental progress on issue #24.
- `StringCrc32HasherTests` — mirrors `StringMurmur2HasherTests` for the CRC-32 path, anchored to ground truth: a `Reference_MatchesCanonicalCheckVector` test asserting the test's own independently-written **table-free, bit-by-bit** CRC-32 reference reproduces the universal CRC-32 check value (`CRC32("123456789")` ASCII `== 0xCBF43926`), so the spec-equivalence theory is pinned to the published standard rather than to a hand-computed value of the hasher itself; the empty-string `0` anchor; a thirteen-case spec-equivalence theory asserting the table-driven hasher equals the bitwise reference (the standard CRC-32) over `Encoding.Unicode.GetBytes(...)` across ASCII / mixed / CJK / embedded-NUL / surrogate-pair inputs and even/odd lengths, pinning the polynomial, the reflected bit order, the `0xFFFFFFFF` pre-set and final XOR, the byte order, and the table-vs-bitwise equivalence without sharing the hasher's char-loop; a `Hash_DiffersFromOtherClassicHashers_ForTypicalInputs` guard asserting CRC-32 is genuinely distinct from `StringElfHasher` and `StringDjb2Hasher` (not an accidental alias); determinism across calls and across stateless struct instances; case sensitivity, single-character-change, and append-character avalanche guards; the full-character-distinction regressions shared with the other full-width string hashers (`StringFnV1AHasher` collides `"A"` / `"Ł"` and `"AB"` / `"Łł"`, `StringCrc32Hasher` keeps them distinct); a 1000-distinct-string distinctness sweep; `Hash(null)` throwing `ArgumentNullException`; and integration tests driving `CelerityDictionary<string, …, StringCrc32Hasher>` and `CeleritySet<string, StringCrc32Hasher>`, including the empty-string regular key, a non-ASCII key, the out-of-band `null` key, and a regression that `'A'` / `'Ł'` are kept as distinct dictionary keys on the probe path.
- `docs/api/hashing.md` and `README.md` — a full `StringCrc32Hasher` section (algorithm, the reflected `0xEDB88320` polynomial and `0xFFFFFFFF` pre-set / final-XOR, the 256-entry lookup table and how it is the family's only table-driven member, the linear-checksum / weaker-avalanche tradeoff, the CRC-32-compatibility framing, the full-character fold, the universal `0xCBF43926` check value, and the `0` empty-string note) added immediately after the `StringElfHasher` entry, the choosing-a-hasher table's `string` row extended to list it next to the table-free classics as the table-driven CRC-32-compatibility option, and the README `string` hasher-picking bullet extended with the same CRC-32 note. The `Celerity.AotSmokeTest` hasher spread now also constructs a `CelerityDictionary<string, int, StringCrc32Hasher>` so the Native AOT publish job compiles the new generic instantiation.
- `StringMurmur2Hasher` in `Celerity.Hashing` — Austin Appleby's original **MurmurHash2** (32-bit, seed `0`) hash provider for `string` keys, over the full little-endian UTF-16 byte stream (both bytes of every character). Struct hasher, `[MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]`. It is the MurmurHash2 predecessor of `StringMurmur3Hasher`: the two share the same family and the same multiply constant `m = 0x5bd1e995`, but MurmurHash2 uses a single mixing pass per 4-byte block (`k *= m; k ^= k >> 24; k *= m; h *= m; h ^= k`) and a lighter two-shift finalization (`h ^= h >> 13; h *= m; h ^= h >> 15`), where MurmurHash3 adds a rotate-based block mix and the stronger `fmix32` finalizer that gives every input bit influence over every output bit and avoids the known MurmurHash2 weaknesses (most notably that XOR-equal differences in adjacent blocks can cancel) — which is why `StringMurmur3Hasher` remains the generally preferred member of the family. `StringMurmur2Hasher` is provided for users who specifically need MurmurHash2 — e.g. to match an external system (Hadoop, Cassandra, Elasticsearch, and many client libraries have historically hashed with MurmurHash2) — or who want its slightly cheaper single-multiply-per-block mix on trusted, already-uniform keys. Like the other full-width string hashers it folds both bytes of every 16-bit code unit (two consecutive chars form one little-endian 32-bit block; a trailing odd char is a 2-byte tail), exactly MurmurHash2 over the string's native little-endian UTF-16 byte stream, so it distinguishes characters that differ only in their upper byte (e.g. `'A'` `U+0041` vs `'Ł'` `U+0141`, which `StringFnV1AHasher` collides on). `StringMurmur2Hasher.Hash(s)` equals canonical MurmurHash2 (seed `0`) over `Encoding.Unicode.GetBytes(s)`; the empty string maps to `0` (seed `0` XOR a zero byte length, left unchanged by the finalization mix), exactly as `StringMurmur3Hasher` maps the empty string, and the dictionaries route the out-of-band `null` key around the hasher so this never collides with the empty-slot sentinel. `Hash(null)` throws `ArgumentNullException` (parameter `"key"`), matching the other string hashers. Incremental progress on issue #24.
- `StringMurmur2HasherTests` — mirrors `StringMurmur3HasherTests` / `StringFnV164HasherTests` for the MurmurHash2 path: the empty-string `0` anchor; a thirteen-case spec-equivalence theory asserting the hasher equals canonical MurmurHash2 (seed `0`) over `Encoding.Unicode.GetBytes(...)` — an independently-written byte-oriented reference with the literal 4-byte-block loop and the canonical `switch` fall-through tail, sharing no code with the hasher's char-loop, pinning the byte order, block read, per-block mix, tail handling, and finalizer — across ASCII / mixed / CJK / embedded-NUL / surrogate-pair inputs and even/odd lengths; an independent algebraic pin for single ASCII characters re-deriving the 2-byte-tail path from the MurmurHash2 definition; a `Hash_DiffersFromMurmur3_ForTypicalInputs` guard asserting MurmurHash2 and MurmurHash3 are genuinely distinct (not an accidental alias); determinism across calls and across stateless struct instances; case sensitivity, single-character-change, and append-character avalanche guards; the full-character-distinction regressions shared with the other full-width string hashers (`StringFnV1AHasher` collides `"A"` / `"Ł"` and `"AB"` / `"Łł"`, `StringMurmur2Hasher` keeps them distinct); a 1000-distinct-string distinctness sweep; `Hash(null)` throwing `ArgumentNullException`; and integration tests driving `CelerityDictionary<string, …, StringMurmur2Hasher>` and `CeleritySet<string, StringMurmur2Hasher>`, including the empty-string regular key, a non-ASCII key, the out-of-band `null` key, and a regression that `'A'` / `'Ł'` are kept as distinct dictionary keys on the probe path.
- `docs/api/hashing.md` and `README.md` — a full `StringMurmur2Hasher` section (algorithm, the single per-block mix and two-shift finalization, how it relates to `StringMurmur3Hasher` as its predecessor, the MurmurHash2-compatibility-vs-prefer-MurmurHash3 framing, the full-character fold and the `0` empty-string note) added immediately before the `StringMurmur3Hasher` entry, the choosing-a-hasher table's `string` row extended to name it as the MurmurHash2-compatibility sibling of `StringMurmur3Hasher`, and the README `string` hasher-picking bullet extended with the same MurmurHash2 note. The `Celerity.AotSmokeTest` hasher spread now also constructs a `CelerityDictionary<string, int, StringMurmur2Hasher>` so the Native AOT publish job compiles the new generic instantiation.
- `StringFnV164Hasher` in `Celerity.Hashing` — the original **FNV-1 64-bit** (multiply-then-XOR) hash provider for `string` keys, over the full little-endian UTF-16 byte stream (both bytes of every character), xor-folded down to a signed 32-bit result. Struct hasher, `[MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]`. It is the wide-accumulator counterpart to `StringFnV1Hasher` and the FNV-1 counterpart to `StringFnV1A64Hasher`, completing the symmetric FNV family: FNV-1a already had both a 32-bit-full (`StringFnV1AFullHasher`) and a 64-bit (`StringFnV1A64Hasher`) variant, but FNV-1 only had the 32-bit-full `StringFnV1Hasher` — this fills the missing 64-bit FNV-1 rung. It seeds the accumulator with the same 64-bit offset basis `14695981039346656037` and folds each byte with the FNV-1 ordering `hash = hash * prime; hash ^= b` (prime `1099511628211`), the inverse of `StringFnV1A64Hasher`'s XOR-then-multiply, exactly the relationship `StringFnV1Hasher` has to `StringFnV1AFullHasher`. Because FNV-1's last byte is only XORed in with no following multiply to diffuse it, a change in the trailing byte avalanches less thoroughly than under FNV-1a, which is why FNV-1a remains the generally preferred default; `StringFnV164Hasher` is provided for users who specifically need the original FNV-1 ordering at 64-bit width (e.g. to match an external system that hashes with FNV-1-64). Carrying twice as many bits through the accumulation as `StringFnV1Hasher` means intermediate values collide far less often, so for longer keys and larger key sets the distribution holds up better before the final `h ^ (h >> 32)` retraction fold; each multiply is 64-bit, which on 64-bit platforms is the same throughput as a 32-bit multiply, so the wider state is effectively free there. Like the other full-width string hashers it folds both bytes of every 16-bit code unit (low byte then high byte), exactly FNV-1-64 over the string's native little-endian UTF-16 byte stream, so it distinguishes characters that differ only in their upper byte (e.g. `'A'` `U+0041` vs `'Ł'` `U+0141`, which `StringFnV1AHasher` collides on). The empty string maps to the 64-bit offset basis folded to 32 bits, exactly as `StringFnV1A64Hasher` maps the empty string (FNV-1 and FNV-1a share the same offset basis), and the dictionaries route the out-of-band `null` key around the hasher so this never collides with the empty-slot sentinel. `Hash(null)` throws `ArgumentNullException` (parameter `"key"`), matching the other string hashers. Prefer `StringFnV1A64Hasher` for general use; reach for `StringFnV164Hasher` when you need FNV-1's ordering at the wider 64-bit width, and escalate to the throughput-oriented strong family for clustered or adversarial keys. Incremental progress on issue #24.
- `StringFnV164HasherTests` — mirrors `StringFnV1A64HasherTests` for the FNV-1 64-bit path: the empty-string folded-offset-basis anchor (expressed symbolically so it pins the fold direction without a hand-computed constant); a twelve-case spec-equivalence theory asserting the hasher equals plain FNV-1-64 (multiply-then-XOR) over `Encoding.Unicode.GetBytes(...)` xor-folded to 32 bits across ASCII / mixed / CJK / embedded-NUL / surrogate-pair inputs (an independent reference that pins byte order, the per-character fold, the FNV-1 step order, and the final fold without sharing the hasher's char-loop); an independent algebraic pin for single ASCII characters re-deriving the pre-fold 64-bit accumulator from the FNV-1 definition (`((offsetBasis * prime) ^ lowByte) * prime`, which would deliberately *not* hold for FNV-1a's ordering) and then folding; a `Hash_DiffersFromFnv1a64_ForTypicalInputs` guard asserting the 64-bit FNV-1 and FNV-1a produce different results (so the two are genuinely distinct, not an accidental alias); determinism across calls and across stateless struct instances; case sensitivity, single-character-change, and append-character avalanche guards; the full-character-distinction regressions shared with the other full-width string hashers (`StringFnV1AHasher` collides `"A"` / `"Ł"` and `"AB"` / `"Łł"`, `StringFnV164Hasher` keeps them distinct); a 1000-distinct-string distinctness sweep; `Hash(null)` throwing `ArgumentNullException`; and integration tests driving `CelerityDictionary<string, …, StringFnV164Hasher>` and `CeleritySet<string, StringFnV164Hasher>`, including the empty-string regular key, a non-ASCII key, the out-of-band `null` key, and a regression that `'A'` / `'Ł'` are kept as distinct dictionary keys on the probe path.
- `docs/api/hashing.md` and `README.md` — a full `StringFnV164Hasher` section (algorithm, the 64-bit accumulator and `h ^ (h >> 32)` xor-fold, the multiply-then-XOR FNV-1 ordering and how it relates to `StringFnV1A64Hasher` exactly as `StringFnV1Hasher` relates to `StringFnV1AFullHasher`, the trailing-byte avalanche tradeoff and the resulting "prefer FNV-1a" recommendation, the FNV-1-64-over-UTF-16 equivalence and the folded-offset-basis empty-string note) added immediately after the `StringFnV1A64Hasher` entry, the `StringFnV1Hasher` section re-pointed at it as the wider-state FNV-1 step-up, the choosing-a-hasher table's `string` row extended to list it next to `StringFnV1Hasher`, and the README `string` hasher-picking bullet extended with the 64-bit FNV-1 step. The `Celerity.AotSmokeTest` hasher spread now also constructs a `CelerityDictionary<string, int, StringFnV164Hasher>` so the Native AOT publish job compiles the new generic instantiation.
- `StringDjb2AHasher` in `Celerity.Hashing` — the **djb2a** (XOR-folding) variant of Daniel J. Bernstein's djb2 hash provider for `string` keys, over the full little-endian UTF-16 byte stream (both bytes of every character). Struct hasher, `[MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]`. It seeds the accumulator with the same magic constant `5381` as `StringDjb2Hasher` and folds each byte with `hash = hash * 33 ^ b`; the **only** difference from `StringDjb2Hasher` is the final combine — djb2 *adds* the byte (`* 33 + b`), djb2a *XORs* it (`* 33 ^ b`), exactly the relationship FNV-1 and FNV-1a have to each other, which is why this type mirrors the `StringFnV1Hasher` / `StringFnV1AHasher` naming. As in djb2 the `* 33` lowers to a shift-and-add (`(hash << 5) + hash`), so it stays **multiply-free, table-free, and finalizer-free**, joining `StringDjb2Hasher`, `StringSdbmHasher`, and `StringElfHasher` at the cheapest, classic end of the `string` escalation ladder. Replacing the trailing add with an XOR sidesteps djb2's low-bit carry bias, so djb2a tends to diffuse the freshly-folded byte a touch more evenly than djb2; it is still a single combine per byte with no shift/xor avalanche step, so like djb2/sdbm/elf a single changed byte propagates less thoroughly than under `StringJenkinsOaatHasher`. Like the other full-width string hashers it folds both bytes of every 16-bit code unit (low byte then high byte), exactly djb2a over the string's native little-endian UTF-16 byte stream, so it distinguishes characters that differ only in their upper byte (e.g. `'A'` `U+0041` vs `'Ł'` `U+0141`, which `StringFnV1AHasher` collides on). The empty string maps to the seed constant `5381` (no characters are folded), exactly as `StringDjb2Hasher` maps the empty string, and the dictionaries route the out-of-band `null` key around the hasher so this never collides with the empty-slot sentinel. `Hash(null)` throws `ArgumentNullException` (parameter `"key"`), matching the other string hashers. Prefer it over `StringDjb2Hasher` when you want the same minimal djb2 cost with the XOR fold's slightly cleaner low-bit diffusion; step up to `StringJenkinsOaatHasher` or the FNV-1a variants when djb2a's weak avalanche clusters keys, and escalate to the throughput-oriented strong family for clustered or adversarial keys. Incremental progress on issue #24.
- `StringDjb2AHasherTests` — mirrors `StringDjb2HasherTests` for the djb2a path: the empty-string seed-constant anchor (`Hash("") == 5381`); a twelve-case spec-equivalence theory asserting the hasher equals djb2a (`hash = hash * 33 ^ b`) over `Encoding.Unicode.GetBytes(...)` across ASCII / mixed / CJK / embedded-NUL / surrogate-pair inputs (an independent reference that pins byte order, the per-character fold, and the XOR combine without sharing the hasher's char-loop); an independent hand-computed value anchor for a single ASCII character (`((5381 * 33) ^ 0x61) * 33 ^ 0x00`) that pins the seed, the per-byte step, and the byte order to the algorithm definition; a `Hash_DiffersFromAdditiveDjb2` guard asserting djb2a and the additive djb2 produce different results for typical inputs (so the XOR variant is genuinely distinct, not an accidental alias of djb2); determinism across calls and across stateless struct instances; case sensitivity, single-character-change, and append-character avalanche guards; the full-character-distinction regressions shared with the other full-width string hashers (`StringFnV1AHasher` collides `"A"` / `"Ł"` and `"AB"` / `"Łł"`, `StringDjb2AHasher` keeps them distinct); a 1000-distinct-string distinctness sweep; `Hash(null)` throwing `ArgumentNullException`; and integration tests driving `CelerityDictionary<string, …, StringDjb2AHasher>` and `CeleritySet<string, StringDjb2AHasher>`, including the empty-string regular key, a non-ASCII key, the out-of-band `null` key, and a regression that `'A'` / `'Ł'` are kept as distinct dictionary keys on the probe path.
- `docs/api/hashing.md` and `README.md` — a full `StringDjb2AHasher` section (algorithm, the shared `5381` seed and the `* 33 ^ b` XOR fold, how the only difference from `StringDjb2Hasher` is add-vs-XOR mirroring the FNV-1/FNV-1a split, the cheaper low-bit diffusion tradeoff, the full-character fold and the `5381` empty-string note) added immediately after the `StringDjb2Hasher` entry, the `StringDjb2Hasher` / `StringSdbmHasher` / `StringElfHasher` escalation-ladder lines cross-referenced to name djb2a as their peer, the choosing-a-hasher table's `string` row extended to list it next to djb2, and the README `string` hasher-picking bullet extended with the djb2a step. The `Celerity.AotSmokeTest` hasher spread now also constructs a `CelerityDictionary<string, int, StringDjb2AHasher>` so the Native AOT publish job compiles the new generic instantiation.
- `StringElfHasher` in `Celerity.Hashing` — the classic **PJW / ELF** hash provider for `string` keys, over the full little-endian UTF-16 byte stream (both bytes of every character). Struct hasher, `[MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]`. It is Peter J. Weinberger's hash from the "Dragon Book" (Aho/Sethi/Ullman) in the exact 32-bit form standardized as the `elf_hash` used by the System V ABI for ELF object-file symbol tables, and it joins `StringDjb2Hasher` and `StringSdbmHasher` as a third peer at the cheapest, classic, multiply-free end of the `string` escalation ladder. The accumulator is seeded with `0` and each byte `b` is folded with `hash = (hash << 4) + b; high = hash & 0xF0000000; if (high != 0) hash ^= high >> 24; hash &= ~high`: the shift-by-4 walks new bytes up through the accumulator, and whenever data reaches the top nibble those four bits are folded back down into bits 4–7 (`high >> 24`) and then cleared, so the state never grows past 28 bits and high-order entropy is recirculated rather than discarded. That top-nibble feedback gives it a touch more diffusion than the pure shift-and-add classics while staying multiply-free, table-free, and finalizer-free; it still lacks a full avalanche step, so like djb2/sdbm a single changed byte propagates less thoroughly than under `StringJenkinsOaatHasher`. Because the top nibble is always cleared, the result is a non-negative 28-bit value (`[0, 0x0FFFFFFF]`), which is immaterial once the dictionary masks the hash to the table size. Like the other full-width string hashers it folds both bytes of every 16-bit code unit (low byte then high byte), exactly the ELF hash over the string's native little-endian UTF-16 byte stream, so it distinguishes characters that differ only in their upper byte (e.g. `'A'` `U+0041` vs `'Ł'` `U+0141`, which `StringFnV1AHasher` collides on). The empty string maps to the seed constant `0` (no characters are folded), and the dictionaries route the out-of-band `null` key around the hasher so this never collides with the empty-slot sentinel. `Hash(null)` throws `ArgumentNullException` (parameter `"key"`), matching the other string hashers. Prefer it when you want a simple, familiar cheap hash on short ASCII identifiers; step up to `StringJenkinsOaatHasher` (still cheap, but with proper shift/xor diffusion) or the FNV-1a variants when the ELF hash's weak avalanche clusters keys, and escalate to the throughput-oriented strong family for clustered or adversarial keys. Incremental progress on issue #24.
- `StringElfHasherTests` — mirrors `StringSdbmHasherTests` for the ELF path: the empty-string seed-constant anchor (`Hash("") == 0`); a twelve-case spec-equivalence theory asserting the hasher equals the canonical System V ABI `elf_hash` over `Encoding.Unicode.GetBytes(...)` (an independent reference that loops over the BCL UTF-16 byte encoding with the literal shift/fold/clear steps, sharing no code with the hasher's char-loop) across ASCII / mixed / CJK / embedded-NUL / surrogate-pair inputs; an independent hand-computed value anchor for a single ASCII character (`Hash("a") == 0x610`, where neither byte drives the accumulator into the top nibble so the feedback never fires) that pins the seed, the per-byte step, and the byte order to the algorithm definition; a `Hash_NeverSetsTopNibble` regression asserting every result is non-negative with a clear top nibble (a naïve shift-and-add without the fold/clear would let the accumulator go negative on long inputs); determinism across calls and across stateless struct instances; case sensitivity, single-character-change, and append-character avalanche guards; the full-character-distinction regressions shared with the other full-width string hashers (`StringFnV1AHasher` collides `"A"` / `"Ł"` and `"AB"` / `"Łł"`, `StringElfHasher` keeps them distinct); a 1000-distinct-string distinctness sweep; `Hash(null)` throwing `ArgumentNullException`; and integration tests driving `CelerityDictionary<string, …, StringElfHasher>` and `CeleritySet<string, StringElfHasher>`, including the empty-string regular key, a non-ASCII key, the out-of-band `null` key, and a regression that `'A'` / `'Ł'` are kept as distinct dictionary keys on the probe path.
- `docs/api/hashing.md` and `README.md` — a full `StringElfHasher` section (algorithm, the `0` seed and the shift-and-add with top-nibble fold-back / clear step, where it sits at the cheapest classic end of the `string` ladder as a peer to `StringDjb2Hasher`, `StringSdbmHasher`, the FNV-1a variants, and `StringJenkinsOaatHasher`, the slightly-better-diffusion-but-still-weak-avalanche tradeoff, the 28-bit non-negative result, the ELF-over-UTF-16 equivalence and the `0` empty-string note) added immediately after the `StringSdbmHasher` entry, the `StringDjb2Hasher` / `StringSdbmHasher` escalation-ladder lines cross-referenced to name the ELF hash as their peer, the choosing-a-hasher table's `string` row extended to list it next to djb2 and sdbm, and the README `string` hasher-picking bullet extended with the ELF step. The `Celerity.AotSmokeTest` hasher spread now also constructs a `CelerityDictionary<string, int, StringElfHasher>` so the Native AOT publish job compiles the new generic instantiation.
- `StringFnV1Hasher` in `Celerity.Hashing` — the original **FNV-1** 32-bit hash provider (multiply-then-XOR) for `string` keys, over the full little-endian UTF-16 byte stream (both bytes of every character). Struct hasher, `[MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]`. It is the FNV-1 counterpart to `StringFnV1AFullHasher`: FNV-1 and FNV-1a share the same constants (offset basis `2166136261`, prime `16777619`) and differ only in the per-byte step order — FNV-1 multiplies first then XORs the byte (`hash = hash * prime; hash ^= b`), where FNV-1a XORs first then multiplies. That ordering is the whole story behind the family: in FNV-1 the last byte folded is only XORed in with no following multiply to diffuse it, so a change in the trailing byte avalanches less thoroughly than in FNV-1a, whose final operation is always a multiply — which is exactly why FNV-1a became the generally preferred default. `StringFnV1Hasher` is provided for users who specifically need the original FNV-1 ordering (e.g. to match an external system that hashes with FNV-1). Like the other full-width string hashers it folds the full 16-bit value of every character (low byte then high byte), so unlike the low-byte `StringFnV1AHasher` it distinguishes characters that differ only in their upper byte (e.g. `'A'` `U+0041` vs `'Ł'` `U+0141`). `StringFnV1Hasher.Hash(s)` equals plain FNV-1 over `Encoding.Unicode.GetBytes(s)`; the empty string maps to the offset basis (`2166136261` unsigned, `-2128831035` signed), exactly as `StringFnV1AFullHasher` maps the empty string, and the dictionaries route the out-of-band `null` key around the hasher so this never collides with the empty-slot sentinel. `Hash(null)` throws `ArgumentNullException` (parameter `"key"`), matching the other string hashers. It sits at the cheap, classic end of the `string` escalation ladder as a peer of the FNV-1a variants; prefer `StringFnV1AFullHasher` for general use and escalate to the throughput-oriented strong family for clustered or adversarial keys. Incremental progress on issue #24.
- `StringFnV1HasherTests` — mirrors `StringFnV1AFullHasherTests` for the FNV-1 path: the empty-string offset-basis anchor; a twelve-case spec-equivalence theory asserting the hasher equals plain FNV-1 (multiply-then-XOR) over `Encoding.Unicode.GetBytes(...)` across ASCII / mixed / CJK / embedded-NUL / surrogate-pair inputs (an independent reference that pins byte order, the per-character fold, and the FNV-1 step order without sharing the hasher's char-loop); an independent algebraic pin for single ASCII characters derived from the FNV-1 definition (`((offsetBasis * prime) ^ c) * prime`, which deliberately would *not* hold for FNV-1a's ordering); a guard that FNV-1 and FNV-1a produce different results for typical inputs (so the two are genuinely distinct algorithms, not an accidental alias); determinism across calls and across stateless struct instances; case sensitivity, single-character-change, and append-character avalanche guards; the full-character-distinction regressions shared with the other full-width string hashers (`StringFnV1AHasher` collides `"A"` / `"Ł"` and `"AB"` / `"Łł"`, `StringFnV1Hasher` keeps them distinct); a 1000-distinct-string distinctness sweep; `Hash(null)` throwing `ArgumentNullException`; and integration tests driving `CelerityDictionary<string, …, StringFnV1Hasher>` and `CeleritySet<string, StringFnV1Hasher>`, including the empty-string regular key, a non-ASCII key, the out-of-band `null` key, and a regression that `'A'` / `'Ł'` are kept as distinct dictionary keys on the probe path.
- `docs/api/hashing.md` and `README.md` — a full `StringFnV1Hasher` section (algorithm, the multiply-then-XOR ordering and how it differs from FNV-1a, the trailing-byte avalanche tradeoff and the resulting "prefer FNV-1a" recommendation, the FNV-1-over-UTF-16 equivalence and the offset-basis empty-string note) added immediately before the `StringFnV1AHasher` entry, the choosing-a-hasher table's `string` row extended to list it as the FNV-1-compatibility option, and the README `string` hasher-picking bullet extended with the FNV-1 step. The `Celerity.AotSmokeTest` hasher spread now also constructs a `CelerityDictionary<string, int, StringFnV1Hasher>` so the Native AOT publish job compiles the new generic instantiation.
- `StringSdbmHasher` in `Celerity.Hashing` — the classic **sdbm** hash provider for `string` keys (from Ozan Yigit's public-domain re-implementation of the `sdbm` database library, also used in gawk and Berkeley DB), over the full little-endian UTF-16 byte stream (both bytes of every character). Struct hasher, `[MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]`. It is a peer of `StringDjb2Hasher` at the cheapest classic end of the ladder: the accumulator is seeded with `0` and each byte is folded with the single step `hash = b + (hash << 6) + (hash << 16) - hash`, which is exactly `hash = hash * 65599 + b` (because `64 + 65536 - 1 = 65599`) — so the multiply by the prime `65599` lowers to two shifts and a subtract, with no real multiply, no table, and no finalizer. Where djb2 mixes with one shift and two adds (`* 33`), sdbm mixes with two shifts, an add, and a subtract (`* 65599`); the larger multiplier spreads each folded byte across more of the accumulator, which tends to give sdbm slightly better distribution on short keys, though both share the same weak avalanche (no shift/xor diffusion or finalizer, so a single changed byte propagates less thoroughly than under `StringJenkinsOaatHasher`). Like the other full-width string hashers it folds both bytes of every 16-bit code unit (low byte then high byte), exactly sdbm over the string's native little-endian UTF-16 byte stream, so it distinguishes characters that differ only in their upper byte (e.g. `'A'` `U+0041` vs `'Ł'` `U+0141`, which `StringFnV1AHasher` collides on). It sits at the cheapest, classic end of the `string` escalation ladder, a peer to `StringDjb2Hasher`, the FNV-1a variants, and `StringJenkinsOaatHasher`: `StringDjb2Hasher` / `StringSdbmHasher` (cheapest, shift-and-add classics, weaker avalanche) / `StringFnV1AHasher` (low-byte only) → `StringFnV1AFullHasher` / `StringFnV1A64Hasher` (cheap FNV-1a, full Unicode width) → `StringJenkinsOaatHasher` (cheap, full Unicode width, multiply-free, stronger per-bit avalanche) → the throughput-oriented strong family. `StringSdbmHasher.Hash(s)` equals plain sdbm over `Encoding.Unicode.GetBytes(s)`; the empty string maps to the seed constant `0` (no characters are folded), and the dictionaries route the out-of-band `null` key around the hasher so this never collides with the empty-slot sentinel. `Hash(null)` throws `ArgumentNullException` (parameter `"key"`), matching the other string hashers. Prefer it when you want a simple, familiar cheap hash on short ASCII identifiers; step up to `StringJenkinsOaatHasher` (still cheap, but with proper shift/xor diffusion) or the FNV-1a variants when sdbm's weak avalanche clusters keys, and escalate to the throughput-oriented strong family for clustered or adversarial keys. Incremental progress on issue #24.
- `StringSdbmHasherTests` — mirrors `StringDjb2HasherTests` for the sdbm path: the empty-string seed-constant anchor (`Hash("") == 0`); a twelve-case spec-equivalence theory asserting the hasher equals plain sdbm over `Encoding.Unicode.GetBytes(...)` (an independent reference that loops over the BCL UTF-16 byte encoding with the literal `* 65599` step, sharing no code with the hasher's char-loop) across ASCII / mixed / CJK / embedded-NUL / surrogate-pair inputs; an independent hand-computed value anchor for a single ASCII character (`(0 * 65599 + 0x61) * 65599 + 0x00`) that pins the seed, the per-byte step, and the byte order to the algorithm definition; determinism across calls and across stateless struct instances; case sensitivity, single-character-change, and append-character avalanche guards; the full-character-distinction regressions shared with the other full-width string hashers (`StringFnV1AHasher` collides `"A"` / `"Ł"` and `"AB"` / `"Łł"`, `StringSdbmHasher` keeps them distinct); a 1000-distinct-string distinctness sweep; `Hash(null)` throwing `ArgumentNullException`; and integration tests driving `CelerityDictionary<string, …, StringSdbmHasher>` and `CeleritySet<string, StringSdbmHasher>`, including the empty-string regular key, a non-ASCII key, the out-of-band `null` key, and a regression that `'A'` / `'Ł'` are kept as distinct dictionary keys on the probe path.
- `docs/api/hashing.md` and `README.md` — a full `StringSdbmHasher` section (algorithm, the `0` seed and the `b + (hash << 6) + (hash << 16) - hash` / `* 65599` step, where it sits at the cheapest classic end of the `string` ladder as a peer to `StringDjb2Hasher`, the FNV-1a variants, and `StringJenkinsOaatHasher`, the weaker-avalanche tradeoff shared with djb2, the sdbm-over-UTF-16 equivalence and the `0` empty-string note) added immediately after the `StringDjb2Hasher` entry, the `StringDjb2Hasher` section's escalation-ladder line cross-referenced to name sdbm as its peer, the choosing-a-hasher table's `string` row extended to list it next to djb2, and the README `string` hasher-picking bullet extended with the sdbm step. The `Celerity.AotSmokeTest` hasher spread now also constructs a `CelerityDictionary<string, int, StringSdbmHasher>` so the Native AOT publish job compiles the new generic instantiation.
- `StringDjb2Hasher` in `Celerity.Hashing` — Daniel J. Bernstein's classic **djb2** hash provider for `string` keys, over the full little-endian UTF-16 byte stream (both bytes of every character). Struct hasher, `[MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]`. It is the simplest and cheapest of the classic string hashes: the accumulator is seeded with the magic constant `5381` and each byte is folded with the single step `hash = hash * 33 + b`, where `* 33` lowers to a shift-and-add (`(hash << 5) + hash`) — so the function uses no real multiply, no table, and no finalizer, strictly cheaper than even FNV-1a's per-byte prime multiply. Like the other full-width string hashers it folds both bytes of every 16-bit code unit (low byte then high byte), exactly djb2 over the string's native little-endian UTF-16 byte stream, so it distinguishes characters that differ only in their upper byte (e.g. `'A'` `U+0041` vs `'Ł'` `U+0141`, which `StringFnV1AHasher` collides on). Its tradeoff is weaker avalanche — djb2 has no shift/xor diffusion step, so a single changed input byte propagates less thoroughly than under `StringJenkinsOaatHasher` — but it is famous, fast, and distributes well on the short ASCII identifiers that dominate many real key sets. It sits at the cheapest, classic end of the `string` escalation ladder, a peer to the FNV-1a variants and `StringJenkinsOaatHasher`: `StringDjb2Hasher` (cheapest, shift-and-add, classic, weaker avalanche) / `StringFnV1AHasher` (low-byte only) → `StringFnV1AFullHasher` / `StringFnV1A64Hasher` (cheap FNV-1a, full Unicode width) → `StringJenkinsOaatHasher` (cheap, full Unicode width, multiply-free, stronger per-bit avalanche) → the throughput-oriented strong family. `StringDjb2Hasher.Hash(s)` equals plain djb2 over `Encoding.Unicode.GetBytes(s)`; the empty string maps to the seed constant `5381` (no characters are folded), exactly as FNV-1a maps the empty string to its offset basis, and the dictionaries route the out-of-band `null` key around the hasher so this never collides with the empty-slot sentinel. `Hash(null)` throws `ArgumentNullException` (parameter `"key"`), matching the other string hashers. Prefer it when you want the simplest, most familiar cheap hash on short ASCII identifiers; step up to `StringJenkinsOaatHasher` (still cheap, but with proper shift/xor diffusion) or the FNV-1a variants when djb2's weak avalanche clusters keys, and escalate to the throughput-oriented strong family for clustered or adversarial keys. Incremental progress on issue #24.
- `StringDjb2HasherTests` — mirrors `StringJenkinsOaatHasherTests` for the djb2 path: the empty-string seed-constant anchor (`Hash("") == 5381`); a twelve-case spec-equivalence theory asserting the hasher equals plain djb2 over `Encoding.Unicode.GetBytes(...)` (an independent reference that loops over the BCL UTF-16 byte encoding with the literal `* 33` step, sharing no code with the hasher's char-loop) across ASCII / mixed / CJK / embedded-NUL / surrogate-pair inputs; an independent hand-computed value anchor for a single ASCII character (`(5381 * 33 + 0x61) * 33 + 0x00`) that pins the seed, the per-byte step, and the byte order to the algorithm definition; determinism across calls and across stateless struct instances; case sensitivity, single-character-change, and append-character avalanche guards; the full-character-distinction regressions shared with the other full-width string hashers (`StringFnV1AHasher` collides `"A"` / `"Ł"` and `"AB"` / `"Łł"`, `StringDjb2Hasher` keeps them distinct); a 1000-distinct-string distinctness sweep; `Hash(null)` throwing `ArgumentNullException`; and integration tests driving `CelerityDictionary<string, …, StringDjb2Hasher>` and `CeleritySet<string, StringDjb2Hasher>`, including the empty-string regular key, a non-ASCII key, the out-of-band `null` key, and a regression that `'A'` / `'Ł'` are kept as distinct dictionary keys on the probe path.
- `docs/api/hashing.md` and `README.md` — a full `StringDjb2Hasher` section (algorithm, the `5381` seed and the shift-and-add `* 33` step, where it sits at the cheapest classic end of the `string` ladder as a peer to the FNV-1a variants and `StringJenkinsOaatHasher`, the weaker-avalanche tradeoff, the djb2-over-UTF-16 equivalence and the `5381` empty-string note) added immediately before the `StringFnV1AHasher` entry, the choosing-a-hasher table's `string` row extended to list it as the simplest/cheapest classic option, and the README `string` hasher-picking bullet extended with the djb2 step. The `Celerity.AotSmokeTest` hasher spread now also constructs a `CelerityDictionary<string, int, StringDjb2Hasher>` so the Native AOT publish job compiles the new generic instantiation.
- `UInt64WangNaiveHasher` in `Celerity.Hashing` — an extremely cheap XOR-fold hash provider for `ulong` keys, the `ulong` counterpart to `Int64WangNaiveHasher`. Struct hasher, `[MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]`. It fills the cheap-default tier of the `ulong` escalation ladder, which until now jumped straight from `UInt64WangHasher` (the full Thomas-Wang `hash64shift` finalizer) to `UInt64Hasher` (the Murmur3 `fmix64` finalizer) with no cheap XOR-fold option — even though `int` (`Int32WangNaiveHasher`), `long` (`Int64WangNaiveHasher`), and `uint` (`UInt32Hasher`) all ship one. The formula is `(int)key ^ (int)(key >> 32) ^ (int)(key >> 16)`: two ops vs the seven-step shift-add Wang mixer and the two-multiply `fmix64`. The extra middle-16-bits fold over a naive `key.GetHashCode()` keeps a chunk of the high-half entropy in the result, which materially improves distribution on keys whose low 32 bits are sequential (e.g. monotonically allocated IDs whose upper bits carry type / shard). Because the fold runs over the raw bits, `UInt64WangNaiveHasher.Hash(u)` returns exactly `Int64WangNaiveHasher.Hash((long)u)` for any matching 64-bit pattern. The XOR-fold maps `0 → 0`; the dictionaries route the out-of-band zero key around the hasher so this never collides with the empty-slot sentinel. Prefer it over `UInt64Hasher` / `UInt64WangHasher` when the key distribution is already reasonably uniform and latency matters more than collision resistance; escalate to `UInt64WangHasher` (full Wang finalizer) or `UInt64Hasher` (`fmix64`) for adversarial or heavily clustered keys. `UInt64WangHasher`'s XML remarks now cross-reference it as the cheaper drop-down tier. Incremental progress on issue #24.
- `UInt64WangNaiveHasherTests` — mirrors `Int64WangNaiveHasherTests` / `UInt64WangHasherTests` for `ulong` keys: a nine-case formula theory (the short XOR-fold acts as its own spec, so expected values are computed inline rather than hard-coded) across `0` / `1` / `42` / `ulong.MaxValue` / `long.MaxValue` & `long.MinValue` bit patterns / `1234567890123456789UL` / a low-48-bits-set key / `0xDEADBEEFCAFEBABEUL`, an eight-case theory asserting bit-for-bit equivalence with `Int64WangNaiveHasher` over the same 64-bit patterns, an explicit `Hash(0UL) == 0` guard documenting the fixed point, determinism across calls and across stateless struct instances, high-bit and mid-bit influence regression guards (pinning the `>> 32` and `>> 16` folds), a 1000-consecutive-input distinctness sweep, a single-high-bit-strided distinctness sweep over bits 32-63 (a hasher that ignored the upper half would map them all to `0`), a no-throw sweep over the key extremes, integration tests driving `CelerityDictionary<ulong, …, UInt64WangNaiveHasher>` and `CeleritySet<ulong, UInt64WangNaiveHasher>` (including the out-of-band zero key / element and `ulong.MaxValue` beyond `long.MaxValue`), and a same-lower-32-bits / different-upper-32-bits regression that guards the probe path against accidental int-truncation.
- `docs/api/hashing.md` and `README.md` — a full `UInt64WangNaiveHasher` section (algorithm, where it sits on the cost-vs-avalanche curve below `UInt64WangHasher` and `UInt64Hasher`, the bit-pattern equivalence with `Int64WangNaiveHasher`, the `0 → 0` note) added immediately after the existing `UInt64WangHasher` entry, the choosing-a-hasher table's `ulong` row extended to list `UInt64WangNaiveHasher` as the cheapest XOR-fold option on already-uniform keys, and the README `ulong` hasher-picking bullet extended with the same drop-down step. The `Celerity.AotSmokeTest` hasher spread now also constructs a `CelerityDictionary<ulong, int, UInt64WangNaiveHasher>` so the Native AOT publish job compiles the new generic instantiation.
- `StringFnV1AFullHasher` in `Celerity.Hashing` — a full-character-width FNV-1a 32-bit hash provider for `string` keys, the full-UTF-16 counterpart to `StringFnV1AHasher`. Struct hasher, `[MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]`. It directly answers the long-standing note in `StringFnV1AHasher`'s own remarks — "for keys with significant non-ASCII content, a full UTF-8 or UTF-16 hash is preferable" — which until now had no in-box answer at the FNV-1a cost class: `StringFnV1AHasher` folds only the low byte of each character (`c & 0xFF`) and therefore collides characters that differ only in their upper byte (e.g. `'A'` `U+0041` and `'Ł'` `U+0141`), and the only escalation was straight to `StringMurmur3Hasher` (block reads, rotates, and the `fmix32` finalizer). The new hasher folds both bytes of every 16-bit code unit, low byte then high byte — exactly the FNV-1a of the string's native little-endian UTF-16 byte stream (`StringFnV1AFullHasher.Hash(s)` equals plain FNV-1a over `Encoding.Unicode.GetBytes(s)`) — so it keeps upper-byte-distinct characters separate while still costing only a pair of XOR / multiply steps per character. It fills the middle tier of the `string` escalation ladder: `StringFnV1AHasher` (cheapest, low-byte only) → `StringFnV1AFullHasher` (cheap, full Unicode width) → `StringMurmur3Hasher` (strongest avalanche). The empty string maps to the FNV-1a offset basis (`2166136261` unsigned, `-2128831035` signed), exactly as `StringFnV1AHasher` does; the dictionaries route the out-of-band `null` key around the hasher so this never collides with the empty-slot sentinel. `Hash(null)` throws `ArgumentNullException` (parameter `"key"`), matching the other string hashers. Prefer it over `StringFnV1AHasher` whenever keys contain non-ASCII characters the low-byte fold would collide; escalate to `StringMurmur3Hasher` when FNV-1a's weaker avalanche pushes clustered or adversarial keys into long probe chains. Incremental progress on issue #24.
- `StringFnV1AFullHasherTests` — mirrors `StringFnV1AHasherTests` / `StringMurmur3HasherTests` for the full-width FNV-1a path: the empty-string offset-basis anchor; a twelve-case spec-equivalence theory asserting the hasher equals plain FNV-1a over `Encoding.Unicode.GetBytes(...)` across ASCII / mixed / CJK / embedded-NUL / surrogate-pair inputs (an independent reference that pins byte order and the per-character fold without sharing the hasher's char-loop implementation); an independent algebraic pin for single ASCII characters (`full(c)` equals the low-byte hash times the FNV prime, derived from the FNV-1a "append zero byte = multiply by prime" identity); determinism across calls and across stateless struct instances; case sensitivity, single-character-change, and append-character avalanche guards; the headline full-character-distinction regressions (`StringFnV1AHasher` collides `"A"` / `"Ł"` and `"AB"` / `"Łł"`, `StringFnV1AFullHasher` keeps them distinct); a 1000-distinct-string distinctness sweep; `Hash(null)` throwing `ArgumentNullException`; and integration tests driving `CelerityDictionary<string, …, StringFnV1AFullHasher>` and `CeleritySet<string, StringFnV1AFullHasher>`, including the empty-string regular key, a non-ASCII key, the out-of-band `null` key, and a regression that `'A'` / `'Ł'` are kept as distinct dictionary keys on the probe path.
- `docs/api/hashing.md` and `README.md` — a full `StringFnV1AFullHasher` section (algorithm, where it sits on the `string` cost-vs-avalanche ladder between `StringFnV1AHasher` and `StringMurmur3Hasher`, the FNV-1a-over-UTF-16 byte-stream equivalence, the offset-basis empty-string note) added between the existing `StringFnV1AHasher` and `StringMurmur3Hasher` entries, the `StringFnV1AHasher` note re-pointed at it as the same-cost full-width drop-up, the choosing-a-hasher table's `string` row extended to list it as the full-width FNV option before `StringMurmur3Hasher`, and the README `string` hasher-picking bullet rewritten as a three-step ladder. The `Celerity.AotSmokeTest` hasher spread now also constructs a `CelerityDictionary<string, int, StringFnV1AFullHasher>` so the Native AOT publish job compiles the new generic instantiation.
- `StringFnV1A64Hasher` in `Celerity.Hashing` — a full-character-width FNV-1a **64-bit** hash provider for `string` keys, the wide-accumulator counterpart to `StringFnV1AFullHasher`. Struct hasher, `[MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]`. It folds the same little-endian UTF-16 byte stream as `StringFnV1AFullHasher` (low byte then high byte of every 16-bit code unit) but accumulates into a 64-bit state using the FNV-1a 64-bit parameters (offset basis `14695981039346656037`, prime `1099511628211`), then xor-folds the result to a signed 32-bit value with the standard FNV retraction `h ^ (h >> 32)`. Carrying twice as many bits through the accumulation means intermediate values collide far less often, so for longer keys and larger key sets the distribution holds up better than the 32-bit FNV-1a hashers before the final fold, while still costing only a pair of XOR / multiply steps per character — and each multiply is 64-bit, which on 64-bit platforms is the same throughput as a 32-bit multiply, so the wider state is effectively free there. It extends the `string` escalation ladder with a fourth rung: `StringFnV1AHasher` (cheapest, low-byte only) → `StringFnV1AFullHasher` (cheap, full Unicode width, 32-bit state) → `StringFnV1A64Hasher` (full Unicode width, 64-bit state) → `StringMurmur3Hasher` (strongest avalanche). `StringFnV1A64Hasher.Hash(s)` equals plain FNV-1a-64 over `Encoding.Unicode.GetBytes(s)` xor-folded to 32 bits; the empty string maps to the 64-bit offset basis folded to 32 bits, and the dictionaries route the out-of-band `null` key around the hasher so this never collides with the empty-slot sentinel. `Hash(null)` throws `ArgumentNullException` (parameter `"key"`), matching the other string hashers. `StringFnV1AFullHasher`'s XML remarks now cross-reference it as the wider-state step-up. Prefer it over `StringFnV1AFullHasher` when keys are long or numerous enough that the 32-bit accumulator starts clustering; escalate to `StringMurmur3Hasher` when FNV-1a's weaker per-bit avalanche pushes clustered or adversarial keys into long probe chains regardless of state width. Incremental progress on issue #24.
- `StringFnV1A64HasherTests` — mirrors `StringFnV1AFullHasherTests` for the 64-bit path: the empty-string folded-offset-basis anchor (expressed symbolically so it pins the fold direction without a hand-computed constant); a twelve-case spec-equivalence theory asserting the hasher equals plain FNV-1a-64 over `Encoding.Unicode.GetBytes(...)` xor-folded to 32 bits across ASCII / mixed / CJK / embedded-NUL / surrogate-pair inputs (an independent reference that pins byte order, the per-character fold, and the final fold without sharing the hasher's char-loop); an independent algebraic pin for single ASCII characters (re-deriving the pre-fold 64-bit accumulator from the FNV-1a "append zero byte = multiply by prime" identity and then folding); determinism across calls and across stateless struct instances; case sensitivity, single-character-change, and append-character avalanche guards; the full-character-distinction regressions shared with `StringFnV1AFullHasher` (`StringFnV1AHasher` collides `"A"` / `"Ł"` and `"AB"` / `"Łł"`, `StringFnV1A64Hasher` keeps them distinct); a 1000-distinct-string distinctness sweep; `Hash(null)` throwing `ArgumentNullException`; and integration tests driving `CelerityDictionary<string, …, StringFnV1A64Hasher>` and `CeleritySet<string, StringFnV1A64Hasher>`, including the empty-string regular key, a non-ASCII key, the out-of-band `null` key, and a regression that `'A'` / `'Ł'` are kept as distinct dictionary keys on the probe path.
- `docs/api/hashing.md` and `README.md` — a full `StringFnV1A64Hasher` section (algorithm, the 64-bit accumulator and xor-fold, where it sits on the `string` ladder above `StringFnV1AFullHasher` and below `StringMurmur3Hasher`, the FNV-1a-64-over-UTF-16 equivalence, the folded-offset-basis empty-string note) added after the `StringFnV1AFullHasher` entry, the `StringFnV1AFullHasher` section's ladder line extended to four rungs and re-pointed at it as the wider-state step-up, the choosing-a-hasher table's `string` row extended to list it, and the README `string` hasher-picking bullet extended with the 64-bit step. The `Celerity.AotSmokeTest` hasher spread now also constructs a `CelerityDictionary<string, int, StringFnV1A64Hasher>` so the Native AOT publish job compiles the new generic instantiation.
- `StringXxHash32Hasher` in `Celerity.Hashing` — a throughput-oriented strong-distribution hash provider for `string` keys using the xxHash32 (XXH32) algorithm, seed `0`, over the string's native little-endian UTF-16 byte stream. Struct hasher, `[MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]`. This is the first member of the XXHash family called for in issue #24, and the throughput-oriented sibling of `StringMurmur3Hasher` at the strong-avalanche top of the `string` ladder: `StringFnV1AHasher` (cheapest, low-byte only) → `StringFnV1AFullHasher` (cheap, full Unicode width, 32-bit state) → `StringFnV1A64Hasher` (full Unicode width, 64-bit state) → `StringMurmur3Hasher` / `StringXxHash32Hasher` (strong avalanche). xxHash processes the input in 16-byte stripes (eight UTF-16 code units) across **four** independent accumulators advanced by `acc = rotl(acc + lane * PRIME32_2, 13) * PRIME32_1`, merges them via `rotl(v1,1) + rotl(v2,7) + rotl(v3,12) + rotl(v4,18)`, mixes in the byte length and any remaining 4-byte lanes / trailing 2-byte char, and finishes with the XXH32 avalanche so every input bit reaches every output bit. Keeping four accumulators in flight (vs MurmurHash3's single accumulator over one 32-bit block at a time) is what lets it pull ahead on throughput as keys get longer; for very short keys MurmurHash3's simpler loop has less fixed overhead. Like the other full-width string hashers it consumes the full 16-bit value of every character, so it distinguishes characters that differ only in their upper byte (e.g. `'A'` `U+0041` vs `'Ł'` `U+0141`, which `StringFnV1AHasher` collides on). `StringXxHash32Hasher.Hash(s)` equals canonical XXH32 (seed `0`) over `Encoding.Unicode.GetBytes(s)`; the empty string maps to the well-known canonical empty-input vector `0x02CC5D05` (its UTF-16 byte stream is zero bytes), and the dictionaries route the out-of-band `null` key around the hasher so this never collides with the empty-slot sentinel. `Hash(null)` throws `ArgumentNullException` (parameter `"key"`), matching the other string hashers. `StringMurmur3Hasher`'s neighbouring docs now cross-reference it as the throughput-oriented peer. Prefer it over `StringMurmur3Hasher` when keys are long enough that the four-accumulator stripe loop wins; prefer `StringMurmur3Hasher` for very short keys. Incremental progress on issue #24.
- `StringXxHash32HasherTests` — mirrors `StringFnV1A64HasherTests` for the XXH32 path: an external canonical anchor asserting `Hash("")` equals the published empty-input vector `0x02CC5D05` (and a companion test pinning the test's own byte-oriented reference against the same constant); a sixteen-case spec-equivalence theory asserting the hasher equals a canonical, independently-written byte-oriented XXH32 over `Encoding.Unicode.GetBytes(...)` (using `BinaryPrimitives.ReadUInt32LittleEndian`, so it shares no code with the hasher's char-loop and pins the stripe / lane boundaries, tail handling, byte order, and finalizer) across ASCII / mixed / CJK / embedded-NUL / surrogate-pair inputs and lengths that exercise the short path, exactly-one-lane, multi-lane, and the 16-byte four-accumulator stripe loop; determinism across calls and across stateless struct instances; case sensitivity, single-character-change, and append-character avalanche guards; the full-character-distinction regressions shared with the other full-width string hashers (`StringFnV1AHasher` collides `"A"` / `"Ł"` and `"AB"` / `"Łł"`, `StringXxHash32Hasher` keeps them distinct); a 1000-distinct-string distinctness sweep; `Hash(null)` throwing `ArgumentNullException`; and integration tests driving `CelerityDictionary<string, …, StringXxHash32Hasher>` and `CeleritySet<string, StringXxHash32Hasher>`, including the empty-string regular key, a non-ASCII key, the out-of-band `null` key, and a regression that `'A'` / `'Ł'` are kept as distinct dictionary keys on the probe path.
- `docs/api/hashing.md` and `README.md` — a full `StringXxHash32Hasher` section (algorithm, the four-accumulator stripe loop and avalanche, where it sits alongside `StringMurmur3Hasher` at the strong-avalanche top of the `string` ladder, the throughput-vs-fixed-overhead tradeoff between the two, the canonical-XXH32-over-UTF-16 equivalence and the `0x02CC5D05` empty-string vector) added after the `StringMurmur3Hasher` entry, the `StringFnV1AFullHasher` / `StringFnV1A64Hasher` ladder lines updated so the strong tier consistently reads `StringMurmur3Hasher` / `StringXxHash32Hasher`, the choosing-a-hasher table's `string` row extended to list it, and the README `string` hasher-picking bullet extended to present the two strong options (`StringMurmur3Hasher` for short keys, `StringXxHash32Hasher` for longer ones). The `Celerity.AotSmokeTest` hasher spread now also constructs a `CelerityDictionary<string, int, StringXxHash32Hasher>` so the Native AOT publish job compiles the new generic instantiation.
- `StringXxHash64Hasher` in `Celerity.Hashing` — a throughput-oriented strong-distribution hash provider for `string` keys using the xxHash64 (XXH64) algorithm, seed `0`, over the string's native little-endian UTF-16 byte stream, xor-folded down to a signed 32-bit result. Struct hasher, `[MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]`. It is the wide-accumulator counterpart to `StringXxHash32Hasher` (mirroring how `StringFnV1A64Hasher` widens `StringFnV1AFullHasher`) and the second member of the XXHash family called for in issue #24. Where XXH32 advances four 32-bit accumulators over 16-byte stripes, XXH64 advances four **64-bit** accumulators (`acc = rotl(acc + lane * PRIME64_2, 31) * PRIME64_1`) over **32-byte** stripes (sixteen UTF-16 code units), merges them via `rotl(v1,1) + rotl(v2,7) + rotl(v3,12) + rotl(v4,18)` followed by four merge rounds, mixes in the byte length, any remaining 8-byte / 4-byte lanes, and the trailing 2-byte char, finishes with the XXH64 avalanche (`>> 33` / `* PRIME64_2` / `>> 29` / `* PRIME64_3` / `>> 32`), and reduces the 64-bit result to 32 bits with the standard xor-fold `h ^ (h >> 32)`. Carrying twice as many bits through the accumulation keeps the distribution holding up even better than XXH32 before the fold, and on 64-bit platforms each 64-bit multiply is the same throughput as a 32-bit one while the wider stripe consumes input twice as fast — so the wider state is effectively free there and pulls ahead on longer keys. It extends the strong-avalanche top of the `string` ladder to three peers: `StringFnV1AHasher` (cheapest, low-byte only) → `StringFnV1AFullHasher` (cheap, full Unicode width, 32-bit state) → `StringFnV1A64Hasher` (full Unicode width, 64-bit state) → `StringMurmur3Hasher` / `StringXxHash32Hasher` / `StringXxHash64Hasher` (strong avalanche). Like the other full-width string hashers it consumes the full 16-bit value of every character, so it distinguishes characters that differ only in their upper byte (e.g. `'A'` `U+0041` vs `'Ł'` `U+0141`, which `StringFnV1AHasher` collides on). `StringXxHash64Hasher.Hash(s)` equals canonical XXH64 (seed `0`) over `Encoding.Unicode.GetBytes(s)` xor-folded to 32 bits; the empty string maps to the well-known canonical empty-input vector `0xEF46DB3751D8E999` folded to 32 bits (its UTF-16 byte stream is zero bytes), and the dictionaries route the out-of-band `null` key around the hasher so this never collides with the empty-slot sentinel. `Hash(null)` throws `ArgumentNullException` (parameter `"key"`), matching the other string hashers. `StringXxHash32Hasher`'s neighbouring docs now cross-reference it as the wider-state step-up. Prefer it over `StringXxHash32Hasher` when keys are long enough that the wider accumulator and 32-byte stripe pull ahead on a 64-bit platform; prefer `StringXxHash32Hasher` / `StringMurmur3Hasher` for shorter keys. Incremental progress on issue #24.
- `StringXxHash64HasherTests` — mirrors `StringXxHash32HasherTests` for the XXH64 path: an external canonical anchor asserting `Hash("")` equals the published empty-input vector `0xEF46DB3751D8E999` xor-folded to 32 bits (expressed symbolically so it pins the fold direction without a hand-computed constant, plus a companion test pinning the test's own byte-oriented reference's raw 64-bit result against `0xEF46DB3751D8E999`); a seventeen-case spec-equivalence theory asserting the hasher equals a canonical, independently-written byte-oriented XXH64 over `Encoding.Unicode.GetBytes(...)` folded to 32 bits (using `BinaryPrimitives.ReadUInt64LittleEndian` / `ReadUInt32LittleEndian`, so it shares no code with the hasher's char-loop and pins the 32-byte stripe / 8-byte and 4-byte lane boundaries, the merge rounds, tail handling, byte order, the avalanche, and the final fold) across ASCII / mixed / CJK / embedded-NUL / surrogate-pair inputs and lengths that exercise the short path, exactly-one 8-byte lane, an 8-byte + 4-byte lane, and the 32-byte four-accumulator stripe loop; determinism across calls and across stateless struct instances; case sensitivity, single-character-change, and append-character avalanche guards; the full-character-distinction regressions shared with the other full-width string hashers (`StringFnV1AHasher` collides `"A"` / `"Ł"` and `"AB"` / `"Łł"`, `StringXxHash64Hasher` keeps them distinct); a 1000-distinct-string distinctness sweep; `Hash(null)` throwing `ArgumentNullException`; and integration tests driving `CelerityDictionary<string, …, StringXxHash64Hasher>` and `CeleritySet<string, StringXxHash64Hasher>`, including the empty-string regular key, a non-ASCII key, the out-of-band `null` key, and a regression that `'A'` / `'Ł'` are kept as distinct dictionary keys on the probe path.
- `docs/api/hashing.md` and `README.md` — a full `StringXxHash64Hasher` section (algorithm, the four 64-bit accumulators over 32-byte stripes, the merge rounds and avalanche, the xor-fold to 32 bits, where it sits alongside `StringMurmur3Hasher` / `StringXxHash32Hasher` at the strong-avalanche top of the `string` ladder, the wider-state-is-free-on-64-bit tradeoff, the canonical-XXH64-over-UTF-16-folded equivalence and the `0xEF46DB3751D8E999` empty-string vector) added after the `StringXxHash32Hasher` entry, the `StringFnV1AFullHasher` / `StringFnV1A64Hasher` / `StringXxHash32Hasher` ladder lines updated so the strong tier consistently reads `StringMurmur3Hasher` / `StringXxHash32Hasher` / `StringXxHash64Hasher`, the choosing-a-hasher table's `string` row extended to list it, and the README `string` hasher-picking bullet extended with the XXH64 step. The `Celerity.AotSmokeTest` hasher spread now also constructs a `CelerityDictionary<string, int, StringXxHash64Hasher>` so the Native AOT publish job compiles the new generic instantiation.
- `StringMetroHash64Hasher` in `Celerity.Hashing` — a throughput-oriented strong-distribution hash provider for `string` keys using the MetroHash64 algorithm (J. Andrew Rogers' `metrohash64_1` variant), seed `0`, over the string's native little-endian UTF-16 byte stream, xor-folded down to a signed 32-bit result. Struct hasher, `[MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]`. It joins `StringMurmur3Hasher` / `StringXxHash32Hasher` / `StringXxHash64Hasher` at the throughput-oriented strong tier called for in issue #24. MetroHash is a family of statistically robust hashes designed for maximum throughput on modern 64-bit CPUs: like XXH64 it advances four independent **64-bit** accumulators over **32-byte stripes** (sixteen UTF-16 code units) — `v += lane * kN; v = rotr(v, 29) + vNext` — then runs a post-loop lattice of `rotr(…, 33)` mixes, consumes the tail as a 16-byte block (two lanes through `rotr 33` / `rotr 35`), an 8-byte lane (`rotr 33`), a 4-byte block (`rotr 15`), and a trailing 2-byte char (`rotr 13`), finishes with `rotr 33` / `* k0` / `rotr 33`, and reduces the 64-bit result to 32 bits with the standard xor-fold `h ^ (h >> 32)`. Its lattice gives the out-of-order core four independent multiply chains to keep in flight, so on mid-length keys it is competitive with — and often beats — the xxHash family; `StringMetroHash64Hasher`, `StringXxHash64Hasher`, and `StringXxHash32Hasher` are peers at the throughput-oriented top of the ladder, to be chosen by profiling on the actual key shape. Like the other full-width string hashers it consumes the full 16-bit value of every character, so it distinguishes characters that differ only in their upper byte (e.g. `'A'` `U+0041` vs `'Ł'` `U+0141`, which `StringFnV1AHasher` collides on). `StringMetroHash64Hasher.Hash(s)` equals canonical MetroHash64 (`metrohash64_1`, seed `0`) over `Encoding.Unicode.GetBytes(s)` xor-folded to 32 bits; the empty string maps to the algorithm's length-`0` result `finalize(k2 * k0)` folded to 32 bits (its UTF-16 byte stream is zero bytes), and the dictionaries route the out-of-band `null` key around the hasher so this never collides with the empty-slot sentinel. `Hash(null)` throws `ArgumentNullException` (parameter `"key"`), matching the other string hashers. The mixing constants are the public-domain `metrohash64_1` values (`k0 = 0xC83A91E1`, `k1 = 0x8648DBDB`, `k2 = 0x7BDEC03B`, `k3 = 0x2F5870A5`). `StringXxHash64Hasher`'s neighbouring docs now cross-reference it as a same-class 64-bit peer. Prefer it (or the xxHash family) over `StringMurmur3Hasher` when keys are long enough that the four-accumulator stripe loop wins on throughput; prefer `StringMurmur3Hasher` for very short keys. Incremental progress on issue #24.
- `StringMetroHash64HasherTests` — mirrors `StringXxHash64HasherTests` for the MetroHash64 path: a spec anchor asserting `Hash("")` equals the length-`0` result `finalize(k2 * k0)` folded to 32 bits (expressed symbolically from the constants so it pins the constants, the finalization, and the fold direction without a hand-computed magic number, plus a companion test pinning the test's own byte-oriented reference's raw 64-bit empty-input result against the same `finalize(k2 * k0)` expression);
