The out-of-band zero / default slot path is on a separate branch and unchanged; `_version`-based concurrent-modification detection still throws on the very first instruction of `MoveNext`. Pinned by the existing enumeration coverage — `IntDictionaryEnumerationTests`, `LongDictionaryEnumerationTests`, `CelerityDictionaryEnumerationTests`, `IntSetEnumerationTests`, `LongSetEnumerationTests`, and `CeleritySetEnumerationTests` (empty / single / many-entry enumeration, default-slot-first ordering, removal / resize / Clear survival, mutation-during-enumeration detection, no-op mutation preservation, `Reset` reuse, post-exhaustion `Current` reset, generic and non-generic `IEnumerable` parity, open-generic smoke tests, and LINQ smoke tests). All 746 tests pass locally on `net8.0`.
- `Resize()` on `IntDictionary<TValue, THasher>`, `IntSet<THasher>`, `LongDictionary<TValue, THasher>`, `LongSet<THasher>`, `CelerityDictionary<TKey, TValue, THasher>`, and `CeleritySet<T, THasher>` now reads from the old arrays and probes / writes into the new arrays via `Unsafe.Add` against `MemoryMarshal.GetArrayDataReference` instead of the indexer. This applies the same bounds-check-elimination pattern already used on `ProbeForInsert` / `ProbeForKey` / `BackwardShiftRemove` to the resize migration: every iteration's `oldKeys[i]` / `oldSlots[i]` load, the probe-for-empty-slot walk on the new arrays, and the final write all dropped their per-iteration `Buffer.GetMaximumArrayLength` / cmp-against-`Length` bounds checks. The bounds are structural — `i < oldKeys.Length` is the for-loop condition, and `index = ... & mask` keeps `index ∈ [0, newSize)` because `mask = newSize - 1` and `newSize` is a power of two — so the per-element BCE removal is provably safe. Casts use the `(nint)(uint)` pattern to give the JIT the non-negativity hint that unlocks a zero-extending load on x64. No public-API change; correctness is unchanged. Pinned by the existing resize-heavy coverage (`LoadFactorBoundaryTests`, `TryAddDuplicateResizeTests`, the `ResizeThenRemoveSweep_*_UnderFullCollision` Facts in all four `*CollisionTests` files, and the multi-resize-from-tiny-capacity Facts across all six collections) — all 746 tests pass locally on `net8.0`.

### Added

- `HashQualityEvaluator` and `HashQualityReport` in `Celerity.Hashing` — a diagnostic tool for comparing how well candidate hashers distribute a representative key sample, the long-standing "create hash function evaluator" roadmap item (1.1.0 infrastructure). `HashQualityEvaluator.Evaluate<T, THasher>(IEnumerable<T> keys, int bucketCount = 1024)` hashes every key with `default(THasher)` (the built-in hashers are stateless structs) and returns a `readonly struct HashQualityReport` of: `KeyCount`, `DistinctHashCount`, `CollisionCount` / `CollisionRate` (raw 32-bit code collisions — the hasher's intrinsic injectivity, independent of table size), `BucketCount` / `OccupiedBucketCount` / `EmptyBucketCount`, `MaxBucketLoad` (worst-case probe-chain seed), `MeanBucketLoad`, `ChiSquared` (Pearson's statistic of the bucket loads vs uniform — ≈ `BucketCount - 1` for a good hash), and `DistributionScore` (observed ÷ ideal sum of squared bucket loads; `1.0` = ideal uniform, above `1.0` = clustering, below `1.0` = better-than-random). Codes are masked into power-of-two buckets with `code & (bucketCount - 1)` exactly as the Celerity collections index their backing arrays (so `bucketCount` is rounded up to the next power of two via `FastUtils.NextPowerOfTwo`), making the bucket metrics reflect the clustering a real table of that size would experience. It is explicitly an offline tool — it allocates working buffers and walks an `IEnumerable<T>`, so it is meant for tests / benchmarks / one-off analysis, not the hot path. `Evaluate` throws `ArgumentNullException` for a null `keys` and `ArgumentOutOfRangeException` for `bucketCount < 1`; an empty sample yields a neutral report (`DistributionScore` `1.0`, `ChiSquared` `0`). The library stays Native-AOT clean — no reflection, just generics over the existing struct-hasher constraint. Closes #2.
- `HashQualityEvaluatorTests` — 21 tests pinning the evaluator: argument validation (null keys, `bucketCount` of `0` / negative), bucket-count round-up to the next power of two and the default `1024`, the neutral empty-sample and ideal single-key reports, raw-code collision accounting on a constant hasher and on a duplicate-key sample, the perfect-distribution case (identity hasher over a contiguous range — one key per bucket, `MaxBucketLoad` `1`, `ChiSquared` `0`, `DistributionScore` below the random baseline), bucket masking (distinct raw codes that collide under the bucket mask), the `OccupiedBucketCount + EmptyBucketCount == BucketCount` invariant, a good hasher (`Int32Murmur3Hasher`) scoring near the `1.0` uniform baseline with zero raw collisions, a constant hasher scoring far worse on every axis, determinism across repeated calls, the string-hasher generic path (`StringMurmur3Hasher`), and the `ToString()` summary.
- `docs/api/hashing.md` — a new "Hash quality evaluation" section documenting `HashQualityEvaluator` and the `HashQualityReport` metrics (with a per-member table and a runnable hasher-comparison example). `README.md`'s "Custom hashing" section now points at it.
- `UInt32Murmur3Hasher` in `Celerity.Hashing` — Murmur3 32-bit finalizer (`fmix32`) for `uint` keys. Struct hasher, `[MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]`. It is the `uint` counterpart to `Int32Murmur3Hasher` and the strong-avalanche escalation tier for `UInt32Hasher`, closing a real gap: the `uint` family shipped only the cheap XOR-fold `UInt32Hasher` (`key ^ (key >> 16)`), whose own remarks pointed at a "full Murmur3 finalizer for clustered or adversarial inputs" that did not exist — `int` had `Int32Murmur3Hasher`, `long` had `Int64Murmur3Hasher`, and `ulong` had `UInt64Hasher` (`fmix64`), but `uint` had no Murmur3 option. The mixer is the standard `fmix32`: `h ^= h >> 16`, `h *= 0x85ebca6b`, `h ^= h >> 13`, `h *= 0xc2b2ae35`, `h ^= h >> 16`, computed on the `uint` directly and reinterpreted as `int` (so for any 32-bit pattern it returns exactly what `Int32Murmur3Hasher` returns for the same bits). Every input bit influences every output bit, holding distribution up on clustered or adversarial keys. Like the other Murmur3 finalizers it maps `0 → 0` (the `fmix32` fixed point); the dictionaries route the out-of-band zero key around the hasher so this never collides with the empty-slot sentinel. Prefer it over the default `UInt32Hasher` when profiling shows the cheap XOR-fold is clustering. `UInt32Hasher`'s XML remarks now reference it by `<see cref>` instead of the dangling prose. Incremental progress on issue #24.
- `UInt32Murmur3HasherTests` — mirrors `Int32Murmur3HasherTests` / `Int32WangHasherTests` for `uint` keys: eight exact-value anchors (`0` / `1` / `42` / `16` / `65536` / `int.MaxValue` / `int.MinValue` / `uint.MaxValue` bit patterns) pinning the round order / shift amounts / `0x85ebca6b` / `0xc2b2ae35` constants against drift, an explicit `Hash(0) == 0` guard documenting the `fmix32` fixed point, determinism across calls and across stateless struct instances, a high-bit avalanche check, a 1000-consecutive-input collision-free sweep (exercising the bijective-on-`uint32` property), a no-throw sweep over the key extremes, and integration tests driving `CelerityDictionary<uint, …, UInt32Murmur3Hasher>` and `CeleritySet<uint, UInt32Murmur3Hasher>` — including the out-of-band zero-key / zero-element slot and keys beyond `int.MaxValue`.
- `docs/api/hashing.md` and `README.md` — a full `UInt32Murmur3Hasher` section (algorithm, where it sits relative to `UInt32Hasher`, the `0 → 0` note) added next to the existing `UInt64Hasher` entry, the choosing-a-hasher table's `uint` row updated to list `UInt32Murmur3Hasher` as the escalation option (previously `—`), and a `uint` bullet added to the README hasher-picking notes mirroring the `int` family's escalation step. The `Celerity.AotSmokeTest` hasher spread now also constructs a `CelerityDictionary<uint, int, UInt32Murmur3Hasher>` so the Native AOT publish job compiles the new generic instantiation.
- `Int32WangHasher` in `Celerity.Hashing` — Thomas Wang's 32-bit integer hash (`hash32shift`) for `int` keys, the 32-bit counterpart to `Int64WangHasher`. Struct hasher, `[MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]`. It fills the missing middle tier of the `int` escalation ladder: the `long` family already shipped `Int64WangNaiveHasher` (cheap XOR-fold default) → `Int64WangHasher` (full Thomas-Wang finalizer) → `Int64Murmur3Hasher` (strongest avalanche), but `int` jumped straight from `Int32WangNaiveHasher` to `Int32Murmur3Hasher` with no full-Wang option in between. The mixer is `~u + (u << 15)`, `^ (u >> 12)`, `+ (u << 2)`, `^ (u >> 4)`, `* 2057` (encoded as `+ (u << 3) + (u << 11)` to avoid the multiply), `^ (u >> 16)`, computed on the `uint` reinterpretation. A single shift-add-encoded multiply plus XOR-shift / shift-add rounds make it cheaper than the two-multiply `Int32Murmur3Hasher` finalizer while still mixing every input bit. It is bijective on `uint`, so it is collision-free on any contiguous key range — only key structure, not the mixer, produces collisions. Unlike the Murmur3 finalizer, it does **not** map `0 → 0` (`Hash(0) == -895235421`); the dictionaries route the out-of-band zero key around the hasher so this never collides with the empty-slot sentinel. Prefer it over the default `Int32WangNaiveHasher` when profiling shows the cheap XOR-fold is clustering; escalate to `Int32Murmur3Hasher` for adversarial keys that need maximum avalanche. Incremental progress on issue #24.
- `Int32WangHasherTests` — mirrors `Int64WangHasherTests` for 32-bit keys: seven exact-value anchors (`0` / `1` / `-1` / `42` / `int.MaxValue` / `int.MinValue` / `1234567890`) pinning the round order / shift constants / `2057` multiply against drift, an explicit `Hash(0) != 0` guard documenting the no-fixed-point property, determinism across calls and across stateless struct instances, a high-bit avalanche check, a 1000-consecutive-input collision-free sweep (exercising the bijective-on-contiguous-range property), a no-throw sweep over the key extremes, and integration tests driving `CelerityDictionary<int, …, Int32WangHasher>`, `IntDictionary<…, Int32WangHasher>`, `CeleritySet<int, Int32WangHasher>`, and `IntSet<Int32WangHasher>` — including the out-of-band zero-key / zero-element slot.
- `docs/api/hashing.md` and `README.md` — a full `Int32WangHasher` section (algorithm, where it sits on the cost-vs-avalanche curve relative to `Int32WangNaiveHasher` and `Int32Murmur3Hasher`, the no-`0 → 0` note) added next to the existing `Int32Murmur3Hasher` entry, the choosing-a-hasher table's `int` row updated to list `Int32WangHasher` as the full-finalizer escalation option before `Int32Murmur3Hasher`, and the README hasher-picking note updated to describe the two-step `int` escalation (`Int32WangHasher` → `Int32Murmur3Hasher`) mirroring the `long` family. The `Celerity.AotSmokeTest` hasher spread now also constructs a `CelerityDictionary<int, int, Int32WangHasher>` so the Native AOT publish job compiles the new generic instantiation.
- **Native AOT and trimming compatibility** — the `Celerity.csproj` library project now sets `<IsAotCompatible>true</IsAotCompatible>`. On `net8.0` this single switch marks the assembly trimmable and enables the trim, AOT, and single-file Roslyn analyzers, so every build statically verifies the library stays free of reflection / trim / AOT hazards. No source changes were required: the library already carried no reflection, no `Activator` / `Type.MakeGenericType` / `System.Linq.Expressions` / IL emit, and the only BCL primitives on its paths are `MemoryMarshal`, `Unsafe`, and `EqualityComparer<T>.Default` — all AOT-safe. Consumers can now reference `Celerity.Collections` from a `PublishAot` or trimmed app and get zero `IL2xxx` / `IL3xxx` warnings. Closes the trim/AOT-compatibility portion of #32 (an AOT-vs-JIT benchmark comparison remains a tracked follow-up).
- `Celerity.AotSmokeTest` — a console app (`<PublishAot>true</PublishAot>`) that constructs every collection shape (`IntDictionary`, `LongDictionary`, `CelerityDictionary`, `IntSet`, `LongSet`, `CeleritySet`) and a representative spread of hashers (`GuidHasher`, `StringMurmur3Hasher`, `StringFnV1AHasher`, `DefaultHasher<T>`, `UInt32Hasher`, `UInt64Hasher`, the Murmur3 / Wang integer hashers), runs the core CRUD + enumeration + `IEnumerable`-ctor operations against them, and asserts the results, exiting non-zero on any mismatch. It exists purely as a Native-AOT publish target so the AOT compiler is forced to compile every generic instantiation down to native code; it is excluded from packaging and from the test run.
- `aot-publish` CI job in `.github/workflows/ci.yml` — installs the Linux Native AOT prerequisites (`clang`, `zlib1g-dev`), runs `dotnet publish -r linux-x64 -c Release` on `Celerity.AotSmokeTest`, and executes the resulting native binary on every push and pull request. A failed publish or a non-zero exit code from the native binary fails CI, so AOT compatibility is proven end-to-end (not just at the analyzer level) on every change.
- `docs/aot.md` — a Native AOT & trimming page covering why the library is AOT-safe, how compatibility is enforced (analyzers + the CI publish smoke test), and how to publish an AOT app that uses Celerity. Linked from `docs/README.md`; a "Native AOT & trimming" section was added to `README.md`, and the `ROADMAP.md` 1.2.0 Native-AOT item is flipped to `done`.
- `Int64WangNaiveHasher` in `Celerity.Hashing` — lightweight XOR-fold hash provider for `long` keys, the 64-bit counterpart to `Int32WangNaiveHasher`. Struct hasher, `[MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]`. Two ops vs eleven for the full Thomas-Wang finalizer: `(int)key ^ (int)((ulong)key >> 32) ^ (int)((ulong)key >> 16)`. The extra middle-16-bits fold over a naive `(int)key.GetHashCode()` keeps a chunk of the high-half entropy in the result, which materially improves distribution on keys whose low 32 bits are sequential (e.g. monotonically allocated IDs whose upper bits carry type / shard). Now the default hasher for the `LongDictionary<TValue>` and `LongSet` convenience subclasses — see the `### Changed` entry above for the user-visible default-hasher switch and how to opt back into the previous default. Prefer it when the key distribution is already reasonably uniform and latency matters more than collision resistance; for adversarial or heavily clustered keys, escalate to `Int64WangHasher` (full Wang finalizer) or `Int64Murmur3Hasher`.
- `LongSet<THasher>` and the `LongSet` convenience subclass — high-performance set of `long` values, mirroring the `IntSet` surface for 64-bit elements. Defaults to `Int64WangNaiveHasher` (matching `LongDictionary`'s default after the default-hasher switch noted in the `### Changed` entry above). Implements `IEnumerable<long>`, ships an allocation-free struct enumerator with `_version`-based concurrent-modification detection, the `IEnumerable<long>` constructor with `ICollection<long>` count sizing and silent dedupe per BCL `HashSet<T>` semantics, full `Add` / `TryAdd` / `Contains` / `Remove` / `Clear` surface, and constructor validation matching `IntSet`. The zero element (`0L`) collides with the `EMPTY_SLOT` sentinel exactly as on `IntSet` and is stored out-of-band via a dedicated flag, so `set.Add(0L)` is round-trippable. Closes the last remaining dictionary-to-set parity gap (`IntDictionary` → `IntSet`, `CelerityDictionary` → `CeleritySet`, `LongDictionary` → `LongSet`).
- `StringMurmur3Hasher` in `Celerity.Hashing` — MurmurHash3 x86_32 over a string's UTF-16 code units. Struct hasher, `AggressiveInlining`. This is the `string` counterpart to `Int32Murmur3Hasher` / `Int64Murmur3Hasher`: it gives strings the same strong-escalation option that `int` and `long` already have over their fast-fold defaults, closing the gap where `string` shipped only `StringFnV1AHasher`. It improves on `StringFnV1AHasher` in two ways. First, it consumes the full 16-bit value of every character (reading consecutive char pairs as little-endian 32-bit blocks, exactly as a byte-oriented Murmur3 would over the native UTF-16 byte stream), so it distinguishes characters that share a low byte but differ in their upper byte — e.g. `'A'` (`U+0041`) and `'Ł'` (`U+0141`), which `StringFnV1AHasher` (low-byte only) collides on. Second, the `fmix32` finalizer gives every input bit influence over every output bit, holding distribution up on clustered or adversarial keys. The empty string `""` maps to `0` (the fixed point of `fmix32` over a zero accumulator), mirroring the `0 → 0` fixed point of the integer Murmur3 hashers; the dictionaries route the out-of-band `null`-key entry around the hasher so this never collides with the empty-slot sentinel. `Hash(null)` throws `ArgumentNullException` (parameter `"key"`), matching `StringFnV1AHasher`. Prefer it over `StringFnV1AHasher` for keys with significant non-ASCII content or when collision resistance matters more than the few cycles FNV-1a saves on short ASCII keys. Incremental progress on issue #24.
- `StringMurmur3HasherTests` — empty-string `→ 0` and five additional exact-value anchors (`"a"`, `"ab"`, `"abc"`, `"hello"`, `"hello world"`) that pin the algorithm against block-read-order / tail-handling / finalizer-constant drift; determinism across calls and across stateless struct instances; case sensitivity; single-character-change and append-character avalanche; the headline full-character-distinction regression (`StringFnV1AHasher` collides `"A"` / `"Ł"` and `"AB"` / `"Łł"`, `StringMurmur3Hasher` keeps them distinct); a 1000-distinct-string collision-free sweep; `Hash(null)` throwing `ArgumentNullException`; and integration tests driving `CelerityDictionary<string, …, StringMurmur3Hasher>` and `CeleritySet<string, StringMurmur3Hasher>`, including the empty-string regular key, a non-ASCII key, and the out-of-band `null` key.
- `docs/api/hashing.md` and `README.md` — a full `StringMurmur3Hasher` section (algorithm, when to prefer it over `StringFnV1AHasher`, empty-string `→ 0` note) added next to the existing `StringFnV1AHasher` entry, the choosing-a-hasher table's `string` row updated to list `StringMurmur3Hasher` as the escalation option, the `StringFnV1AHasher` low-byte note now points at it, and a `string` bullet added to the README hasher-picking notes.
- `LongSetTests` — mirrors the `IntSetTests` coverage (CRUD, zero element, resize survival, remove-then-reinsert, `Clear` reuse, constructor validation, `IEnumerable<long>` ctor null/dedupe, struct-enumerator smoke test, enumerator-invalidation on mutation, `LongSet<THasher>` open-generic smoke) plus long-specific cases: extreme element values (`long.MaxValue`, `long.MinValue`, `int.MaxValue + 1L`, `int.MinValue - 1L`, `-1L`) and a regression test that two elements sharing the same lower 32 bits but differing in the upper 32 bits are kept distinct (guards against any accidental int-truncation on the probe path).
- `LongSetCollisionTests` — mirrors `IntSetCollisionTests` for 64-bit elements via a `ConstantLongHasher` and covers insert, mid-chain `Remove` with cluster rehash, remove-then-reinsert, out-of-band zero (`0L`) coexistence with a colliding chain, multi-resize survival from a tiny capacity at load factor `0.5`, the resize-then-remove-sweep regression for the tightened Resize / RehashAfterRemove path, and a long-specific case that keys sharing lower 32 bits but differing in the upper 32 bits stay distinct under full collision.
- `LongSetEnumerationTests` — mirrors `IntSetEnumerationTests` for 64-bit elements: 24 tests covering empty / single / many-entry enumeration, zero-first-when-present ordering, removal / zero-removal / `Clear` survival, multi-resize survival from a tiny initial capacity, mutation-during-enumeration detection on insert / zero-insert / remove / zero-remove / clear, `Reset` invalidation under mutation, no-op mutations preserving enumerator validity, `Reset` reusability, post-exhaustion `Current` reset, generic and non-generic `IEnumerable` parity, a `LongSet<Int64Murmur3Hasher>` open-generic smoke test, a LINQ smoke test confirming the boxed enumerator path, and a long-specific extreme-key-values enumeration round-trip (including the lower-32-bits-share tripwire).
- `LongSet` coverage in the shared cross-collection test suites: a `LongSet` block in `SetConstructorValidationTests` (load-factor / capacity validation), `SetIEnumerableConstructorTests` (null-source priority, empty / array / list / non-collection enumerable sources, dedupe, zero capture, large source, source independence, caller-capacity dominance, round-trip, open-generic, extreme-key round-trip), `TryAddDuplicateResizeTests` (the issue-#92 duplicate-at-threshold and new-item-at-threshold enumerator-validity regressions), `TryAddProbeCountTests` (single-probe-walk pin for new-item and duplicate-item paths via `CountingLongHasher`), and `IEnumerableConstructorNullPriorityTests` (the issue-#94 null-source-before-invalid-load-factor priority for both the convenience subclass and the open generic). Total new test count across the extended files: 52.
- `LongSetBenchmark` — BenchmarkDotNet category-grouped benchmark for `LongSet` vs BCL `HashSet<long>` covering `Add` / `Contains` / `Remove` at `ItemCount = 1000` and `ItemCount = 100_000`, with the same iteration-setup-per-Remove pattern as `IntSetBenchmark` so the Remove benchmarks do not time no-ops on already-empty collections. Registered in `Program.cs` so the joined CI report and the gh-pages dashboard pick it up automatically. The `web/index.html` "What ships in the box" list, `web/dev/bench/index.html` per-collection panel layout, and `web/dev/bench/detail.html` collection lookup table are updated to include `LongSet` so the dashboard renders the new benchmark group on the next `main` build.
- `docs/api/collections.md` — full `LongSet` and `LongSet<THasher>` sections (constructors, methods, zero-element handling, usage example) mirroring the existing `IntSet` documentation. `README.md` Collections list, "Choosing a collection" decision table, hasher-picking note, and the sets enumeration list are updated to mention `LongSet` so the published API surface and the docs stay in sync.

### Fixed

- The `this[key] = value` indexer setter on `IntDictionary<TValue, THasher>`, `LongDictionary<TValue, THasher>`, and `CelerityDictionary<TKey, TValue, THasher>` no longer calls `Resize()` on the overwrite path. Previously the setter ran its `if (_count >= _threshold) Resize();` check *before* `ProbeForInsert`, so assigning to a key that already existed while the table sat exactly at the load-factor threshold triggered a full `Resize()` — doubling the backing arrays and re-hashing every entry — even though a pure value overwrite does not grow `Count` and therefore can never push the table over its threshold. This is the indexer-setter counterpart to the `TryAdd` ordering fixed in #92: that fix reordered the five `TryAdd` implementations to probe before the threshold check, but the parallel indexer-setter path on the three dictionaries was missed, leaving the same spurious-resize anti-pattern in place (wasted `O(n)` rehash plus premature capacity growth on overwrite-heavy workloads that hover at the threshold). The fix mirrors #92 exactly: `ProbeForInsert` runs first, and `Resize()` (followed by a re-probe in the doubled table) runs only when the probe reports a genuinely new entry *and* `_count >= _threshold`. An overwrite-at-threshold now issues exactly one probe walk and leaves the backing arrays untouched; a new-key-at-threshold insert still resizes and re-probes as before. No public-API or behavioural-contract change beyond "overwrite no longer resizes" (`_version` is still bumped on every indexer set, so enumerator invalidation is unchanged). Pinned by the new `IndexerOverwriteResizeTests`, which on each of the three dictionaries fills to exactly `capacity=4` (threshold = 3) and, via a counting `IHashProvider<T>`, asserts that an overwrite-at-threshold costs exactly one `Hash` call (pre-fix it cost `threshold + 1` because the resize re-hashed every entry), that repeated overwrites never resize, and that a new key at the threshold still resizes with every entry surviving. Closes #117.

## [1.2.1] - 2026-05-17

### Fixed

- `TryAdd` (and therefore `Add`) on `IntDictionary<TValue, THasher>`, `LongDictionary<TValue, THasher>`, `CelerityDictionary<TKey, TValue, THasher>`, `IntSet<THasher>`, and `CeleritySet<T, THasher>` no longer calls `Resize()` on the duplicate-key path. Previously, when the collection was exactly at the load-factor threshold and the caller supplied a duplicate key, `TryAdd` would hit the `if (_count >= _threshold) Resize();` check before the duplicate check, swap out the backing arrays, then walk the probe chain in the new table, detect the duplicate, and return `false` — all without bumping `_version`. An enumerator captured before that call would pass its `_version` check on the next `MoveNext` (because `_version` was unchanged) and silently read from the new arrays with an `_index` from the old coordinate system, yielding stale / duplicated / missing entries instead of throwing `InvalidOperationException`. This was a regression from the single-probe `TryAdd` rewrite in PR #53 — pre-#53 `TryAdd` was `if (ContainsKey(key)) return false; this[key] = value;` and `ContainsKey` does not mutate, so `Resize` only ran on the actual insert path (which bumps `_version`). The fix reorders all five `TryAdd` implementations so the duplicate-detection probe runs *before* the threshold check: a duplicate-at-threshold call now returns `false` without touching `_count`, `_version`, or the backing arrays, and a new-key-at-threshold call probes once in the current table to confirm the key is new, then `Resize()`s and re-probes in the doubled table to find an insert slot. Active enumerator invalidation now follows the visible-mutation rule again: `_version` bumps if and only if the collection actually changed. Pinned by `TryAddDuplicateResizeTests`, which on each of the five collections constructs the collection at exactly `capacity=4` (threshold = 3), fills it to threshold, captures an enumerator, and asserts that a duplicate `TryAdd` / `Add` leaves the enumerator valid (it can complete the enumeration) while a new-key `TryAdd` invalidates it. Closes #92.

### Changed

- `docs/api/collections.md` now covers the public API additions that shipped in `[1.2.0]` but were never propagated into the API reference: `ContainsValue(TValue? value)` on `CelerityDictionary`, `IntDictionary`, and `LongDictionary`, and the `IEnumerable<T>` constructor on `CeleritySet<T, THasher>`, `IntSet<THasher>`, and the `IntSet` convenience subclass. `ContainsValue` is added as a full subsection under `CelerityDictionary` (between `TryGetValue` and `Add`, mirroring source order) and as a bullet on the shared `IntDictionary` / `LongDictionary` method lists. The set `IEnumerable<T>` ctor is documented alongside the existing `(capacity, loadFactor)` ctor on all three set types, including an explicit note that — unlike the dictionary `IEnumerable<KeyValuePair<,>>` ctor — duplicate elements are silently deduplicated to match BCL `HashSet<T>` semantics. `IntSet<THasher>` previously had no Constructors subsection at all; one is now added. No code or behavior changes — `docs/api/collections.md` is the authoritative API-reference target linked from `README.md`, and this closes the drift gap so callers landing there to look up these methods see the actual shipped surface. Closes #89.
- `CelerityDictionary<TKey, TValue, THasher>`'s primary indexer get/set now uses `TValue` instead of `TValue?`, matching the signature `IntDictionary<TValue, THasher>` and `LongDictionary<TValue, THasher>` already shipped. The indexer never returns null as a "miss" sentinel — a missing key throws `KeyNotFoundException` — so the previous `TValue?` annotation was misleading and gave callers `string s = celerityDict[key];`-style CS8600 nullable warnings that the parallel `IntDictionary` / `LongDictionary` callers did not get. The interior reads from the backing `_values` and `_defaultKeyValue` slots are unchanged; they just acquire the same null-forgiving `!` that `IntDictionary` already uses on its `_values[index]!` read. The `IReadOnlyDictionary<TKey, TValue?>` interface contract is preserved through a new explicit interface forwarder (`TValue? IReadOnlyDictionary<TKey, TValue?>.this[TKey key] => this[key];`), mirroring how `IntDictionary` and `LongDictionary` already widen their non-nullable primary indexer to the nullable interface signature. The `docs/api/collections.md` indexer signature is updated to match. Source-compatible at the binary level (nullability is metadata-only) and at the source level for non-null call sites; the only behavioural change is that callers no longer have to suppress a CS8600 to assign the indexer result to a non-nullable local. Pinned by `IndexerReturnTypeTests`, which reflects on each dictionary's public indexer and asserts `PropertyType == TValue`, plus three compile-time tests that assign `dict[k]` directly to a non-nullable `string` local on all three dictionary shapes. Closes #88.
- `IntDictionary<TValue, THasher>.Resize()` / `RehashAfterRemove()`, `CelerityDictionary<TKey, TValue, THasher>.Resize()` / `RehashAfterRemove()`, `IntSet<THasher>.Resize()` / `RehashAfterRemove()`, and `CeleritySet<T, THasher>.Resize()` / `RehashAfterRemove()` now reinsert entries directly into the backing arrays instead of routing through the public indexer setter / `InsertNonZero` / `InsertNonDefault` helpers — applying the same tightened migration shape that `LongDictionary` got in PR #84 to the remaining four collections. The bypassed helpers perform an equality check inside the probe walk (looking for an existing entry to overwrite), test `_count >= _threshold`, branch on the empty-slot sentinel, and bump `_count` and `_version` per call — none of which is meaningful during a migration: every reinserted key is unique in the destination, the threshold can't trigger, the sentinel was already filtered, and `_count` / `_version` are conserved across the migration. `Resize` now builds into a fresh local pair of arrays and swaps them in at the end, which also keeps the collection in a consistent state if the migration ever throws. The now-unused `IntSet.InsertNonZero` and `CeleritySet.InsertNonDefault` private helpers are removed. Behaviour is unchanged — `Count`, `_version`-based enumerator invalidation, the zero / default out-of-band slots, and the contiguous-cluster invariant under linear probing are all preserved. Pinned by new `ResizeThenRemoveSweep_*_UnderFullCollision` Facts in `IntDictionaryCollisionTests`, `CelerityDictionaryCollisionTests`, `IntSetCollisionTests`, and `CeleritySetCollisionTests`, each running 40-entry insert past threshold + every-other remove + reinsert under maximum collision pressure. Closes #83.
- `LongDictionary<TValue, THasher>.Resize()` and `RehashAfterRemove()` now reinsert entries directly into the backing arrays instead of routing through the public indexer setter. The indexer setter is designed for user-facing inserts: it performs an equality check inside `ProbeForInsert` (looking for an existing entry to overwrite), tests `_count >= _threshold`, branches on the zero-key sentinel, and bumps `_count` and `_version` per call. None of that work is meaningful during a migration — the key being reinserted is guaranteed to be unique in the destination, the threshold can't trigger (we just doubled it during `Resize`, or just decremented `_count` during `RehashAfterRemove`), the zero-key entry is out-of-band and filtered before the call, and `_count` / `_version` are conserved across the migration so the user-visible operation that triggered it (e.g. `TryAdd` → `Resize`) bumps `_version` exactly once instead of `N + 1` times. `Resize` now builds into a fresh local pair of arrays and swaps them in at the end, which also keeps the dictionary in a consistent state if the migration ever throws. Behaviour is unchanged — `Count`, `_version`-based enumerator invalidation, the zero-key out-of-band slot, and the contiguous-cluster invariant under linear probing are all preserved. The same anti-pattern still lives in `IntDictionary`, `CelerityDictionary`, `IntSet`, and `CeleritySet`; a follow-up issue will track applying the same fix there. Pinned by the new `LongDictionaryCollisionTests.ResizeThenRemoveSweep_ShouldPreserveAllRemainingKeys_UnderFullCollision` Fact (40-key insert past threshold + every-other remove + reinsert under maximum collision pressure). Closes issue #82.
- `LongDictionary<TValue, THasher>.TryAdd` now walks the probe chain exactly **once** per call instead of twice, matching the single-probe rewrite that PR #53 applied to `IntDictionary`, `CelerityDictionary`, `IntSet`, and `CeleritySet`. `LongDictionary` was added in the same release as that rewrite but landed after it in commit order, so it was missed: `TryAdd` was still calling `ContainsKey` followed by the indexer setter, doing two `ProbeForInsert`-style walks per call. Behaviour is unchanged — `Add` still throws on duplicates, `TryAdd` still returns `false` and leaves the existing value untouched, the out-of-band zero-key path is unchanged — but bulk-loads via the `IEnumerable<KeyValuePair<long, TValue>>` constructor and any `if (!dict.TryAdd(...))` insert-or-skip pattern now do roughly half the probe work. Pinned by three new `LongDictionary`-shaped Facts in `TryAddProbeCountTests` (`_NewKey_DoesExactlyOneProbeWalk`, `_DuplicateKey_DoesExactlyOneProbeWalk`, `_PreservesExistingValueOnDuplicate`) using a counting `IHashProvider<long>` mirror of the existing `CountingIntHasher`. Closes issue #77.

### Fixed

- The `IEnumerable` constructor on `IntDictionary<TValue, THasher>`, `LongDictionary<TValue, THasher>`, `CelerityDictionary<TKey, TValue, THasher>`, `IntSet<THasher>`, and `CeleritySet<T, THasher>` (and the `IntDictionary<TValue>` / `LongDictionary<TValue>` / `IntSet` convenience subclasses) now surfaces a `null` source as `ArgumentNullException` even when the caller also passed an invalid `loadFactor` or `capacity`. Previously, the null check sat in the constructor body *after* the chained `: this(Math.Max(capacity, (source as ICollection<...>)?.Count ?? 0), loadFactor)` call: that chain forwarded the user-supplied `loadFactor` into the primary constructor's validation, which threw `ArgumentOutOfRangeException("loadFactor", ...)` first when the load factor was outside `(0, 1)`, masking the more important null-argument violation. The null check is now lifted into a private static `InitialCapacityForSource` helper invoked as part of the chained-ctor argument expression, so it runs before the primary ctor's range validation and matches the framework design guideline that `ArgumentNullException` for a parameter should be reported before other validation errors on sibling parameters. Behaviour is unchanged on the happy path and unchanged for any single-argument failure (a non-null source with bad `loadFactor` still throws `ArgumentOutOfRangeException`); only the null-source-plus-other-invalid-argument path is corrected. Pinned by the new `IEnumerableConstructorNullPriorityTests` (one Fact per collection, plus an `IntDictionary` boundary Fact for `loadFactor: 0f` and a generic-shape Fact for `IntDictionary<,>`, `LongDictionary<,>`, `IntSet<>`). Closes #94.
- `StringFnV1AHasher.Hash(null)` now throws `ArgumentNullException` (parameter name `"key"`) instead of `NullReferenceException`. Public APIs should signal a null argument as an explicit contract violation, not as an unchecked dereference. The Celerity dictionaries store the out-of-band `null` / `default(TKey)` key entry without ever calling the hasher, so the surface area of this change is limited to direct `StringFnV1AHasher` usage and to consumers that plug the hasher into custom `IHashProvider<string>` callers that do not handle the null-key slot themselves. The XML doc comment on `Hash` now declares the exception, and `StringFnV1AHasherTests.Hash_NullString_*` is updated to assert `ArgumentNullException` rather than pinning the previous wart. Closes #71.

## [1.2.0] - 2026-05-10

### Added

- `LongDictionaryCollisionTests` — closes the last forced-collision coverage gap on the dictionaries / sets. `IntDictionary`, `CelerityDictionary`, `IntSet`, and `CeleritySet` already shipped dedicated `*CollisionTests.cs` files driven by a constant-hash `IHashProvider`; `LongDictionary` did not, so its `ProbeForInsert` / `ProbeForKey` / `RehashAfterRemove` paths were never exercised under maximum probing pressure (every key forced into a single linear-probing chain). The new file mirrors `IntDictionaryCollisionTests` for 64-bit keys via a `ConstantLongHasher` and covers insert, overwrite, `ContainsKey`, `TryGetValue`, mid-chain `Remove` with cluster rehash, full-chain `Remove`, remove-then-reinsert, out-of-band zero-key (`0L`) coexistence with a colliding chain, multi-resize survival from a tiny capacity at load factor `0.5`, and a `long`-specific extreme-key case (`long.MaxValue`, `long.MinValue`, `int.MaxValue + 1L`, `int.MinValue - 1L`, `-1L`) that also pins the "lower-32-bits-equal but upper-32-bits-differ → distinct" invariant under full collision. Incremental progress on issue #29.
- `Remove(long key, out TValue? value)` BCL-parity overload on `LongDictionary<TValue, THasher>` (and the `LongDictionary<TValue>` convenience subclass), closing the parity gap with `IntDictionary` and `CelerityDictionary` shipped in `[1.1.2]`. The captured value is the value that was associated with the key immediately before removal, and is `default(TValue)` when the key was not found. The out-of-band zero-key (`0L`) slot is surfaced through the same path. The existing void `Remove(key)` overload now delegates to this method, so the rehash-after-remove path is unchanged and continues to bump the dictionary's `_version` counter so active enumerators throw `InvalidOperationException` on the next `MoveNext`. The README and `docs/api/collections.md` already documented this overload as part of the `LongDictionary` surface; this change makes the implementation match the docs. Closes issue #76.
- `RemoveOutValueTests` — extended with a parallel `LongDictionary` block mirroring the `IntDictionary` coverage: standard-key capture, missing-key on populated and empty maps, zero-key capture, zero-key absent, default-`TValue` capture (guards against conflating the captured value with the empty-slot sentinel), rehash-after-remove of an interior cluster element under forced full-collision, remove-then-reinsert, enumerator invalidation on the new overload, and a regression check that the void `Remove` overload still returns `true` after the delegation refactor.
- `ContainsValue(TValue? value)` on `IntDictionary<TValue, THasher>`, `LongDictionary<TValue, THasher>`, and `CelerityDictionary<TKey, TValue, THasher>` — BCL-parity `O(n)` linear scan that returns `true` if any entry's value equals `value` under `EqualityComparer<TValue>.Default`, matching `Dictionary<TKey, TValue>.ContainsValue(TValue)`. The scan walks the probe table (skipping `EMPTY_KEY` / `default(TKey)` slots so the empty `default(TValue)` payload there is not mistaken for a real entry) and, when present, the out-of-band zero-key / default-key slot. No allocation on the hot path beyond the cached `EqualityComparer<TValue>.Default` access. Closes #73.
- `ContainsValueTests` — coverage on all three dictionaries: empty-map false return, match in a regular slot, match found only in the zero-key / default-key / null-string-key slot, missing-value false return, default-`TValue` (`0`) lookup on both empty and populated dictionaries (regression check that `EMPTY_KEY` slots are skipped and not reported as `0` matches), `null`-`TValue` lookup on a reference-type value, duplicate values short-circuiting, post-resize correctness across a 100-entry insert from a tiny initial capacity, and post-`Remove` / post-`Clear` invalidation.
- `IEnumerable<T>` constructor on `IntSet`, `IntSet<THasher>`, and `CeleritySet<T, THasher>` (and the `IntSet` convenience subclass), mirroring the dictionary `IEnumerable<KeyValuePair<,>>` ctor shipped in 1.1.2. Throws `ArgumentNullException` on a null source. Unlike the dictionary ctor, duplicate elements (including duplicate `default(T)` / zero entries) are silently deduplicated to match BCL `HashSet<T>(IEnumerable<T>)` semantics — sets do not have a duplicate-key contract. When the source implements `ICollection<T>`, its `Count` is used to size the backing storage; otherwise the caller-supplied `capacity` parameter is used. The out-of-band `default(T)` / zero slot is populated correctly when the source contains it. Closes the last set-side API-parity gap for milestone 1.1.0 and unblocks future `IReadOnlySet<T>` work. Closes #69.
- `SetIEnumerableConstructorTests` — coverage for both sets: null-source and invalid-load-factor validation, empty sources, array / list / non-collection enumerable sources, duplicate-element silent dedupe (including duplicate zero / `null` / `default(T)` entries), zero-element / null-reference-element capture, 500-entry large-source round-trip, source-independence after construction, caller-specified capacity dominating the source count, cross-set copy (`CeleritySet` from an `IntSet` enumeration), and an open-generic `IntSet<Int32WangNaiveHasher>` smoke test.
- `README.md` — new "Choosing a collection" section: a decision table mapping common workloads (`int`-keyed, `long`-keyed, `Guid` / `string` / other-keyed dictionaries, the two set shapes) onto the right Celerity type, plus a short note on picking a hasher and an honest "where Celerity is not the right answer today" list (concurrent access, mutable `IDictionary<,>` consumers, `FrozenDictionary`-style build-once lookups). Sits between the Quick start and Benchmarks sections so a reader who has scanned the API surface can pick the right type without spelunking `docs/api/`. Implements the "Document when to use which collection" item from issue #15.
- `README.md` — new "Quick start" section with concrete, runnable usage examples for `IntDictionary`, `CelerityDictionary` (with `GuidHasher`, `StringFnV1AHasher`, `DefaultHasher<T>`), the sets (`IntSet`, `CeleritySet`), and the `IEnumerable<KeyValuePair<,>>` constructor. Covers indexer get/set, `TryAdd` / `Add` semantics, `TryGetValue`, removal, and bulk-load from a BCL `Dictionary<,>`. Closes the "Add usage examples to README" item from issue #15.

## [1.1.2] - 2026-05-01

First successful 1.1.x publish. Tags `v1.1.0` and `v1.1.1` exist on the repository but never published to nuget.org: `v1.1.0` failed at deploy with HTTP 403 (NuGet API key had expired), and the follow-up `v1.1.1` failed with HTTP 401 because the trusted-publishing migration used the wrong NuGet account name (`marius-bughiu` instead of `marius.bughiu`). 1.1.2 is the same library code as the 1.1.0 tag plus the trusted-publishing migration with the correct user, shipped under a fresh version because the failed tags couldn't be cleanly recycled.

### Changed

- **CS1591 (missing XML doc comment) is now a build error in `Celerity.csproj`**, not just a warning. Celerity ships its generated `.xml` documentation file with the NuGet package; gating on CS1591 ensures every public type / member retains a doc comment so that file is never silently incomplete. The library was already at 100% public-symbol doc coverage at the time of the change, so no source had to be updated — this is purely a guardrail to prevent regression. Implements the "Bump XML doc coverage; treat missing docs as warning-as-error" item from the milestone 1.1.0 infrastructure roadmap. Scoped to the main library `.csproj` only; the test and benchmark projects are unaffected because they do not set `<GenerateDocumentationFile>true</GenerateDocumentationFile>`.

### Added

- Cross-platform CI matrix — `.github/workflows/ci.yml` now runs `dotnet build` and `dotnet test` on `ubuntu-latest`, `windows-latest`, and `macos-latest` for every push to `main` and every pull request, with `fail-fast: false` so a regression on one OS does not mask the result on the others. Test-result artifacts are uploaded per-OS (`test-results-<os>`) to avoid name collisions. Closes the cross-platform testing item on milestone 1.1.0 (#28).
- `Remove(TKey key, out TValue? value)` BCL-parity overload on both `CelerityDictionary<TKey, TValue, THasher>` and `IntDictionary<TValue, THasher>`. The captured value is the value that was associated with the key immediately before removal, and is `default(TValue)` when the key was not found. The out-of-band default-key / zero-key slot is surfaced through the same path. The existing void `Remove(key)` overload now delegates to this method, so the rehash-after-remove path is unchanged and continues to bump the dictionary's `_version` counter so active enumerators throw `InvalidOperationException` on the next `MoveNext`. Closes issue #23.
- `RemoveOutValueTests` — coverage for both dictionaries: standard-key capture, missing-key returning `false` and `default`, out-of-band default-key / zero-key / null-string-key capture, rehash-after-remove of an interior cluster element under forced full-collision, remove-then-reinsert, default-value-type capture (guards against conflating the captured value with the empty-slot sentinel), enumerator invalidation on the new overload, and a regression check that the void `Remove` overload still returns `true` after the delegation refactor.
- `LongDictionary<TValue, THasher>` and the `LongDictionary<TValue>` convenience subclass — high-performance dictionary keyed by `long`, mirroring the `IntDictionary` surface for 64-bit keys. Defaults to `Int64WangHasher`. Implements `IReadOnlyDictionary<long, TValue?>`, ships allocation-free struct enumerator and `KeyCollection` / `ValueCollection` views, the `IEnumerable<KeyValuePair<long, TValue>>` constructor, full `Add` / `TryAdd` / `TryGetValue` / `Clear` surface, and constructor validation matching `IntDictionary`. The zero key (`0L`) collides with the `EMPTY_KEY` sentinel exactly as on `IntDictionary` and is stored out-of-band via a dedicated flag + value slot, so `map[0L] = x` is round-trippable. Closes the last collection-shape gap in milestone 1.1.0.
- `LongDictionaryTests` — mirrors the `IntDictionaryTests` coverage (CRUD, zero-key, resize survival, remove-then-reinsert, constructor validation, `IEnumerable` constructor, `Add` / `TryAdd` duplicate semantics, struct-enumerator and `Keys` / `Values` views, and the boxed `IReadOnlyDictionary<long, TValue?>` surface) plus long-specific cases: extreme key values (`long.MaxValue`, `long.MinValue`, `int.MaxValue + 1L`, `int.MinValue - 1L`, `-1L`) and a regression test that two keys sharing the same lower 32 bits but differing in the upper 32 bits are kept distinct (guards against any accidental int-truncation on the probe path).
- `CeleritySet.GetEnumerator()` and `IEnumerable<T>` conformance — struct-based, allocation-free enumeration over a `CeleritySet<T, THasher>`. The out-of-band `default(T)` entry (zero for primitives, `Guid.Empty` for `Guid`, `null` for reference-type elements) is yielded first; the rest of the elements follow in unspecified order. The struct enumerator tracks a `_version` counter (bumped on every entry-point structural mutation: `Add`, `TryAdd`, `Remove`, `Clear`) and throws `InvalidOperationException` on `MoveNext` / `Reset` if the set is mutated mid-enumeration, matching BCL `HashSet<T>` semantics. Closes the second slice of issue #23 (`IntSet` shipped in PR #50); the sets are now at full enumeration parity with the dictionaries. Unblocks the post-1.1.0 `IReadOnlySet<T>` interface and an `IEnumerable<T>` constructor mirroring dictionary issue #22.
- `CeleritySetEnumerationTests` — 26 tests mirroring `IntSetEnumerationTests`, covering empty / single / many-entry enumeration, default-value-first ordering for both value-type and reference-type (`null`) elements, removal / default-removal / `Clear` survival, multi-resize survival from a tiny initial capacity, mutation-during-enumeration detection on insert / default-insert / remove / default-remove / clear, `Reset` invalidation under mutation, no-op mutations (re-adding an existing item, re-adding a present default item, removing an absent item, `Clear` on an empty set) preserving enumerator validity, `Reset` reusability, post-exhaustion `Current` reset, generic and non-generic `IEnumerable` parity, `CeleritySet<int, Int32Murmur3Hasher>` open-generic coverage, and a LINQ smoke test (`Count` / `Sum` / `Contains`) confirming the boxed enumerator path.
- `IntSet.GetEnumerator()` and `IEnumerable<int>` conformance — struct-based, allocation-free enumeration over an `IntSet<THasher>`. The out-of-band zero entry is yielded first; the rest of the elements follow in unspecified order. The struct enumerator tracks a `_version` counter (bumped on every entry-point structural mutation: `Add`, `TryAdd`, `Remove`, `Clear`) and throws `InvalidOperationException` on `MoveNext` / `Reset` if the set is mutated mid-enumeration, matching BCL `HashSet<T>` semantics. The dictionaries already shipped this surface (issue #10); this closes the symmetric gap on the sets and is the first slice of issue #23 (`CeleritySet` follows in a separate PR). Unblocks the `IEnumerable<int>` constructor and the post-1.1.0 `IReadOnlySet<int>` interface.
- `IntSetEnumerationTests` — 25 tests covering empty / single / many-entry enumeration, zero-first-when-present ordering, removal / zero-removal / `Clear` survival, multi-resize survival from a tiny initial capacity, mutation-during-enumeration detection on insert / zero-insert / remove / zero-remove / clear, `Reset` invalidation under mutation, no-op mutations (re-adding an existing item, removing an absent item, `Clear` on an empty set) preserving enumerator validity, `Reset` reusability, post-exhaustion `Current` reset, generic and non-generic `IEnumerable` parity, `IntSet<Int32Murmur3Hasher>` open-generic coverage, and a LINQ smoke test (`Count` / `Sum` / `Contains`) confirming the boxed enumerator path.
- `IEnumerable<KeyValuePair<TKey, TValue>>` constructor on both `CelerityDictionary<TKey, TValue, THasher>` and `IntDictionary<TValue, THasher>` (and the `IntDictionary<TValue>` convenience subclass). Matches BCL `Dictionary<,>` semantics: throws `ArgumentNullException` on a null source and `ArgumentException` on duplicate keys (including duplicate zero / default keys). When the source implements `ICollection<T>`, its `Count` is used to size the backing storage so the initial fill avoids at least some resize work; non-collection enumerables fall back to the caller-supplied `capacity` parameter. The out-of-band zero-key / default-key slot is populated correctly when the source contains an entry with `default(TKey)`. Completes the last of the milestone 1.1.0 API-parity items on the dictionaries.
- `IEnumerableConstructorTests` — 28 tests covering null-source and invalid-load-factor validation, empty sources, array / list / non-collection enumerable sources, duplicate-key detection (including duplicate zero / default keys), zero-key and null-reference-key capture, 500-entry large-source round-trip, source-independence after construction, caller-specified capacity dominating the source count, cross-dictionary copy via `Select`, and projection through `IReadOnlyDictionary<,>` to verify the new ctor flows into the existing interface surface.
- `IReadOnlyDictionary<TKey, TValue?>` implementation on both `CelerityDictionary<TKey, TValue, THasher>` and `IntDictionary<TValue, THasher>` — the dictionaries can now be passed to any API that accepts `IReadOnlyDictionary<,>` (LINQ, DI, BCL `ToDictionary`, etc.) without a wrapper. The implementation is a thin set of explicit interface forwarders on top of the existing struct `KeyCollection` / `ValueCollection` views and struct `Enumerator`, so the zero-allocation `foreach (var kvp in map)` / `foreach (var k in map.Keys)` fast paths remain unchanged and the interface path boxes the enumerator exactly once per call, matching BCL `Dictionary<,>` behaviour. The out-of-band default-key / zero-key entry is surfaced through every interface member (`ContainsKey`, `TryGetValue`, indexer, `Keys`, `Values`, generic `IEnumerable<KeyValuePair<TKey, TValue?>>`, and non-generic `IEnumerable`), and mid-enumeration mutation still throws `InvalidOperationException`. Closes issue #9; completes the last of the 1.1.0 API-parity collection work.
- `ReadOnlyDictionaryInterfaceTests` — boxed-path coverage for both dictionaries through the `IReadOnlyDictionary<TKey, TValue?>` surface: indexer, `ContainsKey`, `TryGetValue`, `Keys` / `Values` widened to `IEnumerable<T>`, generic `IEnumerable<KeyValuePair<,>>` and non-generic `IEnumerable` enumeration, default-key / zero-key / null-reference-key inclusion, mutation-during-enumeration detection on the boxed enumerator, `Enumerable.Count()` LINQ dispatch, and a polymorphic consumer function proving both dictionary shapes flow through the same `IReadOnlyDictionary<int, int>` parameter.
- `CelerityDictionary.GetEnumerator()`, `CelerityDictionary.Keys`, and `CelerityDictionary.Values` — struct-based, allocation-free enumeration over a `CelerityDictionary<TKey, TValue, THasher>`, mirroring the `IntDictionary` surface added earlier in 1.1.0. `Keys` and `Values` expose `KeyCollection` / `ValueCollection` readonly structs, each with their own struct enumerator, so `foreach (var kvp in map)` / `foreach (var k in map.Keys)` / `foreach (var v in map.Values)` do not box. The out-of-band default-key entry is yielded first — including `null` for reference-type keys. The enumerators track a `_version` counter and throw `InvalidOperationException` on `MoveNext` / `Reset` if the dictionary is mutated mid-enumeration, matching BCL `Dictionary<,>` semantics. Completes issue #10 and unblocks `IReadOnlyDictionary<TKey, TValue>` (#9).
- `CelerityDictionaryEnumerationTests` — mirror of `IntDictionaryEnumerationTests` covering empty / single / many-entry enumeration, default-key-first ordering for both value-type and reference-type (`null`) keys, `Remove` / `Clear` / resize survival, mutation-during-enumeration detection on insert / overwrite / default-key-insert / remove / clear, `Reset` reuse, `Keys.Count` / `Values.Count` tracking, and `IEnumerable<T>` interface parity.
- `IntDictionary.GetEnumerator()`, `IntDictionary.Keys`, and `IntDictionary.Values` — struct-based, allocation-free enumeration over an `IntDictionary<TValue, THasher>`. `Keys` and `Values` expose `KeyCollection` / `ValueCollection` readonly structs, each with their own struct enumerator, so `foreach (var kvp in map)` / `foreach (int k in map.Keys)` / `foreach (var v in map.Values)` do not box. The out-of-band zero-key entry is yielded first. The enumerators track a `_version` counter and throw `InvalidOperationException` on `MoveNext` / `Reset` if the dictionary is mutated mid-enumeration, matching BCL `Dictionary<,>` semantics. First step toward implementing `IReadOnlyDictionary<int, TValue>` (#10).
- `Int32Murmur3Hasher` in `Celerity.Hashing` — Murmur3 32-bit finalizer ("fmix32") for `int` keys. Struct hasher, `AggressiveInlining`. Provides excellent avalanche properties; prefer over `Int32WangNaiveHasher` when key distribution is clustered or adversarial. Maps `0 → 0` (fixed point of fmix32).
- `Int64WangHasher` in `Celerity.Hashing` — Thomas Wang 64-bit integer hash for `long` keys. Struct hasher, `AggressiveInlining`. Faster than `Int64Murmur3Hasher` while providing better avalanche than a simple XOR-fold; prefer when throughput matters more than adversarial collision resistance. Invertible (bijective on `ulong`) so truncation to 32 bits is the only source of collisions.
- `Int32Murmur3HasherTests` — exact anchor values for key extremes, determinism, high-bit avalanche check, 1000-value distinctness sweep, and integration tests driving `CelerityDictionary` and `CeleritySet` including the `default(int)` out-of-band slot.
- `Int64WangHasherTests` — exact anchor values for key extremes, determinism, high-bit avalanche check, 1000-value distinctness sweep, and integration tests driving `CelerityDictionary` and `CeleritySet` including the `default(long)` out-of-band slot.
- `GuidHasher` in `Celerity.Hashing` — reinterprets the 128-bit `Guid` as two 64-bit halves, runs Murmur3 `fmix64` on each, and XORs the mixed halves. Struct hasher, `AggressiveInlining`, zero-allocation (no stack buffer — reinterpret via `Unsafe.As<Guid, ulong>`). Prefer over `DefaultHasher<Guid>` on hot paths: fully inlineable and avoids the `EqualityComparer<T>.Default` virtual dispatch.
- `GuidHasherTests` — `Guid.Empty → 0` anchor, determinism across calls and struct instances, avalanche on both the low and high 64-bit halves, shared-prefix/shared-suffix divergence (guards against hashers that weight one half too heavily), two 1000-value distinctness sweeps (sequential low-half keys and `Guid.NewGuid()`), and integration tests confirming `GuidHasher` satisfies the hasher constraint on `CeleritySet<Guid,THasher>` and `CelerityDictionary<Guid,TValue,THasher>` (including the `Guid.Empty` out-of-band slot).
- `UInt32Hasher` in `Celerity.Hashing` — Wang/Jenkins-style bit-mixer for `uint` keys. Struct hasher, `AggressiveInlining`. Counterpart to `Int32WangNaiveHasher`.
- `UInt64Hasher` in `Celerity.Hashing` — Murmur3 `fmix64` finalizer for `ulong` keys. Struct hasher, `AggressiveInlining`. Counterpart to `Int64Murmur3Hasher`.
- `UInt32HasherTests` and `UInt64HasherTests` — exact-value cases (including values crossing the sign bit), determinism, avalanche on the top bit, and a 1000-value distinctness sweep for the 64-bit mixer.
- `DefaultHasher<T>` in `Celerity.Hashing` — a general-purpose `IHashProvider<T>` that delegates to `EqualityComparer<T>.Default.GetHashCode()`. Use it when no specialized hasher exists for a type (e.g. `Guid`, custom structs, or reference types). It is a struct, so the JIT devirtualizes the outer call on the probe path; the inner `EqualityComparer<T>` dispatch is unavoidable but acceptable for non-hot-path types.
- XML doc comments added to `IHashProvider<T>`, `Int32WangNaiveHasher`, `Int64Murmur3Hasher`, and `StringFnV1AHasher`. All public hasher types now carry full XML documentation.
- `DefaultHasherTests` — verifies BCL contract equivalence for int, string, and Guid keys; determinism across calls and struct instances; and integration tests confirming `DefaultHasher<T>` satisfies the hasher constraints on `CeleritySet<T,THasher>`, `IntSet<THasher>`, and `CelerityDictionary<TKey,TValue,THasher>`.
- `Add(TKey, TValue)` on `CelerityDictionary` and `IntDictionary` — inserts a key/value pair and throws `ArgumentException` if the key already exists, matching BCL `Dictionary<,>` semantics.
- `TryAdd(TKey, TValue)` on `CelerityDictionary` and `IntDictionary` — inserts without overwriting; returns `true` on success, `false` if the key already exists.  Both methods correctly handle the zero/default-key out-of-band slot.
- `TryGetValue(TKey, out TValue?)` on `CelerityDictionary` and `IntDictionary`, following BCL semantics.
- `Clear()` on `CelerityDictionary` and `IntDictionary` — resets the map without releasing the backing arrays, so pooled/reused instances don't pay an allocation on every generation.
- `.github/workflows/ci.yml` — `dotnet build` and `dotnet test` now run automatically on every push to `main` and every pull request.
- `ROADMAP.md` — prioritized plan through 1.0.
- `ISSUES.md` — snapshot of the known issue backlog.
- `CONTRIBUTING.md` — build, test, and PR conventions.
- `CHANGELOG.md` — this file.
- Forced-collision test suites for both `IntDictionary` and `CelerityDictionary` using a constant-hash `IHashProvider`, exercising insert, overwrite, remove, remove-then-reinsert, and resize under maximum probing pressure.
- String-key tests for `CelerityDictionary` covering the `null` default-key path (`null` insert, remove, `TryGetValue`, `Clear`).
- Remove-then-reinsert stress test for `CelerityDictionary` with the standard hasher (parity with the existing `IntDictionary` test).
- Load-factor boundary test suite (`LoadFactorBoundaryTests.cs`) covering low load factor (0.5), high load factor (0.95), multiple sequential resizes from a tiny initial capacity, default/zero-key coexistence with the resize threshold, and a parameterized Theory across `{0.25, 0.5, 0.75, 0.95}` for both `IntDictionary` and `CelerityDictionary`. Closes the remaining gap from issue #7.

### Fixed

- **`IntDictionary<TValue>` constructor arguments were silently discarded.** The convenience subclass `IntDictionary<TValue>` accepted `capacity` and `loadFactor` parameters but forwarded to `: base()` with no arguments, so every instance was created with the defaults regardless of what the caller passed. It now forwards `capacity` and `loadFactor` to the base constructor.
- **`IntDictionary` could not store the key `0`.** `EMPTY_KEY = 0` was used as the "empty slot" sentinel, which collided with the legitimate key value `0`. `map[0] = x` appeared to succeed but subsequent `ContainsKey(0)`, `map[0]`, and `Count` returned wrong answers. The zero key is now stored out-of-band via a dedicated flag + value slot, a pattern borrowed from `fastutil` / `HPPC`.
- **`CelerityDictionary` could not store `default(TKey)`.** Same root cause as above, generalized: `default(int)` / `default(long)` / `default(Guid)` / `null` strings were all lost. Fixed the same way, via a `_hasDefaultKey` flag and a dedicated value slot.

- Constructor validation test suite (`ConstructorValidationTests.cs`) covering rejection of invalid `loadFactor` (≤0, ≥1) and negative `capacity` for both `IntDictionary` and `CelerityDictionary`, plus acceptance of valid edge values.

### Fixed (additional)

- **`CelerityDictionary` and `IntDictionary` accepted invalid constructor arguments.** `loadFactor >= 1.0` caused an infinite loop in `ProbeForInsert` once the table was full; `loadFactor <= 0` caused a resize on every insert. Both constructors now throw `ArgumentOutOfRangeException` for `capacity < 0`, `loadFactor <= 0`, or `loadFactor >= 1`.

### Changed

- `TryAdd` (and therefore `Add`) on `IntDictionary<TValue, THasher>`, `CelerityDictionary<TKey, TValue, THasher>`, `IntSet<THasher>`, and `CeleritySet<T, THasher>` now walks the probe chain exactly **once** per call instead of twice. The previous implementation called `ContainsKey` / `Contains` followed by the indexer setter / `InsertNon*` helper, each starting its own probe walk; the rewrite uses a single `ProbeForInsert`-style walk that either lands on the existing entry (return `false`) or on the first empty slot (insert in place). Behaviour is identical to before — including the duplicate-key contract on `Add` and the "unchanged on duplicate" contract on `TryAdd` — but bulk-loads via the new `IEnumerable<KeyValuePair<,>>` constructor and any `Add`-heavy hot path now do roughly half the probe work. Closes issue #24. Pinned by `TryAddProbeCountTests`, which uses a counting `IHashProvider` to assert that `TryAdd` calls `Hash` exactly once on both the new-key and duplicate-key paths across all four collections.
- The `IntDictionary` `EMPTY_VALUE` field is now `static readonly` instead of an instance field. No behavior change; just removes per-instance overhead.

## [0.1.0] - initial releases

Initial public versions, including `CelerityDictionary<TKey, TValue, THasher>`, `IntDictionary<TValue>`, the `Int32WangNaiveHasher`, `Int64Murmur3Hasher`, and `StringFnV1AHasher` hash providers, and the BenchmarkDotNet benchmark suite comparing `CelerityDictionary` against the BCL `Dictionary<int, int>`. See the git history under tags `v0.1.*` for specifics.
